primary line~$L$, the weighted shadow generating function
$H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q_L(t)}$ for a quadratic polynomial~$Q_L$
determined by three seed invariants $(\kappa, \alpha, S_4)$.
The inverse limit
$\Theta_\cA = \varprojlim_r \Theta_\cA^{\leq r}$
is proved to exist and to be automatically Maurer--Cartan
because $D_\cA^2 = 0$.

In three dimensions, $\Theta_\cA$ extends to an open/closed
Maurer--Cartan element
$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA = \Theta_\cA + \sum_j \mu^{M_j}$
that packages the complete holomorphic-topological quantum field
theory on $\mathbb C_z \times \mathbb R_t$: the bar complex encodes
the closed (holomorphic) colour, the coproduct encodes the open
(topological) colour, and the chiral derived center
$\cZ^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)$ is the universal bulk
(Volume~II).

\medskip
\noindent
\textbf{Corollary} (MC replaces the sum over topologies).
On the Koszul locus, the tree-level complex carries a contracting
homotopy (from the PBW degeneration), so the genus-$g$ component
$\Theta^{(g)}$ is determined (up to the contractible ambiguity
in the choice of strong deformation retract) by induction from
$\Theta^{(0)}$.  No free parameters appear at any genus; the
contracting homotopy is unique up to homotopy, and distinct
choices yield gauge-equivalent MC elements.  No choice of bulk
topologies is required.  The genus expansion is computed algebraically
from the genus-$0$ chiral bracket by the clutching recursion of
Section~4.6, not approximated perturbatively.  The
Maloney--Witten problem (negative Fourier coefficients in the
Poincar\'e series) does not arise: the MC equation determines each $F_g$ uniquely
by algebraic induction, without summing over bulk topologies at fixed genus.
The non-perturbative sum over distinct three-manifold topologies is
outside the scope of the MC framework.

% ====================================================================
\section*{5.\quad The modular tangent complex and Chern--Weil theory}
% ====================================================================

The MC element $\Theta_\cA$ exists
unconditionally and satisfies
$D\Theta_\cA + \tfrac{1}{2}[\Theta_\cA,\Theta_\cA] = 0$.  Its
deformation theory is controlled by the modular tangent complex,
obtained by twisting the convolution algebra by $\Theta_\cA$ itself.

\subsection*{5.1.\enspace The $L_\infty$-twisted differential}

The MC element $\Theta_\cA$ twists the convolution differential.  For $x\in\gAmod$:
\[
d_{\Theta_\cA}(x)
\;:=\;
\sum_{n\ge 0}\sum_{g\ge 0}
\frac{\hbar^g}{n!}\,
\ell_{n+1}^{(g)}(\Theta_\cA^{\otimes n},x).
\]
Expanding:
\[
d_{\Theta_\cA}(x)
\;=\;
d(x)
\;+\;
[\Theta_\cA,x]
\;+\;
\tfrac{1}{2!}\ell_3^{(0)}(\Theta_\cA,\Theta_\cA,x)
\;+\;
\hbar\,\ell_1^{(1)}(x)
\;+\;
\hbar\,\ell_2^{(1)}(\Theta_\cA,x)
\;+\;\cdots
\]
In the strict chart (the dg Lie model $\Convstr$), this collapses to:
\[
d_{\Theta_\cA}(x)\;=\;d(x)+[\Theta_\cA,x].
\]
The identity $d_{\Theta_\cA}^2=0$ is equivalent to the MC equation
for~$\Theta_\cA$.

\subsection*{5.2.\enspace The modular tangent complex}

The \emph{modular tangent complex at~$\Theta_\cA$} is the twisted
cochain complex:
\[
T^{\mathrm{mod}}_{\Theta_\cA}
\;:=\;
(\gAmod,\;d_{\Theta_\cA}).
\]
Its cohomology governs deformations of~$\Theta_\cA$:
\begin{align*}
H^0(T^{\mathrm{mod}}_{\Theta_\cA})
&=\text{infinitesimal automorphisms of~$\Theta_\cA$}
  &&\text{(stabiliser)},\\[3pt]
H^1(T^{\mathrm{mod}}_{\Theta_\cA})
&=\text{first-order deformations of~$\Theta_\cA$}
  &&\text{(tangent space)},\\[3pt]
H^2(T^{\mathrm{mod}}_{\Theta_\cA})
&=\text{obstructions to extending deformations}
  &&\text{(obstruction space)}.
\end{align*}
When $H^2=0$, the MC moduli is smooth at~$\Theta_\cA$.
When $H^1=0$, the MC element is rigid: every nearby element is
gauge-equivalent.

For a one-parameter family $\cA_t$ varying continuously in
level~$k(t)$ or central charge~$c(t)$, the tangent complex
$T^{\mathrm{mod}}_{\Theta_{\cA_t}}$ forms a local system over the
parameter space, and the obstruction class traces a path
in~$H^2$.  The vanishing locus of this obstruction path is the
moduli of liftable deformations.

\subsection*{5.3.\enspace Three characteristic projections}

Three successive
projections of $\Theta_\cA$ capture progressively finer structure:
$\kappa(\cA)$ is a \emph{number} (the leading scalar curvature,
analogous to the first Chern class);
$\Delta_\cA(x)$ is a \emph{polynomial} (encoding a finite
spectrum of branch points, analogous to the Chern character);
$\mathfrak{R}^{\mathrm{mod}}_4(\cA)$ is a \emph{cohomology
class} (the first invariant that sees nonlinear OPE interaction
beyond the spectral data).  Together, they
seed the algebraicity theorem.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{The scalar curvature $\kappa(\cA)$:}\enspace
the arity-two, genus-zero trace:
\[
\kappa(\cA)
\;=\;
\operatorname{tr}(\Theta_\cA)_{2,0}
\;=\;
\operatorname{tr}(\pi\circ m_2\circ\iota^{\otimes 2}
\circ\Delta_{\mathrm{sep}})
\;\in\;\Bbbk.
\]
This is the first Chern class of the modular bar bundle:
$\operatorname{obs}_g(\cA)=
\kappa(\cA)\cdot\lambda_g$, where $\lambda_g$ is the Hodge
class on~$\overline{\cM}_g$.  The Mumford relation
$\lambda_g^{g+1}=0$ confines genus-$g$ scalar obstructions to a space of dimension at most~$g$.

Explicit values across the standard landscape:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{lccl}
\textbf{Algebra $\cA$}
  & $\kappa(\cA)$
  & $\kappa(\cA^!)$
  & \textbf{Sum rule}\\
\hline
Heisenberg $\cH_k$ & $k$ & $-k$ & $0$\\[2pt]
Affine $\widehat{\fg}_k$
  & $\dfrac{(k+h^\vee)\dim\fg}{2h^\vee}$
  & $-\dfrac{(k+h^\vee)\dim\fg}{2h^\vee}$ & $0$\\[6pt]
Virasoro $\mathrm{Vir}_c$ & $c/2$ & $(26-c)/2$ & $13$\\[2pt]
$\beta\gamma$ system & $1$ & $-1$ & $0$\\[2pt]
Lattice $V_\Lambda$ & $\operatorname{rank}(\Lambda)$
  & $-\operatorname{rank}(\Lambda)$ & $0$\\[2pt]
$\mathcal W_N(\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_N)$
  & $c\cdot(H_N{-}1)$
  & $c'\cdot(H_N{-}1)$
  & $K_N\cdot(H_N{-}1)$\\[6pt]
Free fermion $\psi$ & $1/4$ & $-1/4$ & $0$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The complementarity sum rule $\kappa(\cA)+\kappa(\cA^!)=0$ holds for
Kac--Moody algebras, free fields, and lattice vertex algebras.
For $\mathcal W$-algebras the sum is a nonzero constant
determined by the anomaly ratio: $\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c)+
\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c})=13$, and
$\kappa(\mathcal W_{N,c})+\kappa(\mathcal W_{N,c'})
=K_N\cdot(H_N{-}1)$ where $K_N=c+c'$ is the family constant.
Self-duality occurs at $c=13$ for Virasoro and
$c=50$ for~$\mathcal W_3$.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{The spectral discriminant $\Delta_\cA(x)$
and the branch transport operator.}

The second characteristic invariant is the
characteristic polynomial of a finite-rank operator.  The Koszul dual Hilbert series
\[
h_{\cA^!}(q)
\;=\;
\sum_{n\ge 0}\dim H^n(\barB(\cA))\,q^n,
\]
records bar cohomology dimensions.  For every standard family, $h_{\cA^!}(q)$ is a
\emph{rational} function: it satisfies a holonomic recurrence relation
of finite order~$d$, and the transfer matrix of this recurrence is
a $d\times d$ matrix $T_{\mathrm{rec}}$.

Define the \emph{spectral branch object} to be a finite-rank perfect
complex $V^{\mathrm{br}}_\cA$ together with a \emph{branch transport
operator} $T_{\mathrm{br},\cA}\colon
V^{\mathrm{br}}_\cA\to V^{\mathrm{br}}_\cA$ such that
\begin{equation}\label{eq:pref-delta-def}
\Delta_\cA(x)
\;:=\;
\operatorname{sdet}\!\bigl(1-x\,T_{\mathrm{br},\cA}\bigr).
\end{equation}
The rank of $V^{\mathrm{br}}_\cA$ equals the degree of algebraicity
of~$h_{\cA^!}(q)$: the order of the minimal recurrence.  The
eigenvalues of $T_{\mathrm{br},\cA}$ are the reciprocal branch
points of the analytic continuation of~$h_{\cA^!}$.

Three structural properties:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
\item $\Delta_{\cA^!}(x)=\Delta_\cA(x)$: the spectral
  discriminant is \emph{self-dual}, unlike~$\kappa$ which is
  anti-symmetric for KM/free fields ($\kappa + \kappa' = 0$).
\item Exact factorization functors preserving quadratic OPE data
  preserve~$T_{\mathrm{br},\cA}$.
\item The spectral radius
  $\rho(T_{\mathrm{br},\cA})=\max_i|\lambda_i|$ equals
  $\dim\mathfrak g$ for affine Kac--Moody at generic level.
\end{enumerate}

\emph{Example: $\mathfrak{sl}_3$.}  The Koszul dual Hilbert series
of $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_3$ satisfies a degree-$3$ recurrence.
The transfer matrix is $3\times 3$ with eigenvalues $8$,
$(3+\sqrt{13})/2$, $(3-\sqrt{13})/2$.  The spectral discriminant is
\[
\Delta_{\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_3}(x)
\;=\;
(1-8x)(1-3x-x^2).
\]
The dominant eigenvalue $8=\dim(\mathfrak{sl}_3)$ controls the
exponential growth of bar cohomology dimensions.  The remaining
eigenvalues $(3\pm\sqrt{13})/2$ are the roots of the DS
discriminant factor, shared with the $\mathcal W_3$ generating
function.

\emph{Example: Heisenberg.}  The Hilbert series
$h_{\mathcal H_k^!}(q)=1+q$ is a polynomial (the recurrence has
order~$0$ after the first term), so
$\Delta_{\mathcal H_k}(x)=1$: there is no non-scalar
structure.  This is the Gaussian archetype: $\kappa$ alone
determines everything.

\emph{Example: $\beta\gamma$.}  The Hilbert series is
$\sqrt{(1{+}q)/(1{-}3q)}$; the discriminant is
$\Delta_{\beta\gamma}(x)=(1-3x)(1+x)$.  The two roots at
$x=1/3$ and $x=-1$ coincide with $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$
and the Virasoro algebra.

In the Chern--Weil dictionary, $\Delta_\cA$ plays the role of the
Chern character: the logarithmic derivative
\[
\operatorname{ch}_r(\cA)
\;=\;
\frac{1}{r!}\,
\frac{d^r}{dt^r}\Big|_{t=0}\bigl[-\log\Delta_\cA(t)\bigr]
\;=\;
\frac{1}{r}\operatorname{tr}(T_{\mathrm{br},\cA}^r)
\]
recovers the power-sum symmetric functions of the eigenvalues.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{The quartic shadow
$\mathfrak R^{\mathrm{mod}}_{4,g,n}(\cA)$:}
\[
\mathfrak R^{\mathrm{mod}}_{4,g,n}(\cA)
\;=\;
\operatorname{pr}_{4,g,n}(\Theta_\cA)
\;\in\;
H^*(\overline{\cM}_{g,n})\otimes
(\bar\cA^{\vee})^{\otimes n}_{\mathrm{cyc}}.
\]
This is the first \emph{nonlinear} characteristic class: the first
invariant that cannot be recovered from~$\kappa$ and~$\Delta_\cA$.
Its genus-zero, four-point specialisation is the quartic contact
invariant $Q^{\mathrm{contact}}(\cA)$.  Explicit:
\[
Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{Vir}}
\;=\;
\frac{10}{c(5c+22)},
\qquad
Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\cH}=0,
\qquad
Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\beta\gamma}
\;\neq\; 0.
\]
For Heisenberg, the quartic vanishes (no cubic OPE pole).
For $\beta\gamma$, the quartic is the first gauge-nontrivial
shadow (the cubic is gauge-removable by
Theorem~\ref{thm:cubic-gauge-triviality}).  For Virasoro, both cubic and
quartic are nonvanishing.

\subsection*{5.4.\enspace The Chern--Weil dictionary}

The analogy between $\Theta_\cA$ and a connection $1$-form is
exact.  The modular bar bundle
$\mathrm{B}^{\log}_{\mathrm{mod}}(\cA)\to\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$
is a principal bundle for the gauge group of the convolution
algebra; $\Theta_\cA$ is its flat connection (flatness automatic
from the bar-intrinsic construction); and the shadow
tower is its Chern--Weil theory.  Holonomy becomes factorisation
homology, gauge equivalence becomes MC gauge, and the Weil
homomorphism becomes the shadow algebra
$\cA^{\mathrm{sh}} = H_\bullet(\Defcyc^{\mathrm{mod}})$.

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.25}
\begin{tabular}{ll}
\textbf{Classical Chern--Weil}
  & \textbf{Modular factorization}\\
\hline
Principal $G$-bundle $P\to M$
  & Modular bar bundle
    $\mathrm{B}^{\log}_{\mathrm{mod}}(\cA)\to\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$\\[2pt]
Connection $1$-form $\omega\in\Omega^1(P,\fg)$
  & MC element $\Theta_\cA\in\mathrm{MC}(\gAmod)$\\[2pt]
Curvature $\Omega=d\omega+\frac{1}{2}[\omega,\omega]$
  & MC equation $D\Theta_\cA+\tfrac12[\Theta_\cA,\Theta_\cA]=0$\\[2pt]
Flatness $\Omega=0$
  & Automatic (bar-intrinsic)\\[2pt]
First Chern class $c_1\in H^2(M;\mathbb Z)$
  & Scalar curvature $\kappa(\cA)=\operatorname{tr}(\Theta_\cA)_{2,0}$\\[2pt]
Chern character $\operatorname{ch}=\operatorname{tr}\exp(\Omega/2\pi i)$
  & Spectral determinant
    $\Delta_\cA(t)=\operatorname{sdet}(1-tH_{d_\Theta})$\\[2pt]
Higher Chern classes $c_r$
  & Shadows $\mathfrak R^{\mathrm{mod}}_{4,g,n}$,
    $\mathrm{Sh}_r$ for $r\ge 5$\\[2pt]
Weil homomorphism $W\colon\operatorname{Sym}^*(\fg^*)^G\to H^*(M)$
  & Shadow algebra
    $\cA^{\mathrm{sh}}=H_\bullet(\Defcyc^{\mathrm{mod}})$\\[2pt]
$\operatorname{ad}$-invariant polynomial
  & Cyclic cocycle in $\Defcyc^{\mathrm{mod}}(\cA)$\\[2pt]
Cyclic pairing $\operatorname{tr}(XY)$
  & Verdier duality on $\operatorname{Ran}(X)$\\[2pt]
Group multiplication $G\times G\to G$
  & Operadic composition in $\cP^{\mathrm{ch}}$\\[2pt]
Coproduct on $\cO(G)$
  & Operadic cocomposition / clutching / degeneration\\[2pt]
Lagrangian splitting $T^*G=\fg\oplus\fg^*$
  & Complementarity $Q_g(\cA)\oplus Q_g(\cA^!)
    =H^*(\overline{\cM}_g,\mathcal Z(\cA))$\\[2pt]
Holonomy $\operatorname{Hol}(\gamma)\in G$
  & Factorisation homology $\int_\Sigma\cA$\\[2pt]
Gauge equivalence $\omega\sim g^{-1}\omega g+g^{-1}dg$
  & MC gauge in
    $\mathrm{MC}_\bullet(\gAmod)$\\[2pt]
Transgression $\mathrm{CS}(\omega)\in\Omega^3$
  & Shadow Postnikov obstruction tower (Section~6)\\[2pt]
Flat sections $\nabla s=0$
  & Twisted cochains $d_{\Theta_\cA}(x)=0$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\subsection*{5.5.\enspace The genus spectral sequence}

The genus filtration $F^g L_{\mathrm{mod}}:=\bigoplus_{g'\ge g}
(\gAmod)_{g',*,*}$ yields a convergent spectral sequence.  Write
$D_0=D_{\mathrm{int}}+D_{\mathrm{sep}}$ for the genus-preserving
part of the differential and $D_1=D_{\mathrm{nsep}}$ for the
genus-raising part.  These satisfy $D_0^2=0$,
$D_0D_1+D_1D_0=0$, $D_1^2=0$ (a bicomplex structure).

The spectral sequence:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
\item $E_0^{p,q}=\operatorname{gr}_F^p L_{\mathrm{mod}}^{p+q}$
  with differential $d_0=[D_0,-]$.
\item $E_1^{p,*}=H^*(\operatorname{gr}_F^p L_{\mathrm{mod}},d_0)$:
  the associated graded cohomology, genus by genus.  $p=0$:
  tree-level (unlooped homotopy transfer).  $p=1$:
  one-loop (BV trace and deformations).  $p=2$:
  genus-two shells (loops, clutching, planted forests).
\item $d_1\colon E_1^{0,*}\to E_1^{1,*}$ is the genus-one
  obstruction $\operatorname{Ob}_1$: the obstruction to lifting a
  tree-level MC element to one-loop.  More generally,
  $d_r\colon E_r^{p,*}\to E_r^{p+r,*-r+1}$ encodes
  $\operatorname{Ob}_r$.
\item $E_\infty^{p,q}\cong\operatorname{gr}_F^p H^{p+q}
  (L_{\mathrm{mod}})$: the associated graded of the full modular
  cohomology.
\end{enumerate}
Convergence follows from completeness of the depth filtration and
pronilpotence of the weight filtration: the
$\varprojlim^1$ term vanishes by Mittag-Leffler
(finite-dimensionality in each conformal weight).

This spectral sequence is \emph{distinct} from the PBW spectral
sequence (which decomposes by conformal weight within a fixed genus).
PBW computes \emph{what} bar cohomology is;
the genus spectral sequence determines \emph{whether} the MC element
extends across genera.  For Heisenberg, it
degenerates at $E_1$.  For Virasoro,
$d_1\neq 0$ and nontrivial differentials persist at every page.

\subsection*{5.6.\enspace Homotopy invariance and functoriality}

The shadow algebra
$\cA^{\mathrm{sh}}=H_\bullet(\Defcyc^{\mathrm{mod}}(\cA))$ is a
homotopy invariant of the chiral algebra.  For any
$\infty_\alpha$-quasi-isomorphism
$f\colon\cA\xrightarrow{\sim}\cA'$, the induced map on MC
$\infty$-groupoids
\[
f_*\colon
\operatorname{MC}_\bullet(\gAmod)
\;\xrightarrow{\;\sim\;}
\operatorname{MC}_\bullet(\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{mod}}_{\cA'})
\]
is a weak homotopy equivalence (a quasi-isomorphism on tangent
complexes at corresponding MC elements).  In particular:
\begin{itemize}
\item The scalar $\kappa(\cA)$ is a quasi-isomorphism invariant.
\item The spectral determinant $\Delta_\cA(t)$ is a
  quasi-isomorphism invariant.
\item The full shadow obstruction tower
  $(\kappa,\Delta,\mathfrak C,\mathfrak Q,\mathrm{Sh}_5,
  \mathrm{Sh}_6,\dots)$ consists of quasi-isomorphism invariants.
\item The MC element $\Theta_\cA$ is a quasi-isomorphism invariant
  up to gauge: $f_*(\Theta_\cA)$ and $\Theta_{\cA'}$ are
  gauge-equivalent in $\mathrm{MC}_\bullet(\mathfrak
  g^{\mathrm{mod}}_{\cA'})$.
\end{itemize}

The assignment
$\cA\mapsto(\gAmod,\Theta_\cA)$ is a functor from
chiral algebras (with $\infty_\alpha$-quasi-isos
inverted) to MC moduli problems:
modular Koszul duality is a derived invariant.

The convolution $L_\infty$ algebra
$\Convinf(\cC,\cP)$ is functorial in each slot separately, but
\emph{not} simultaneously as a bifunctor (\S3).  Functoriality of
$\cA\mapsto\gAmod$ proceeds through the source slot,
with the target operad held fixed.

\subsection*{5.7.\enspace The shadow CohFT and topological recursion}

Projected
to $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$, the MC equation produces
tautological classes and tautological relations.
The MC element $\Theta_\cA$ determines shadow tautological classes
$\tau_{g,n}(\cA)\in R^*(\overline{\cM}_{g,n+1})$
that assemble into a cohomological field theory
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-cohft}):
the factorisation axiom holds by the clutching law
for~$\Theta_\cA$, the $\Sigma_n$-equivariance by the symmetry of
stable-graph summation, and the flat identity conditionally (when
the vacuum lies in~$V$).

Projecting the MC equation
$D\Theta_\cA+\tfrac12[\Theta_\cA,\Theta_\cA]=0$ to the
$(g,n)$-component yields a tautological relation in
$R^*(\overline{\cM}_{g,n})$ at each $(g,n)$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:mc-tautological-descent}):
\[
\sum_{\mathrm{sep}/\mathrm{nsep}}
\xi_{\mathrm{sep},*}\bigl(
\tau_{g_1,|S|}(\cA)\cdot\tau_{g_2,|S^c|}(\cA)\bigr)
+\delta_{\mathrm{pf}}^{(g,n)}
\;=\;0.
\]

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{WDVV and Mumford from MC.}\enspace
At genus~$0$, arity~$3$: the MC tautological relation on
$\overline{\cM}_{0,4}$ reduces to the WDVV equations
(Proposition~\ref{prop:wdvv-from-mc}).  At arity~$2$,
genus~$g\geq 2$: substituting
$\tau_{g,2}(\cA)=\kappa(\cA)\cdot\pi^*\lambda_g$ recovers
the Mumford $\lambda$-class clutching relation on
$\overline{\cM}_g$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:mumford-from-mc}).

The complementarity propagator
$P_\cA\colon H^*(\cA)\otimes H^*(\cA^!)\to\mathbb C$
is the Givental $R$-matrix of the shadow CohFT; when
it carries a flat unit (all standard families
with vacuum in~$V$; Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-cohft}),
Teleman reconstruction recovers $\{\tau_{g,n}\}$
at all $(g,n)$ from genus-$0$ data and~$P_\cA$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:cohft-reconstruction}).  Eynard--Orantin
topological recursion is the MC equation applied to the shadow obstruction tower
(Corollary~\ref{cor:topological-recursion-mc-shadow}).

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{ll}
\textbf{MC datum} & \textbf{Tautological output} \\ \hline
$\Theta_\cA\in\mathrm{MC}(\gAmod)$
  & shadow CohFT $\Omega_{g,n}^\cA$ \\[2pt]
$D^2=0$ on $\mathrm{FM}^{\log}$
  & CohFT axioms \\[2pt]
$D\Theta+\tfrac12[\Theta,\Theta]=0$ at $(g,n)$
  & tautological relation \\[2pt]
$[\Theta,\Theta]|_{\mathrm{sep}}$
  & WDVV / associativity \\[2pt]
$\hbar\Delta(\Theta)|_{\mathrm{nsep}}$
  & Mumford $\lambda$-class relations \\[2pt]
$P_\cA$
  & Givental $R$-matrix \\[2pt]
MC recursion
  & EO topological recursion
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The Pixton shadow bridge.}\enspace
For class-M algebras (infinite shadow obstruction tower), $\Theta_\cA$ generates tautological classes at every genus.
At genus~$2$--$3$, the relations
$\tau_{g,n}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$ for generic~$c$ produce elements of the
Pixton ideal in~$R^*(\overline{\cM}_{g,n})$: Pixton's tautological ring
relations arise as shadows of the Virasoro MC
equation.  Conjecture~\ref{conj:pixton-from-shadows}: class-M algebras
generate the Pixton ideal via the infinite MC tower.  Computationally
supported at genus~$2$--$3$; formal ideal membership
in the strata algebra is open.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The B\"ocherer bridge.}\enspace
At genus~$2$, the shadow tautological class
$\tau_{2,0}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$ for lattice vertex algebras computes a
central $L$-value via the B\"ocherer conjecture (now a theorem of
Furusawa--Morimoto).  For the Leech lattice:
$\chi_{12}=\mathrm{SK}(f_{22})$ (the Saito--Kurokawa lift of the
unique weight-$22$ cuspidal eigenform), and the MC-derived second
Fourier coefficient $c_2\approx -1.918\times 10^{-6}\neq 0$ is the
first nonzero central $L$-value produced by the shadow obstruction tower.

\subsection*{5.8.\enspace The primitive kernel and cofree reduction}

The MC element $\Theta_\cA$ lives in the cofree
conilpotent coalgebra underlying the modular bar construction.
By Milnor--Moore for modular operads, $\Theta_\cA$
is determined by its restriction to primitive
corollas and rigid cutting strata, the \emph{primitive
logarithmic modular kernel}
\[
\mathfrak K_\cA
\;=\;
\sum_{g\geq 0,\,n\geq 2}K_{g,n}^\cA
+\sum_{\rho\in\mathrm{Rig}}K_\rho^\cA,
\]
where $K_{g,n}^\cA$ are genus-$g$ corolla coefficients and
$K_\rho^\cA$ are rigid boundary cutting terms.
The fundamental equivalence
(Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-to-global-reconstruction}):
\[
(Q_\cA^{\mathrm{mod}})^2=0
\quad\iff\quad
d\,\mathfrak K_\cA+\mathfrak K_\cA\star\mathfrak K_\cA
+\hbar\,\Delta_{\mathrm{ns}}(\mathfrak K_\cA)=0,
\]
where $\star$ is the primitive pre-Lie product from log-FM
residues, replaces the genus-by-genus obstruction programme
by a single equation on primitive data.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{Shell equations.}\enspace
Projecting the primitive master equation to genus~$2$ and
genus~$3$ shells gives explicit constraints:
\begin{align*}
R_2(\mathfrak K_\cA)
&=\Delta_{\mathrm{ns}}(K_1)
  +\tfrac12[K_1,K_1]
  +\textstyle\sum_{\rho\in\mathrm{Rig}_2}R_\rho^\cA(K_{0,2}^\cA),\\
R_3(\mathfrak K_\cA)
&=\Delta_{\mathrm{ns}}(K_2)
  +[K_1,K_2]
  +\tfrac{1}{3!}\ell_3(K_1,K_1,K_1)
  +\textstyle\sum_\rho R_\rho^\cA(\ldots).
\end{align*}
For the Heisenberg algebra, only the BV term
$\Delta_{\mathrm{ns}}$ survives.  For affine Kac--Moody,
the bracket $[K_1,K_1]$ contributes the cubic shadow.  For
$\beta\gamma$, cubic gauge triviality kills the bracket term
and the rigid stratum contributes the quartic contact
invariant.  For Virasoro and $\mathcal W_N$, all three terms
are active at every genus.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{The branch BV action.}\enspace
The finite-rank branch-active quotient
$V_\cA^{\mathrm{br}}=V_\cA^+\oplus V_\cA^-$, a
quotient of the modular tangent complex,
spanned by spectral generators, carries a BV master action
\[
S_\cA^{\mathrm{br}}(x,\xi)
=\tfrac12\Omega_\cA(K_\cA^{\mathrm{br}}x,x)
+\sum_{m+n\geq 3}
\frac{1}{m!\,n!}\mu_{m,n}^\cA(x^{\otimes m};\xi^{\otimes n}),
\]
satisfying
$\hbar\,\Delta_\cA^{\mathrm{br}}S_\cA^{\mathrm{br}}
+\tfrac12\{S_\cA^{\mathrm{br}},S_\cA^{\mathrm{br}}\}_{\mathrm{BV}}
=0$,
where $\{-,-\}_{\mathrm{BV}}$ is the odd Poisson bracket
induced by the invariant pairing on~$\cA$.
The \emph{metaplectic half-density}
$\delta_\cA\in 1+x\,\Bbbk\llbracket x\rrbracket$ satisfies
$\delta_\cA^2=\Delta_\cA=\det(1-x\,T_\cA^{\mathrm{br,red}})$:
the spectral discriminant is the square of a canonical
half-density.

\subsection*{5.9.\enspace Entanglement from the modular characteristic}

The bar coalgebra carries a natural bipartite structure: its
coproduct splits a configuration of points into two halves, one on
each side of a spatial cut.  This splitting connects the modular
characteristic directly to entanglement.

For a
spatial bipartition of an interval of length~$L$ with UV
cutoff~$\varepsilon$, the scalar projection of $\Theta_\cA$
restricted to the bipartite cut yields the
Ryu--Takayanagi formula:
\[
S_{\mathrm{EE}}(\cA)
\;=\;
\frac{c(\cA)}{3}\log\frac{L}{\varepsilon},
\]
where $c(\cA)$ is the central charge.
(For the Virasoro algebra, $c=2\kappa$; the relationship between
$c$ and~$\kappa$ is family-dependent.)
Complementarity gives the entanglement sum rule:
\[
S_{\mathrm{EE}}(\cA)+S_{\mathrm{EE}}(\cA^!)
\;=\;
\frac{c(\cA)+c(\cA^!)}{3}\cdot\log\frac{L}{\varepsilon}.
\]
For the Virasoro family $\mathrm{Vir}_c^!=\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$,
this gives $c+c'=26$ and the universal sum~$26/3\cdot\log(L/\varepsilon)$.

The four shadow-depth classes (G/L/C/M) classify entanglement
complexity: class~G algebras (Gaussian, $r_{\max}=2$) exhibit
area-law entanglement only; class~L ($r_{\max}=3$) adds subleading
logarithmic corrections from the cubic shadow; class~C
($r_{\max}=4$) adds a contact correction from the quartic
invariant; and class~M ($r_{\max}=\infty$) carries an infinite tower
of entanglement corrections, one for each shadow.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The entanglement programme (G11--G16).}\enspace
Six theorem targets extend the scalar result.
\emph{G11}: the Ryu--Takayanagi formula above, proved from the
scalar projection of~$\Theta_\cA$.
\emph{G12} (Koszulness $=$ exact quantum error correction): the
Knill--Laflamme condition for quantum error correction is the
Lagrangian isotropy condition from the complementarity pairing;
shadow depth~$r_{\max}$ equals the number of redundancy channels;
the twelve Koszulness characterizations (K1--K12; ten
unconditional equivalences, one conditional, one
one-directional) translate into a
twelve-fold code dictionary; failure of Koszulness is failure of
the code.
\emph{G13}: the replica trick from the MC equation (the
$n$-sheeted cover computation is the $n$-fold bar coproduct).
\emph{G14}: modular flow from the tangent complex (the Tomita
modular operator is the $L_\infty$-twisted differential
$d_{\Theta_\cA}$, restricted to the bipartite subalgebra).
\emph{G15}: the quantum extremal surface as the shadow
connection Ward identity: the QES equation is the stationarity
condition for the shadow metric~$Q_L(t)$ restricted to the
entanglement cut.
\emph{G16}: the Page curve from the shadow connection at $c = 13$
(the self-dual point): the Page transition occurs when the
shadow growth rate~$\rho(\cA)$ crosses the entanglement
threshold, and the scrambling time is controlled by the
spectral discriminant~$\Delta_\cA$.

% ====================================================================
\section*{6.\quad The shadow obstruction tower}
% ====================================================================

\subsection*{6.1.\enspace The extension tower}

Can $\Theta_\cA$ be approximated by finitely many
arities, and what controls the passage from one finite
approximation to the next?  The total weight
filtration answers both.

Define the \emph{total weight} $w(g,r,d):=2g-2+r+d$, where $g$ is
loop genus, $r$ is arity, and $d$ is log boundary depth.  The total
weight filtration $F^N\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{amb}}_\cA:=\bigoplus_{w\ge N}(\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{amb}}_\cA)_{g,r,d}$
is an exhaustive, separated, complete filtration.  Here
$\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{amb}}_\cA$ denotes the \emph{ambient}
(planted-forest-extended) modular convolution algebra, the
extension of $\gAmod$ by the planted-forest coefficient algebra
$\mathcal G_{\mathrm{pf}}$ that incorporates log boundary
strata.  The \emph{modular extension tower}:
\[
\cE_\cA(N)
:=\operatorname{MC}\bigl(\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{amb}}_\cA/F^{N+1}\bigr),
\qquad N\ge 1.
\]
Restriction maps
$\cE_\cA(N+1)\to\cE_\cA(N)$ truncate the top weight.  A
\emph{full lift} is a compatible point of the inverse system:
\[
\Theta_\cA\;\in\;
\varprojlim_{N}\,\cE_\cA(N).
\]
The bar-intrinsic construction provides such a point
unconditionally.  The shadow obstruction tower is the study of the
extension tower $\cE_\cA(1)\leftarrow
\cE_\cA(2)\leftarrow\cE_\cA(3)\leftarrow\cdots$ and the
obstructions that arise at each stage.

\subsection*{6.2.\enspace Obstruction classes and the all-arity master equation}

Define the truncated MC elements $\Theta_\cA^{\le r}$ by projecting
$\Theta_\cA$ to total weight $\le r$.  The \emph{shadow obstruction
tower} is the sequence
\[
\Theta_\cA^{\le 2},\quad
\Theta_\cA^{\le 3},\quad
\Theta_\cA^{\le 4},\quad
\Theta_\cA^{\le 5},\quad\dots
\]
At each truncation, the MC equation fails by a remainder:
\[
D\Theta^{\le r}_\cA
+\tfrac12[\Theta^{\le r}_\cA,\Theta^{\le r}_\cA]
\;=\;
-o_{r+1}(\cA),
\]
where the \emph{obstruction class} $o_{r+1}(\cA)$ lives in the
$(r+1)$-graded piece:
\[
o_{r+1}(\cA)
\;\in\;
Z^2\!\left(\frac{F^{r+1}\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{amb}}_\cA}
{F^{r+2}\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{amb}}_\cA},\;d_{\le r}\right).
\]
The truncation extends to
$\Theta^{\le r+1}$ if and only if $[o_{r+1}(\cA)]=0$ in
$H^2(F^{r+1}/F^{r+2},d_{\le r})$.  The bar-intrinsic
construction guarantees that extension always exists, so
the obstruction class is always exact; the shadow obstruction tower
records the gauge choices at each stage.

The all-arity master equation at arity~$r$ is:
\[
\nabla_H(\mathrm{Sh}_r(\cA))+o^{(r)}(\cA)=0,
\qquad r\ge 3,
\]
where $\nabla_H$ is the Hodge covariant derivative (the linearised
MC operator twisted by the previous stages) and $\mathrm{Sh}_r(\cA)$
is the arity-$r$ shadow (the named invariant extracted from
$\Theta^{\le r}$).  This equation determines $\mathrm{Sh}_r$
uniquely modulo gauge if $H^1(F^r/F^{r+1},d_{\le r-1})=0$, and
up to the image of a gauge map otherwise.

\subsection*{6.3.\enspace Cubic gauge triviality and the canonical quartic}

\begin{quote}
\textbf{Cubic gauge triviality.}\enspace
When $H^1(F^3\mathfrak g/F^4\mathfrak g,\,d_2)=0$, the cubic MC
term $\Theta^{[3]}_\cA$ is gauge-trivial: there exists a gauge
transformation $\exp(\xi_3)$ with $\xi_3\in F^3$ such that
$\exp(\xi_3)\cdot\Theta^{\le 3}_\cA$ has vanishing weight-$3$
component.
\end{quote}

After this gauge transformation, the quartic obstruction class
$[\mathfrak Q(\cA)]\in H^2(F^4\mathfrak g/F^5\mathfrak g,\,d_2)$
is \emph{canonical}: independent of homotopy
retraction data, cubic gauge, and MC gauge orbit representative.
This is the first characteristic class
not polynomial in~$\kappa$.

The mechanism is standard Postnikov:
$o_3(\cA)\in H^2(F^3/F^4,d_2)$ is exact (since
$\Theta_\cA$ exists), and the cochain $\Theta^{[3]}$
lifting it is unique up to coboundary when
$H^1(F^3/F^4,d_2)=0$.  After removal, the quartic error is a
well-defined cohomology class: trivial $H^1$ at level~$n$ makes the $H^2$ class at
level~$n+1$ canonical.

The clutching law for the quartic class follows from Mok's log
FM degeneration formula.  For a degeneration
$C\leadsto C_0=C_1\cup_p C_2$:
\[
\mathfrak Q(\cA)\big|_{C_0}
\;=\;
\sum_{a+b=4}\mathfrak Q^{(a)}(\cA)\big|_{C_1}
\cdot\mathfrak Q^{(b)}(\cA)\big|_{C_2}
\;+\;
\text{planted-forest correction}.
\]
The planted-forest correction is genuinely logarithmic,
with no counterpart in the classical Deligne--Mumford setting.

The quartic contact invariant:
\[
Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{Vir}}
\;=\;
\frac{10}{c(5c+22)}
\;\in\;
H^2(F^4/F^5,d_2).
\]
The denominator $c(5c+22)$ has physical meaning: $c=0$ is the
logarithmic threshold; $c=-22/5$ is the minimal model accumulation
point $\mathcal M(2,5)$.  The numerator~$10=\binom{5}{2}$ counts
the arity-four Catalan channels.


\subsection*{6.4.\enspace The Hamilton--Jacobi generating function}

For a multi-generator algebra ($\mathcal{W}_3$ with
generators $T$ (weight~$2$) and $W$ (weight~$3$)), the
deformation space is two-dimensional.  The Riccati ODE lifts
to a Hamilton--Jacobi PDE.  Write
$U=\sum_{s\ge 3}\mathrm{Sh}_s(x_T,x_W)$.  The master equation
becomes
\[
2\,E(U)+\tfrac{1}{2}\lVert\nabla U\rVert^2_H
\;=\;R(x_T,x_W),
\]
with Euler operator $E=x_T\partial_T+x_W\partial_W$,
kinetic energy
$\lVert\nabla U\rVert^2_H
=(2/c)(\partial_T U)^2+(3/c)(\partial_W U)^2$,
and $R$ a polynomial of degree~$\le 4$ encoding the
three inputs $(\kappa,\mathfrak{C},\mathfrak{Q})$.
The gradient
$dU\colon X\to T^*X$ embeds the deformation space as a
Lagrangian submanifold of $T^*X$
($X = \bC\cdot x_T\oplus\bC\cdot x_W$,
kinetic form positive-definite for $c>0$),
by the Hamilton--Jacobi theorem applied to the stationary
equation with Euler operator~$E$ as
arity-filtration weight.  Whether the genus expansion
$\Theta_\cA = \sum_{g \geq 0}\hbar^g\Theta_\cA^{(g)}$
admits a quantisation in which $U$ is the leading
semiclassical term is an open problem: it would require
constructing a quantum Hamiltonian whose WKB expansion
has leading term~$U$ and whose quantum corrections
reproduce the genus-$g$ shadow amplitudes.

On the $T$-line ($x_W=0$): conformal weight forces the
transverse momentum $p_W=(\partial_W U)|_{x_W=0}$ to vanish,
and the Hamilton--Jacobi PDE collapses to the Riccati ODE.
On the $W$-line ($x_T=0$): the cubic shadow
$\mathrm{Sh}_3 = 2x_T^3 + 3x_T x_W^2$
has nonzero normal derivative
$(\partial_T\mathrm{Sh}_3)|_{x_T=0}=3x_W^2$,
so the transverse kinetic energy is nonzero.  The first
inter-channel coupling correction enters at arity~$6$:
\[
\delta_6^{W\text{-line}}
\;=\;
\frac{576(5c+38)}{c^3(5c+22)^3}.
\]
The $T$-line is autonomous; the $W$-line is not.  The
asymmetry is intrinsic: it traces to the conformal-weight
asymmetry between $T$ (weight~$2$) and $W$ (weight~$3$).

\subsection*{6.5.\enspace The four depth classes}

The \emph{shadow depth} $r_{\max}(\cA)$ is the smallest integer~$r$
such that $o_{r+1}(\cA)=0$ for all subsequent levels, or
$r_{\max}=\infty$ if the tower never terminates.  Equivalently,
$r_{\max}$ is the largest arity at which the shadow obstruction tower carries a
nontrivial invariant.

The standard landscape partitions into exactly four depth classes;
no other values occur on any one-dimensional primary
slice.  The single-line dichotomy
(Theorem~\ref{thm:single-line-dichotomy}): the shadow metric
$Q_L(t)$ is quadratic in $(\kappa,\alpha,S_4)$,
and its factorisation type (perfect square or
irreducible) determines whether the tower terminates.

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{lcccll}
\textbf{Class} & \textbf{Symbol} & $r_{\max}$
  & $\ell_3^{(0)},\;\ell_4^{(0)}$
  & \textbf{Potential type} & \textbf{Examples}\\
\hline
Gaussian & G & $2$ & $0,\;0$
  & quadratic
  & Heisenberg $\cH_k$, free fermion $\psi$\\
Lie/tree & L & $3$ & $\neq 0,\;0$
  & cubic
  & Affine $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_N$, current algebras\\
Contact & C & $4$ & $0,\;\neq 0$
  & quartic
  & $\beta\gamma$, $bc$ ghosts\\
Mixed & M & $\infty$ & $\neq 0,\;\neq 0$
  & non-polynomial
  & Virasoro, $\mathcal W_N$, $\mathcal W_\infty$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent
The depth class is determined by the OPE structure:
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Gaussian} ($r_{\max}=2$): the transferred brackets
  $\ell_k^{(0)}$ vanish for $k \ge 3$ on bar cohomology, so
  the tower terminates at~$\kappa$.  Two mechanisms:
  Heisenberg has no simple pole ($S_3 = 0$, no
  Lie bracket); the free fermion has a simple pole but
  fermionic antisymmetry forces $S_3 = 0$ (parity on three-point configuration space).
  Sewing is by Fredholm determinant
  (Heisenberg) or Pfaffian (fermion).
  The potential is quadratic.
\item \textbf{Lie/tree} ($r_{\max}=3$): the OPE has a simple pole
  generating a Lie bracket, but the transferred quaternary bracket
  $\ell_4^{(0)}$ vanishes on bar cohomology.  The ternary bracket
  is the last nontrivial shadow.  The potential is cubic.
\item \textbf{Contact} ($r_{\max}=4$): the simple-pole bracket
  vanishes on bar cohomology (as in Heisenberg), but the quaternary
  bracket survives.  The first nontrivial shadow is
  $\mathfrak Q(\cA)$, and the tower terminates there.
  The potential is quartic.
\item \textbf{Mixed} ($r_{\max}=\infty$): both cubic and quartic
  shadows are nontrivial, and their interaction (the Poisson bracket
  $\{\mathfrak C,\mathfrak Q\}_H$) generates a nonvanishing quintic
  obstruction, which in turn generates a sextic, and so on.  The
  tower never terminates.  The potential is transcendental.
\end{itemize}

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{Shadow depth is not Koszulness.}\enspace
All four depth classes contain chirally Koszul algebras.  Heisenberg
(depth~$2$), affine at generic level (depth~$3$), $\beta\gamma$
(depth~$4$), and Virasoro (depth~$\infty$) are all chirally Koszul.
Shadow depth classifies the \emph{complexity} of Koszul algebras,
not Koszulness itself.

The \emph{operadic complexity theorem}
(Theorem~\ref{conj:operadic-complexity-detailed}): the shadow depth
equals the $A_\infty$-depth equals the $L_\infty$-formality level:
\[
r_{\max}(\cA)
\;=\;
A_\infty\text{-depth}(\cA)
\;=\;
L_\infty\text{-formality level}(\cA).
\]
Here $A_\infty$-depth is the largest~$r$ with $m_r\neq 0$ in
the minimal $A_\infty$ model; $L_\infty$-formality
level is the largest~$r$ with a nontrivial $r$-ary bracket on bar
cohomology (not removable by
$L_\infty$-isomorphism).  The shadow obstruction tower equals
the $L_\infty$ formality obstruction tower at all
arities
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-formality-identification}).

\subsection*{6.6.\enspace The genus--arity bigrading}

The MC equation decomposes along two orthogonal axes
(Remark~\ref{rem:two-orthogonal-axes}).  The \emph{genus axis}
extends $\Theta_\cA$ from genus~$0$ to~$1$ to~$2$,
controlled by the genus spectral sequence
(Construction~\ref{const:vol1-genus-spectral-sequence}).  The
\emph{arity axis} extends $\Theta_\cA^{\leq 2}$ to
$\Theta_\cA^{\leq 3}$ to $\Theta_\cA^{\leq 4}$,
controlled by cyclic obstruction classes.  At fixed arity~$2$
the genus tower is governed by~$\kappa$ alone; at fixed genus~$0$ each new shadow coefficient introduces
independent data.
The axes couple through the \emph{visibility formula}
(Corollary~\ref{cor:shadow-visibility-genus}):
$g_{\min}(S_r) = \lfloor r/2 \rfloor + 1$, so $S_r$ first
contributes at genus $\lfloor r/2 \rfloor + 1$ and two new shadow
coefficients enter at each genus.

\subsection*{6.7.\enspace Genus-two shells}

Genus~$2$ is the first level where all three boundary
strata interact.  The genus-two MC component
decomposes as:
\[
\Theta^{(2)}_\cA
\;=\;
\underbrace{\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{loop}\circ\mathrm{loop}}}_{%
\text{iterated BV: two self-loops}}
\;+\;
\underbrace{\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{sep}\circ\mathrm{loop}}}_{%
\text{clutching $\times$ BV: one separating + one self-loop}}
\;+\;
\underbrace{\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{pf}}}_{%
\text{planted-forest: Mok's log-FM strata}}.
\]

The iterated-BV term $\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{loop}^2}$ involves the
graph with one vertex of genus~$0$ and two self-loops (the
``figure-eight'').  Its amplitude is the iterated trace:
\[
\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{loop}^2}
\;=\;
\tfrac{1}{2}\operatorname{tr}_1\operatorname{tr}_2
\bigl(P_\cA^{\otimes 2}\circ m^{(h)}_{0,4}\circ\Delta^{\otimes 2}\bigr).
\]

The separating-times-loop term
$\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{sep}\circ\mathrm{loop}}$ is the graph with
two vertices connected by a separating edge, one vertex carrying a
self-loop.  Its amplitude is:
\[
\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{sep}\circ\mathrm{loop}}
\;=\;
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{ns}}\bigl(
P_\cA\circ\ell_2^{(0)}(\Theta^{(1,\bullet)},\Theta^{(1,\bullet)})
\bigr).
\]

The planted-forest term is the genuinely logarithmic contribution,
present only when the algebra has nontrivial cubic or quartic
shadows.  It arises from depth-$2$ strata of
$\operatorname{FM}_n(X\mathbin{|}D)$ that have no classical
counterpart.

\medskip

\noindent
The family-by-family structure:

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{lcccc}
& $\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{loop}^2}$
& $\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{sep}\circ\mathrm{loop}}$
& $\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{pf}}$
& \textbf{Depth class}\\
\hline
\textbf{Heisenberg} $\cH_k$
  & $\checkmark$ & --- & --- & G\\
\textbf{Affine} $\widehat{\fg}_k$
  & $\checkmark$ & $\checkmark$ & --- & L\\
\textbf{$\beta\gamma$ system}
  & $\checkmark$ & --- & --- & C\\
\textbf{Virasoro} $\mathrm{Vir}_c$
  & $\checkmark$ & $\checkmark$ & $\checkmark$ & M\\
$\boldsymbol{\mathcal W_N}$
  & $\checkmark$ & $\checkmark$ & $\checkmark$ & M
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

For Heisenberg: only the iterated BV contributes (two independent
loop contractions on a free field).  No separating clutching (the Lie
bracket on bar cohomology is central) and no planted forests (no
higher interactions).  For affine: the separating-times-loop term
appears (the Lie bracket creates a nontrivial genus-one correction
after one clutching), but planted forests are absent (the cubic
shadow terminates the tower).  For Virasoro and $\mathcal W_N$: all
three terms contribute, and the planted-forest term carries the
quartic resonance data.  For $\beta\gamma$: both the separating and planted-forest terms
vanish: the separating term because the Lie bracket is trivial on
bar cohomology, the planted-forest term because the quartic contact
invariant $\mu_{\beta\gamma}=0$ (rank-one abelian rigidity).  Only
the iterated BV shell contributes, as for Heisenberg, but via
contact termination rather than Gaussian collapse.

\subsection*{6.8.\enspace The genus loop operator}

The \emph{genus loop operator}
$\Lambda_P\colon\operatorname{Sym}^r(\bar\cA^\vee)_{\mathrm{cyc}}
\to\operatorname{Sym}^{r-2}(\bar\cA^\vee)_{\mathrm{cyc}}$ contracts
two legs of an arity-$r$ cyclic cochain with the propagator:
\[
\Lambda_P(\phi)(a_1,\dots,a_{r-2})
\;=\;
\sum_i\phi(a_1,\dots,a_{r-2},e_i,e^i),
\]
where $\{e_i\}$, $\{e^i\}$ is a dual basis for the cyclic pairing.
This raises genus by~$1$ and lowers arity by~$2$: the shadow-level incarnation of the
BV operator $\Delta_{\mathrm{ns}}$.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{Explicit Virasoro computation.}\enspace
On the Virasoro primary line, the conformal-weight-$2$ bar
cohomology is one-dimensional, spanned by the class~$x$ dual to the
stress tensor~$T$.  The Killing form is $H=\frac{c}{2}x^2$ and the
propagator is $P=\frac{2}{c}$.  The quartic contact invariant is
$Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{Vir}}\cdot x^4$ with
$Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{Vir}}=10/[c(5c+22)]$.  The genus loop
operator applied to this quartic:
\[
\Lambda_P\!\left(\frac{10}{c(5c+22)}\cdot x^4\right)
\;=\;
\binom{4}{2}\cdot\frac{2}{c}\cdot
\frac{10}{c(5c+22)}\cdot x^2
\;=\;
\frac{120}{c^2(5c+22)}\,x^2.
\]
Here $\binom{4}{2}=6$ counts leg selections and
$2/c$ is the propagator.  The result is the \emph{genus-one Hessian
correction} $\delta_{H,\mathrm{Vir}}^{(1)}=120/[c^2(5c+22)]\cdot x^2$.

The \emph{loop ratio}:
\[
\rho^{(1)}_{\mathrm{Vir}}
\;=\;
\frac{\Lambda_P(Q\cdot x^4)}{\kappa\cdot x^2}
\;=\;
\frac{120/[c^2(5c+22)]}{c/2}
\;=\;
\frac{240}{c^3(5c+22)}.
\]
This ratio is not determined by $\kappa=c/2$: it
detects the quartic structure of the Virasoro algebra through its
genus-one projection.  The asymptotic behaviour
$\rho^{(1)}\sim 48/c^4$ for $c\to\infty$ reflects the weakening of
quartic corrections in the semiclassical limit.

\subsection*{6.9.\enspace Quintic forcing and infinite towers}

The quintic obstruction determines whether the tower
terminates at arity~$4$.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{Virasoro.}\enspace
The cubic shadow $\mathfrak C_{\mathrm{Vir}}$ and the quartic contact
invariant $Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{Vir}}$ are both nonzero.
Their Poisson bracket under the Hodge pairing gives the quintic
obstruction:
\[
o^{(5)}_{\mathrm{Vir}}
\;=\;
\{\mathfrak C_{\mathrm{Vir}},\,
Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{Vir}}\}_H
\;=\;
\frac{480}{c^2(5c+22)}\,x^5
\;\neq\;0.
\]
Since $o^{(5)}\neq 0$ for all $c\neq 0,-22/5$, the Virasoro shadow
tower does not terminate at any finite arity.  The tower is infinite:
$r_{\max}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)=\infty$.  The same holds for every
$\mathcal W_N$ algebra ($N\ge 2$): the cubic and quartic shadows
coexist and their bracket forces an infinite sequence of higher
obstructions.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{Heisenberg.}\enspace
$\mathfrak C_{\cH}=0$ and $Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\cH}=0$.  The
quintic obstruction $o^{(5)}=\{0,0\}_H=0$.  Every higher obstruction
also vanishes.  The tower terminates at $r_{\max}=2$.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{Affine.}\enspace
$\mathfrak C_{\widehat\fg}\neq 0$ but
$Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\widehat\fg}=0$ (the quaternary bracket
vanishes on bar cohomology by the PBW theorem for Kac--Moody
algebras).  The quintic obstruction
$o^{(5)}=\{\mathfrak C,0\}_H=0$.  The tower terminates at
$r_{\max}=3$.

\medskip

\noindent\textbf{$\beta\gamma$.}\enspace
$\mathfrak C_{\beta\gamma}=0$ (the Lie bracket is trivial on bar
cohomology) but $Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\beta\gamma}\neq 0$.
The quintic obstruction $o^{(5)}=\{0,Q\}_H=0$.  The tower terminates
at $r_{\max}=4$.

\medskip

\noindent
The pattern:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{lcccc}
& $\mathfrak C$ & $\mathfrak Q$
  & $o^{(5)}=\{\mathfrak C,\mathfrak Q\}_H$ & $r_{\max}$\\
\hline
Heisenberg & $0$ & $0$ & $0$ & $2$\\
Affine & $\neq 0$ & $0$ & $0$ & $3$\\
$\beta\gamma$ & $0$ & $\neq 0$ & $0$ & $4$\\
Virasoro & $\neq 0$ & $\neq 0$ & $\neq 0$ & $\infty$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
Finite termination requires $\mathfrak C=0$ or
$\mathfrak Q=0$.  When both are nonzero, their bracket generates
the quintic, the quintic and quartic generate the sextic, and
the induction continues without bound: a transcendental potential
on the MC moduli.


\medskip

\noindent\textbf{The shadow growth rate.}\enspace
For class~M algebras (infinite shadow depth), the Taylor
coefficients $S_r$ of $\sqrt{Q_L}$ grow as
$S_r \sim A\cdot\rho(\cA)^r\cdot r^{-5/2}\cos(r\theta+\varphi)$,
where the \emph{shadow growth rate}
$\rho(\cA) = \sqrt{9\alpha^2+2\Delta}\,/\,(2|\kappa|)$
is a continuous invariant on the modular deformation space.
Self-dual Virasoro ($c=13$) has $\rho\approx 0.467$.
The critical cubic $5c^3+22c^2-180c-872=0$ has root
$c^*\approx 6.125$: the tower converges for $c>c^*$ and
diverges for $c<c^*$.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The shadow partition function.}\enspace
The double sum $Z^{\mathrm{sh}}_\cA =
\sum_{g,r} \hbar^{2g-2}\,Z_g^{(r)}$ converges absolutely.
Genus decay is at rate $1/(2\pi)^{2g}$
(Faber--Pandharipande $\lambda_g$-integral); arity decay is at
rate $\rho^r \cdot r^{-5/2}$ (Darboux analysis of the shadow
metric).  By contrast, the string partition function
diverges as $(2g{-}2)!$.  For Virasoro at $c=26$:
$\rho\approx 0.234$, and $Z^{\mathrm{sh}}$ has radius of
absolute convergence in both $\hbar$ and arity.

\subsection*{6.10.\enspace Independent sum factorisation}

For a direct sum $L=L_1\oplus L_2$ of Lie conformal algebras with
vanishing mixed OPE ($[L_1{}_\lambda L_2]=0$), all shadow invariants
separate:
\begin{align*}
\kappa(L_1\oplus L_2)
&=\kappa(L_1)+\kappa(L_2)
&&\text{(additive)},\\[3pt]
T^{\mathrm{br}}(L_1\oplus L_2)
&=T^{\mathrm{br}}(L_1)\oplus T^{\mathrm{br}}(L_2)
&&\text{(direct sum)},\\[3pt]
\Delta_{L_1\oplus L_2}(t)
&=\Delta_{L_1}(t)\cdot\Delta_{L_2}(t)
&&\text{(multiplicative)},\\[3pt]
R_4^{\mathrm{mod}}(L_1\oplus L_2)
&=R_4^{\mathrm{mod}}(L_1)+R_4^{\mathrm{mod}}(L_2)
&&\text{(additive)}.
\end{align*}
More generally, the full MC element factorises:
\[
\Theta_{L_1\oplus L_2}
\;=\;
\Theta_{L_1}\hat\otimes 1+1\hat\otimes\Theta_{L_2}
\;\in\;
\gAmod[L_1]\;\hat\otimes\;\gAmod[L_2],
\]
where $\hat\otimes$ is the completed tensor product with respect to
the depth filtration; at the level of partition functions,
$Z_{L_1\oplus L_2}=Z_{L_1}\cdot Z_{L_2}$.

The factorisation principle reduces computation for composite
algebras to their primitive summands.  Every algebra in the standard
landscape is either primitive (Heisenberg, Virasoro, $\beta\gamma$)
or built from primitive pieces by direct sum plus extension
(affine = current algebra over simple Lie, lattice = exponential
extension of Heisenberg, $\mathcal W_N$ = quantum Drinfeld--Sokolov
reduction of affine).  The full shadow obstruction tower of any composite
algebra is determined by its primitive constituents.
Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction is the \emph{shadow-depth escalator}
(Principle~\ref{princ:shadow-depth-escalator}): it sends
current-algebra systems (class~$\mathbf{L}$, $r_{\max}=3$,
finite towers) to $\mathcal{W}$-algebra systems
(class~$\mathbf{M}$, $r_{\max}=\infty$, infinite towers).
The nonlinearity of the Dirac bracket on the Slodowy slice creates
the quartic and all higher shadows; no finite truncation survives
the reduction.

\subsection*{6.11.\enspace The representation-theoretic perspective}

The categorical logarithm $\eta_{ij} = d\log(z_i - z_j)$ of
Section~1 is the integral kernel of a tautology: $D_\cA^2 = 0$ on
the modular bar complex.  From this identity, three structure theorems
emerge.  \emph{Algebraicity}: on each primary slice~$L$, the shadow
generating function satisfies $H(t)^2 = t^4 Q_L(t)$, where $Q_L$ is
a quadratic polynomial in three invariants $\kappa$, $\alpha$, $S_4$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:riccati-algebraicity}).  \emph{Formality}: the
genus-$0$ shadow obstruction tower is the $L_\infty$ formality obstruction tower
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-formality-identification}); the four depth
classes G/L/C/M are the corresponding formality types, while
positive-genus corrections form a separate quantum layer.
\emph{Complementarity}: for a Koszul pair $(\cA, \cA^!)$, the summands
$\mathbf Q_g(\cA) \oplus \mathbf Q_g(\cA^!)$ are Lagrangian
(Theorem~C).

The discriminant $\Delta = 8\kappa S_4$ governs the
single-line dichotomy: on each primary deformation line,
$\Delta = 0$ forces tower termination ($L_\infty$-formality)
and $\Delta \neq 0$ forces an infinite tower
(intrinsic non-formality).  The contact class~C ($r_{\max} = 4$,
$\beta\gamma$) escapes via stratum separation.  No classical invariant of an algebra over a point
sees $\Delta$: it is visible only on curves of positive genus, where
the Arnold relation acquires a defect.

Classical Koszul duality (Priddy, Beilinson--Ginzburg--Soergel)
occupies genus~$0$, arity~$2$, $\Delta = 0$: the formal, class-G
case.  The $R$-matrix of quantum groups arises as the genus-$0$
shadow
$\mathrm{Sh}_{0,2}(\Theta_{\widehat{\fg}_k})$ (\S7.7).
At the critical level $k = -h^\vee$, the scalar class vanishes
($\kappa = 0$) and bar cohomology recovers the Feigin--Frenkel
center $\operatorname{Fun}(\mathrm{Op}_{{}^L\fg})$; the Langlands
programme lives on this orthogonal axis, not in the MC element
but in the cohomology that emerges on the uncurved scalar locus.

% ====================================================================
\section*{7.\quad The standard landscape}
% ====================================================================

The machine of Sections~1--6 accepts any chiral algebra as input.
The seven families
below exhaust the standard Lie-theoretic landscape: each exhibits a
different bar-complex structure, shadow archetype,
genus-two shell profile, and completion
behaviour.  No two families share all four invariants; taken
together, they realise every depth class (G/L/C/M), every curvature
sign, and every pattern of genus-two shell activation.

For each family we display the complete OPE,
bar complex with explicit differential, Koszul dual,
shadow obstruction tower with depth classification, modular characteristic
with complementarity, genus-two shell profile, and any structural
feature unique to that family.


% ----- 7.1 Heisenberg -----
\subsection*{7.1.\quad Heisenberg}

The Gaussian archetype: shadow depth~$2$,
the tower terminates at arity~$2$, and every higher-genus invariant is
determined by~$\kappa$ alone.

A single bosonic field $\alpha$ of conformal weight~$1$.  The OPE is
\[
\alpha(z)\,\alpha(w)
\;\sim\;
\frac{k}{(z-w)^2}.
\]
No simple pole: the singularity is purely of order~$2$.  The mode
algebra is the Heisenberg Lie algebra
$[\alpha_m,\alpha_n]=km\,\delta_{m+n,0}$, and the vertex algebra
$\mathcal H_k$ is the vacuum module at level~$k\neq 0$.  Central
charge $c=1$.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Bar complex.}
The augmentation ideal
$\bar{\mathcal H}_k=\mathcal H_k/\mathbb C\cdot\mathbf{1}$ is
spanned by normally ordered monomials in~$\alpha$ and its
derivatives.  The bar construction is the tensor coalgebra on the
desuspension:
\[
\barB(\mathcal H_k)
\;=\;
T^c\!\bigl(s^{-1}\bar{\mathcal H}_k\bigr),
\qquad
d_{\barB}\bigl(s^{-1}a_1|\cdots|s^{-1}a_n\bigr)
\;=\;
\sum_{i<j}\pm\,
s^{-1}a_1|\cdots|s^{-1}\operatorname{Res}_{z_i=z_j}
\bigl(a_i(z_i)\,a_j(z_j)\,\eta_{ij}\bigr)|\cdots|s^{-1}a_n.
\]
Because the only singularity is a double pole (producing a scalar),
$d_{\barB}$ acts by contraction: it pairs two tensor factors and
replaces them by a scalar.  Explicitly:
\begin{align*}
d_{\barB}(s^{-1}\alpha) &= 0,\\
d_{\barB}(s^{-1}\alpha|s^{-1}\alpha) &=
  k\cdot s^{-1}\mathbf{1} = 0 \quad
  \text{(in the reduced complex)},\\
d_{\barB}(s^{-1}\partial^m\alpha|s^{-1}\partial^n\alpha) &=
  k\binom{m+n+1}{m}\cdot s^{-1}\mathbf{1} = 0 \quad (m+n\ge 1).
\end{align*}
Bar cohomology concentrates:
\[
H^1\bigl(\barB(\mathcal H_k)\bigr) = \mathbb C\cdot\alpha^*,
\qquad
H^n\bigl(\barB(\mathcal H_k)\bigr) = 0 \;\;\text{for}\;\; n\ge 2.
\]
PBW concentration: bar cohomology is one-dimensional in degree~$1$.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Koszul dual.}
The bar cohomology $\cA^{\mathrm i}=H^*(\barB(\mathcal H_k))$
is a one-dimensional graded coalgebra concentrated in degree~$1$.
Taking graded linear duals gives the Koszul dual algebra:
\[
\mathcal H_k^!
\;:=\;
\bigl(\cA^{\mathrm i}\bigr)^\vee
\;=\;
\bigl(\operatorname{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^*),\;m_0=-k\omega\bigr),
\]
where $V^*=\mathbb C\cdot\alpha^*$ is the dual generator space and
$m_0=-k\omega$ is the curvature: a curving element, not a
differential.  The curved $A_\infty$-relation reads
$m_1^2(a)=[m_0,a]$ (commutator, with sign).  The Koszul dual of
Heisenberg is \emph{not} Heisenberg: $\mathcal H_k^!$ is a
\emph{curved} symmetric algebra, while $\mathcal H_k$ is a
\emph{flat} vertex algebra.  Chiral
Koszul duality is not an involution but a Verdier-type reflection.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Shadow obstruction tower.}
The OPE has no simple pole: $\alpha_{(0)}\alpha=0$.
Every transferred operation beyond arity~$2$ vanishes,
so the only stable graphs contributing
to~\eqref{eq:pref-theta} have all vertices of valence~$2$;
stability forces $g(v)\ge 1$ at each bivalent vertex.
Since the only nonvanishing OPE coefficient is the scalar~$k$
and the desuspended generator $s^{-1}\eta$ has odd degree,
the parity argument
(Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic})
forces the graph sum to collapse:
\[
\Theta_{\mathcal H_k}
\;=\;
k\cdot\eta\otimes\Lambda,
\]
where $\eta=d\log(z_1-z_2)$ is the propagator on
$\operatorname{FM}_2(X)$ and
$\Lambda=\lambda_1\in H^2(\overline{\cM}_{1,1})$ is the
generator of $H^*(\overline{\cM}_{1,1})$.
The five-component differential collapses completely:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item $d_{\mathrm{Ch}_\infty}=0$: no higher transferred operations,
\item $d_{\mathrm{coll}}=0$: collisions produce scalars only,
\item $d_{\mathrm{pf}}=0$: no planted-forest contributions,
\item only $d_{\check C}+d_{\mathrm{loop}}$ survive.
\end{itemize}
Cubic shadow: $\mathfrak{C}(\mathcal H_k)=0$.  Quartic contact
shadow: $Q^{\mathrm{contact}}(\mathcal H_k)=0$.  All higher
obstructions vanish.  Shadow depth~$2$.  Gaussian archetype.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Modular characteristic and complementarity.}
\[
\kappa(\mathcal H_k) = k,
\qquad
\kappa(\mathcal H_k^!) = -k,
\qquad
\kappa(\mathcal H_k)+\kappa(\mathcal H_k^!) = 0.
\]
A single scalar $\kappa(\cH_k)=k$ determines every
projection: the generating function is
$\sum_{g\ge 1}F_g\,x^{2g}=k\bigl(\frac{x/2}{\sin(x/2)}-1\bigr)
= k\bigl(\hat A(ix)-1\bigr)$,
giving $F_1=k/24$, $F_2=7k/5760$, $F_3=31k/967680$, \ldots
(the Taylor coefficients of the $\hat{A}$-genus).
At genus~$g$, $Q_g(\mathcal H_k)$ is a polynomial of degree~$2g$
in~$k$, computed entirely from iterated loop contractions of the
single propagator~$\eta$.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Genus-two shell profile.}
Only the loop$\circ$loop shell contributes:
\[
\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{loop}\circ\mathrm{loop}}\neq 0,
\qquad
\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{sep}\circ\mathrm{loop}}= 0,
\qquad
\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{pf}}= 0.
\]
Every genus correction reduces to iterated loop contractions of a
single propagator: the Gaussian measure of chiral algebra theory.

% ----- 7.2 Kac-Moody -----
\subsection*{7.2.\quad Affine Kac--Moody}

The Lie/tree archetype: shadow
depth~$3$, the cubic shadow is the Lie bracket, and the Jacobi
identity kills all higher obstructions.  The first family
with a nonabelian bar differential.

Let $\mathfrak g$ be a simple Lie algebra of rank~$\ell$,
dimension~$d=\dim\mathfrak g$, dual Coxeter number~$h^\vee$,
with structure constants $f^{ab}{}_c$ and normalised Killing
form~$\kappa^{ab}$.  The affine vertex algebra
$\widehat{\mathfrak g}_k$ has generators $J^a$,
$a=1,\dots,d$, of conformal weight~$1$, with OPE
\[
J^a(z)\,J^b(w)
\;\sim\;
\frac{f^{ab}{}_c\,J^c(w)}{z-w}
\;+\;
\frac{k\,\kappa^{ab}}{(z-w)^2}.
\]
Both pole orders are present.  The simple pole carries the Lie
bracket; the double pole carries the invariant inner product at
level~$k$.  The mode algebra is the affine Lie algebra
$\widehat{\mathfrak g}$:
\[
[J^a_m,J^b_n]
\;=\;
f^{ab}{}_c\,J^c_{m+n}
\;+\;
km\,\kappa^{ab}\,\delta_{m+n,0}.
\]

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Bar complex.}
The simple-pole residue contributes a bracket component
to~$d_{\barB}$:
\[
d_{\barB}(s^{-1}J^a|s^{-1}J^b)
\;=\;
f^{ab}{}_c\,s^{-1}J^c
\;+\;
k\,\kappa^{ab}\cdot(\text{curvature term}).
\]
The bracket component is the Chevalley--Eilenberg differential of
$L\mathfrak g$; the curvature component is the central
extension by~$k$.  The identity $d_{\barB}^2=0$ requires the
\emph{Borcherds identity}, not Jacobi: the $n$-fold residue relations from all pole orders
simultaneously, replacing $[d,[d,-]]=0$.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{PBW spectral sequence.}
Filter $\barB(\widehat{\mathfrak g}_k)$ by conformal weight.  The
spectral sequence $E_1^{p,q}(g)$ at genus~$g$ has $E_1$ page given
by the bar cohomology of the associated graded, a free-field
computation in the Heisenberg algebra
$\mathcal H_k^{\otimes d}$.  PBW concentration at all genera is
proved: $E_\infty^{p,q}(g)=0$ for $q\neq 0$.  The enriched
genus-$g$ $E_1$ page carries the structure of a free resolution of the
diagonal $\widehat{\mathfrak g}_k$-bimodule, with the Hodge
bundle~$\mathbb E$ supplying the curvature twist at each genus.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Sugawara construction.}
At non-critical level $k\neq -h^\vee$, the stress tensor is
\[
T(z)
\;=\;
\frac{1}{2(k+h^\vee)}
\sum_{a=1}^{d}{:}J^a(z)J^a(z){:}\,,
\qquad
c
\;=\;
\frac{k\,\dim\mathfrak g}{k+h^\vee}.
\]
The Sugawara field is composite, not in the generating set.  At
$k=-h^\vee$, the construction is
\emph{undefined} ($c$ does not exist, not ``$c$ diverges'').  The Feigin--Frenkel
center $\mathfrak z(\widehat{\mathfrak g}_{-h^\vee})\cong
\operatorname{Fun}(\operatorname{Op}_{{}^L\fg}(D))$
is a commutative vertex algebra of ${}^L\mathfrak g$-opers on the formal disk.  At critical level, the bar
complex is flat but noncommutative.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Shadow obstruction tower.}
The cubic shadow is the Lie bracket itself:
\[
\mathfrak C(\widehat{\mathfrak g}_k)
\;=\;
\bigl[f_{abc}\,J^a\otimes J^b\otimes J^c\bigr]
\;\in\;
H^1(F^3\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{mod}}/F^4\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{mod}},\,d_2).
\]
The quartic obstruction $o^{(4)}(\widehat{\mathfrak g}_k)=0$: the
Jacobi identity on~$\mathfrak g$ kills the only candidate quartic
cocycle via $f^{ab}{}_e f^{ec}{}_d+\text{cyclic}=0$.  The quintic
obstruction vanishes by the same mechanism.  Shadow depth~$3$.
Lie/tree archetype.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Modular characteristic and complementarity.}
\[
\kappa(\widehat{\mathfrak g}_k)
\;=\;
\frac{(k+h^\vee)\dim\mathfrak g}{2h^\vee},
\qquad
\kappa(\widehat{\mathfrak g}_k^!)
\;=\;
-\frac{(k+h^\vee)\dim\mathfrak g}{2h^\vee}.
\]
Complementarity: $\kappa(\widehat{\mathfrak g}_k)+
\kappa(\widehat{\mathfrak g}_k^!)=0$ for all $k\neq -h^\vee$.
The Feigin--Frenkel involution
\[
k\;\longleftrightarrow\; -k-2h^\vee
\]
is Koszul duality in the modular sense: the level of the dual algebra
is the Langlands dual level.  The complementarity sum $c(k)+c(-k-2h^\vee)=2\dim\mathfrak g$
becomes the complementarity relation evaluated on this family.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Genus-two shell profile.}
At genus~$2$, the loop$\circ$loop and sep$\circ$loop shells both
contribute:
\[
\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{loop}\circ\mathrm{loop}}\neq 0,
\qquad
\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{sep}\circ\mathrm{loop}}\neq 0,
\qquad
\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{pf}}= 0.
\]
The planted-forest shell vanishes because the quartic shadow is zero
and planted forests require arity~$\ge 4$.  Separating degeneration
activates through the cubic shadow (the Lie bracket) composed with
the loop contraction: the genus-two correction factors through
$\mathfrak g \otimes \mathfrak g \xrightarrow{[-,-]}
\mathfrak g \xrightarrow{\mathrm{loop}} \mathbb C$.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Special feature: Feigin--Frenkel at critical level.}
At $k=-h^\vee$, the vertex algebra
$\widehat{\mathfrak g}_{-h^\vee}$ has a large center.
The center $\mathfrak z(\widehat{\mathfrak g}_{-h^\vee})
\cong \operatorname{Fun}(\operatorname{Op}_{{}^L\mathfrak g}(D))$
is the ring of opers on the formal disk for the Langlands dual.  The
bar complex at critical level is \emph{flat} ($m_0^{(1)}=0$): the
modular characteristic $\kappa(-h^\vee)=0$.  Critical-level chiral
Koszul duality is the geometric Langlands correspondence at the
level of the bar construction.


% ----- 7.3 Virasoro -----
\subsection*{7.3.\quad Virasoro}

The mixed archetype: shadow depth infinity,
the tower never terminates, and new invariants appear at every arity.
The self-coupling $T_{(1)}T = 2T$ drives all nonlinear
complexity.

One generator~$T$ of conformal weight~$2$.  The OPE is
\[
T(z)\,T(w)
\;\sim\;
\frac{c/2}{(z-w)^4}
\;+\;
\frac{2\,T(w)}{(z-w)^2}
\;+\;
\frac{\partial T(w)}{z-w}.
\]
Three pole orders: the fourth-order pole carries~$c$;
the second-order pole carries $T_{(1)}T=2T$; the simple pole
carries~$\partial T$.  The mode algebra:
\[
[L_m,L_n]
\;=\;
(m-n)L_{m+n}
\;+\;
\frac{c}{12}(m^3-m)\,\delta_{m+n,0}.
\]

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Bar complex.}
The bar differential on the Virasoro vacuum module has three components:
\begin{align*}
d_{\barB}(s^{-1}T|s^{-1}T)
&=
2\,s^{-1}T + \frac{c}{2}\cdot(\text{curvature})
\quad\text{(from $(z-w)^{-2}$ and $(z-w)^{-4}$ poles)},\\
d_{\barB}(s^{-1}T|s^{-1}\partial T)
&=
s^{-1}\partial T + 3\,s^{-1}T
\quad\text{(from $(z-w)^{-1}$ and $(z-w)^{-2}$ poles)}.
\end{align*}
At higher tensor degree, the bar differential on
$s^{-1}T|s^{-1}T|s^{-1}T$ produces terms involving the
self-coupling $T_{(1)}T=2T$ composed with itself, the first
instance of a bar differential that is genuinely quadratic in the
structure constants.  PBW concentration still holds: at every
genus~$g$, the spectral sequence collapses to $E_\infty^{p,0}$.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Koszul dual.}
\[
\operatorname{Vir}_c^!
\;=\;
\operatorname{Vir}_{26-c}.
\]
The duality is an involution on the one-parameter Virasoro family.
The fixed point is $c=13$, \emph{not}~$c=26$.  Self-duality:
$\operatorname{Vir}_c \cong \operatorname{Vir}_c^!$ iff $c=13$.
The central charge~$26$ plays no special role in Koszul duality; its
appearance in string theory is the vanishing of
$\kappa(\operatorname{Vir}_{26})=13$,
$\kappa(\operatorname{Vir}_{26}^!)=\kappa(\operatorname{Vir}_0)=0$: the
\emph{anomaly-cancellation} condition, not the self-duality condition.

The same-family shadow $\operatorname{Vir}_{26-c}$ is the
depth-zero resonance shadow: the image of the finite-dimensional
resonance truncation $R_{\mathrm{Vir}}$, not the final Koszul dual in
the completed sense.  The genuine $\mathcal W_\infty$-type dual
requires the full resonance-filtered completion.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Shadow obstruction tower.}
The cubic shadow is determined by the self-coupling $T_{(1)}T=2T$:
\[
\mathfrak{C}_{\mathrm{Vir}} \;\neq\; 0.
\]
The quartic contact shadow, extracted from the four-point collision
residue on $\overline{C}_4(\mathbb P^1)$, is
\[
Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{Vir}}
\;=\;
\frac{10}{c(5c+22)}.
\]
The poles at $c=0$ and $c=-22/5$ reflect the degeneration of the
Virasoro vacuum module: at $c=0$ the identity representation
degenerates, and at $c=-22/5$ the $(2,5)$ minimal model forces the
vacuum Verma module to acquire a singular vector at weight~$4$.

The quintic obstruction is the Poisson bracket in the shadow algebra:
\[
o^{(5)}_{\mathrm{Vir}}
\;=\;
\bigl\{C_{\mathrm{Vir}},\,
Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{Vir}}\bigr\}_H
\;=\;
\frac{480}{c^2(5c+22)}\,x^5
\;\neq\; 0.
\]
Since $o^{(5)}\neq 0$, no finite truncation captures the
Virasoro algebra.  Shadow depth~$\infty$.  Mixed archetype.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Modular characteristic and complementarity.}
\[
\kappa(\operatorname{Vir}_c) = \frac{c}{2},
\qquad
\kappa(\operatorname{Vir}_{26-c}) = \frac{26-c}{2} = 13 - \frac{c}{2},
\qquad
\kappa(\operatorname{Vir}_c)+\kappa(\operatorname{Vir}_c^!)
= 13.
\]
This is the unique standard family where complementarity gives a
\emph{nonzero} constant: $\kappa+\kappa^!=13$ rather than~$0$.  The
constant~$13$ is half the critical dimension~$26$, and its
nonvanishing reflects that $\operatorname{Vir}$ is a
one-generator algebra whose bar complex has nontrivial
self-coupling: the curvature of the dual cannot cancel the curvature
of the algebra when both live in the same one-dimensional family.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Higher-genus corrections.}
At genus~$1$, the shadow obstruction tower produces corrections beyond the
linear curvature.  The genus-$1$ Hessian correction:
\[
\delta H^{(1)}_{\mathrm{Vir}}
\;=\;
\frac{120}{c^2(5c+22)}\cdot x^2.
\]
The loop ratio:
\[
\rho^{(1)}_{\mathrm{Vir}}
\;=\;
\frac{240}{c^3(5c+22)}.
\]
The Hessian correction $\delta H^{(1)}$ is the genus-$1$ quadratic
deviation from the linearised curvature; the loop
ratio~$\rho^{(1)}$ is the ratio of the quadratic correction
to~$\kappa^2$.  Both are determined by the quartic contact shadow
and are not determined by~$\kappa=c/2$: they are the
first nonlinear genus-$1$ invariants, visible only because the shadow
tower has depth~$\ge 4$.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Genus-two shell profile.}
All three primitive shells contribute:
\[
\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{loop}\circ\mathrm{loop}}\neq 0,
\qquad
\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{sep}\circ\mathrm{loop}}\neq 0,
\qquad
\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{pf}}\neq 0.
\]
The loop$\circ$loop shell comes from iterated curvature; the
sep$\circ$loop shell from mixed clutching; and the planted-forest
shell from the quartic contact channel~$Q^{\mathrm{contact}}$.  The
Virasoro algebra is the simplest family in which the planted-forest
shell is nonzero, the first family that sees the log-FM boundary
strata of $\overline{\mathcal M}_{2,n}$.



\medskip

\noindent\textbf{The critical dimension.}\enspace
\[
\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}}_c
\;=\;
d
\;-\;\frac{c}{2}\,\omega_g
\;-\;\frac{10}{c(5c+22)}\,\delta_4
\;-\;\frac{120}{c^2(5c+22)}\,\delta_H
\;-\;\cdots\,.
\]
The connection is flat for every~$c$ by the MC equation.
The critical dimension $c=26$ arises from the \emph{dual}
curvature vanishing:
\[
\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c})\;=\;\frac{26-c}{2}\;=\;0
\qquad\Longrightarrow\qquad
\boxed{\;c\;=\;26\;}.
\]
At $c=26$ the Koszul dual
$\mathrm{Vir}_{26}^!=\mathrm{Vir}_0$ is \emph{uncurved}:
the dual bar complex is a genuine cochain complex.
The quartic contact correction evaluates to
$\mathfrak Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{26}
=10/(26\cdot 152)=5/1976$.
The algebra itself retains curvature $\kappa=13$; it is
the depth-zero resonance shadow $\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$
at $c=26$ that is trivial.
The holographic datum $\mathcal H(\mathrm{Vir}_{26})$
has unobstructed dual; this is the string-theoretic content
of the critical dimension.

The Polyakov formula (\cite{Pol87}) for a single scalar on a
surface~$\Sigma$ with conformal factor~$\sigma$ ($g_1=e^{2\sigma}g_0$) is
\[
\log\frac{\det'\!\Delta_{g_1}}{\det'\!\Delta_{g_0}}
\;=\;
-\frac{1}{6\pi}\int_\Sigma
\bigl(|\nabla\sigma|^2+R_{g_0}\,\sigma\bigr)\,d\mu_{g_0}.
\]
This is the arity-$2$ shadow evaluation at $\kappa=1$: for
general~$\kappa$, on the proved uniform-weight scalar lane (Definition~\ref{def:scalar-lane}) the
minimal shadow satisfies
$\Theta^{\min}_\cA=\kappa\cdot\eta\otimes\Lambda$
evaluates against~$\sigma$ to give
$\langle\Theta^{\min},\sigma\rangle
=-(\kappa/6\pi)\int(|\nabla\sigma|^2+R\sigma)\,d\mu$,
reproducing the conformal anomaly with coefficient~$\kappa/(6\pi)$.
The higher-arity corrections $\delta_4,\delta_H,\ldots$ displayed
in the shadow connection above are inaccessible to the free-field
path integral: they require the shadow obstruction tower.
For uniform-weight algebras, the genus expansion is controlled
by the $\hat{A}$-genus:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ahat-universality-preface}
\textstyle
F_g(\cA) \;=\; \kappa(\cA)\cdot\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}},
\qquad
\sum_{g\geq 1} F_g\,x^{2g}
\;=\;
\kappa\bigl(\hat{A}(ix) - 1\bigr)
\;=\;
\kappa\Bigl(\frac{x/2}{\sin(x/2)} - 1\Bigr).
\end{equation}
The Taylor coefficients $\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$ are the
Faber--Pandharipande evaluations of the Hodge class: $\lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}} = 1/24$,
$\lambda_2^{\mathrm{FP}} = 7/5760$,
$\lambda_3^{\mathrm{FP}} = 31/967680$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:universal-generating-function}).
The series converges:
$|F_g|\sim 2|\kappa|/(2\pi)^{2g}$
(exponential decay), in contrast to the bosonic string where
$F_g\sim(2g{-}2)!$ from the noncompactness of~$\mathbf{R}^d$.
The critical dimension is the zero of the dual curvature
$\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c})=(26-c)/2$.

% ----- 7.4 W_3 -----
\subsection*{7.4.\quad $\boldsymbol{\mathcal W_3}$}

The first multi-generator family:
two generators of different conformal weights produce cross-channel
mixing in the genus-$1$ Hessian, a $2\times 2$ spectral
discriminant, and the first multi-channel genus-$2$
amplitude.  Infinite shadow depth, with
propagator mixing as a new structural feature.

Two generators: the stress tensor~$T$ (weight~$2$) and a primary
field~$W$ (weight~$3$).  The $TT$~OPE is Virasoro.  The $TW$~OPE
encodes the primary property:
\[
T(z)\,W(w)
\;\sim\;
\frac{3\,W(w)}{(z-w)^2}
\;+\;
\frac{\partial W(w)}{z-w}.
\]
The $WW$~OPE is the first genuinely nonlinear datum in the standard
landscape:
\begin{align*}
W(z)\,W(w)
\;\sim\;\;
&\frac{c/3}{(z-w)^6}
\;+\;
\frac{2\,T(w)}{(z-w)^4}
\;+\;
\frac{\partial T(w)}{(z-w)^3}\\[4pt]
&+\;
\frac{1}{(z-w)^2}
\biggl[
\frac{16}{22+5c}\,\Lambda(w)
\;+\;
\frac{3}{10}\,\partial^2 T(w)
\biggr]
\;+\;\cdots\,,
\end{align*}
where the composite field
\[
\Lambda
\;=\;
{:}TT{:}\;-\;\tfrac{3}{10}\,\partial^2 T
\]
is the unique quasi-primary of weight~$4$ in the vacuum module.  The
coefficient $-3/10$ is fixed by requiring $T(z)\Lambda(w)$ to have
no third-order pole: quasi-primary projection orthogonal to the
descendant~$\partial^2 T$.  The structure constant
$16/(22+5c)$ governs the $WW\Lambda$ coupling.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The $c=-22/5$ degeneration.}
At $c=-22/5$, the denominator vanishes and $\Lambda$ becomes a null
field.  The vacuum Verma module has a singular vector at weight~$4$:
the Kac determinant vanishes there, and $\mathcal W_3$ is not
finitely generated by $T$ and~$W$ alone.  Infinitely many new
generators are required.  This is the first $\mathcal W$-algebra
where the structure constants have poles in the central charge.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Shadow obstruction tower.}
The cubic shadow inherits the Virasoro self-coupling $T_{(1)}T=2T$
and acquires a contribution from $T_{(1)}W=3W$:
$\mathfrak{C}_{\mathcal W_3}\neq 0$.  The quartic contact channel
is the composition
\[
W\otimes W
\;\xrightarrow{\text{OPE at }(z-w)^{-2}}\;
\Lambda
\;\xrightarrow{\text{OPE of }{:}TT{:}}\;
T\otimes T,
\]
which factors through the quasi-primary projection and then the
Virasoro OPE.  This factorisation is represented in the bar complex
by a planted forest with two leaves and an internal vertex of
weight~$4$: the first time a planted-forest correction appears in the
bar differential.

The quartic contact shadow includes the Virasoro contribution
$Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{Vir}}=10/[c(5c+22)]$ plus an
additional term from the $WW\Lambda$ channel, proportional to
$16/(22+5c)$.  Both are singular at $c=-22/5$: the quartic shadow
detects the vacuum degeneracy.  Shadow depth~$\infty$.  Mixed modular
archetype.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Modular characteristic.}
\[
\kappa(\mathcal W_3)
\;=\;
\frac{5c}{6}\,.
\]
The weight-$2$ generator contributes $c/2$ and the weight-$3$
generator contributes $c/3$, giving
$\kappa=c/2+c/3=5c/6$.  The Koszul dual
$\mathcal W_3^!$ is a $\mathcal W_3$-algebra at the dual central
charge $c'=100-c$ (self-dual at $c=50$); complementarity:
$\kappa(\mathcal W_3{}_c)+\kappa(\mathcal W_3{}_{100-c})=250/3$.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Genus-two shell profile.}
All three shells are active:
$\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{loop}\circ\mathrm{loop}}\neq 0$,
$\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{sep}\circ\mathrm{loop}}\neq 0$,
$\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{pf}}\neq 0$.
The planted-forest shell is sensitive to the $WW\Lambda$ channel:
$\mathcal W_3$ is the first family that is genuinely planted-forest
sensitive, detecting log-FM boundary strata that are invisible to
Heisenberg and affine Kac--Moody.
The genus-$2$ free energy decomposes as
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-genus2-preface}
F_2(\cW_3)
= \underbrace{\frac{7c}{6912}}_{\kappa \cdot \lambda_2^{\mathrm{FP}}}
\;+\;
\underbrace{\frac{c+120}{16c}}_{\delta F_2},
\end{equation}
where $\delta F_2 = (c{+}120)/(16c)$ is the cross-channel
correction from mixed $TW$-propagator graphs, verified by
graph-by-graph recomputation over all seven genus-$2$ stable graphs
(Remark~\ref{rem:w3-genus2-cross-channel}).  This is the first
explicit multi-channel genus-$2$ amplitude;  the scalar part
$\kappa\cdot\lambda_2^{\mathrm{FP}}$ is unconditional, the
cross-channel correction is conditional on
Open Problem~\ref{op:multi-generator-universality}.



\medskip

\noindent\textbf{The $\mathcal W_3$ holographic datum.}\enspace
The deformation space of the modular MC problem is two-dimensional:
deformations along $\partial_c T$ and along $\partial_c W$.
At $c=0$: $\kappa=0$ and the bar complex is uncurved.
The dual curvature vanishes at $c=100$ ($K=c+c'=100$).
The Hessian eigenvalue $\kappa_c=(c-50)/2$ (defined below) governs
the spectral discriminant; its zero at $c=50$ (the FF fixed point)
is the $\mathcal W_3$ self-dual central charge.

The quartic contact shadow is controlled by the quasi-primary
\[
\Lambda\;=\;{:}TT{:}-\tfrac{3}{10}\,\partial^2 T,
\qquad
[\ell_4^{(0)}]
\;=\;
\frac{16}{22+5c}\;\Lambda.
\]
At $c=-22/5$ (the $(2,5)$ minimal model) the quartic diverges;
this is a resonance point of the $\mathcal W_3$ shadow obstruction tower,
shared with Virasoro.

The genus-$1$ tangent map is a $2\times 2$ matrix
\[
H^{(1)}_{\mathcal W_3}
\;=\;
\begin{pmatrix}
\kappa_c & 0 \\[2pt]
0 & \kappa_c + \dfrac{48}{5c+22}
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\kappa_c \;:=\; \frac{c-50}{2}\,,
\]
in the basis $(\partial_c T,\,\partial_c W)$; here $\kappa_c$
is the Hessian eigenvalue, \emph{not} the modular
characteristic $\kappa=5c/6$.  Its determinant
is the spectral discriminant
\[
\Delta_{\mathcal W_3}(x)
\;=\;
\bigl(1-\kappa_c\,x\bigr)
\Bigl(1-\Bigl(\kappa_c+\frac{48}{5c+22}\Bigr)x\Bigr).
\]
The two branch points $x_1=1/\kappa_c$ and
$x_2=(5c+22)/(\kappa_c(5c+22)+48)$ are the reciprocals of the
eigenvalues of the genus-$1$ Hessian.
They coincide at the resonance value
$c=-22/5+48/(5\kappa_c)$, where the two deformation
directions merge.

The holographic datum:
\[
\mathcal H(\mathcal W_3{}_c)
\;=\;
\Bigl(
\mathcal W_3{}_c,\;
\mathcal W_3{}_{100-c},\;
\cC_c^{W_3},\;
r_c^{W_3}(z),\;
\Theta_c,\;
\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}}_c
\Bigr),
\]
with Koszul dual $\mathcal W_3{}_{100-c}$
($\kappa_c+\kappa_{100-c}=250/3$, self-dual at $c = 50$), line-operator category
$\cC_c^{W_3}$ a module category for the dg-shifted $W_3$-Yangian,
and shadow connection
\[
\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}}_c
\;=\;
d
\;-\;\frac{5c}{6}\,\omega_g
\;-\;\frac{16}{22+5c}\,\Lambda\cdot\delta_4
\;-\;\cdots\,.
\]

% ----- 7.5 beta-gamma -----
\subsection*{7.5.\quad $\boldsymbol{\beta\gamma}$ system}

The $\beta\gamma$ system is the contact archetype: the first
nonlinearity appears at arity~$4$ (not~$3$), and a rank-one abelian
rigidity argument kills it, producing shadow depth~$4$.  This is the
unique standard family in which the tower terminates for a structural
reason distinct from Lie-algebraic cancellation.

Two fields: $\beta$ of conformal weight~$\lambda$ and $\gamma$ of
conformal weight~$1-\lambda$.  The OPE is
\[
\beta(z)\,\gamma(w)
\;\sim\;
\frac{1}{z-w},
\qquad
\beta(z)\,\beta(w)\;\sim\;0,
\qquad
\gamma(z)\,\gamma(w)\;\sim\;0.
\]
A simple pole with no double pole: the contact archetype.  Central
charge $c_{\beta\gamma}=3(2\lambda-1)^2-1=12\lambda^2-12\lambda+2$.
At the standard weight $\lambda=1$, $c_{\beta\gamma}=2$
(the fermionic $bc$~ghost system has $c_{bc}=-2$).

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Shadow obstruction tower.}
The cubic shadow on the weight line vanishes: $\ell_3^{(0)}=0$,
because $\beta$ and $\gamma$ carry different conformal weights and the
three-point residue on the diagonal weight sector is zero.  The
quartic operation is nonzero: $\ell_4^{(0)}\neq 0$, from the
four-point function
$\langle\beta\gamma\beta\gamma\rangle$.  This is the defining
property of the contact archetype: the first nonlinearity appears at
arity~$4$, not~$3$.

The quartic contact invariant
$\mu_{\beta\gamma}=\langle\eta,m_3(\eta,\eta,\eta)\rangle=0$ vanishes
by rank-one abelian rigidity: the $\beta\gamma$~system has a
$\mathrm{U}(1)$ ghost-number symmetry, and the cyclic pairing
on the deformation complex vanishes on the arity-$4$ component by
weight considerations.  The quintic obstruction vanishes because the
cubic shadow is zero: $o^{(5)}=\{0,Q\}_H=0$.  Shadow depth~$4$.
Contact/quartic archetype.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Koszul dual.}
The Koszul dual is the $bc$~ghost system: $(\beta\gamma)^!=bc$.
Replacing bosonic statistics by fermionic statistics negates the
central charge: $c_{bc}=-c_{\beta\gamma}$.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Modular characteristic and complementarity.}
\[
\kappa(\beta\gamma)
\;=\;
\frac{c_{\beta\gamma}}{2}
\;=\;
6\lambda^2-6\lambda+1,
\qquad
\kappa(bc) = -\kappa(\beta\gamma),
\qquad
\kappa(\beta\gamma)+\kappa(bc)=0.
\]
At $\lambda=1$: $\kappa(\beta\gamma)=1$,
$\kappa(bc)=-1$.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Genus-two shell profile.}
\[
\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{loop}\circ\mathrm{loop}}\neq 0,
\qquad
\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{sep}\circ\mathrm{loop}}= 0,
\qquad
\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{pf}}= 0.
\]
The sep$\circ$loop shell vanishes because the cubic shadow is zero;
the planted-forest shell vanishes because the contact invariant
$\mu_{\beta\gamma}=0$.  Only iterated curvature contributes at
genus~$2$: the same shell pattern as Heisenberg, but with a different
mechanism (contact termination rather than Gaussian collapse).


% ----- 7.6 Lattice -----
\subsection*{7.6.\quad Lattice vertex algebras}

Lattice vertex algebras are the arithmetic laboratory: the shadow
tower inherits the Gaussian archetype from the Heisenberg factor, but
the braiding carries the full arithmetic of the lattice.  The
curvature sees only the rank; the braiding sees the quadratic form.

Let $\Lambda$ be an even lattice of rank~$N$ with quadratic
form~$q$ and $2$-cocycle~$\varepsilon$.  The lattice vertex algebra
\[
V_\Lambda^{N,q}
\;=\;
\mathcal H_k^{\otimes N}
\;\otimes_{\mathbb C}\;
\mathbb C[\Lambda]_\varepsilon
\]
is the tensor product of the rank-$N$ Heisenberg algebra with the
$\varepsilon$-twisted group algebra of the lattice.  The generators
include the Heisenberg currents $\alpha^i$ ($i=1,\dots,N$) and the
exponential vertex operators $e^{\lambda\cdot\phi}$ for
$\lambda\in\Lambda$.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Modular characteristic.}
\[
\kappa(V_\Lambda^{N,q})
\;=\;
\operatorname{rank}(\Lambda)
\;=\;
N,
\]
independent of the cocycle~$\varepsilon$ and the quadratic form~$q$.
The curvature is determined entirely by the Heisenberg part:
the exponential vertex operators $e^{\lambda\cdot\phi}$ contribute to
the braiding but not to the curvature.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Curvature-braiding orthogonality.}
The modular curvature class
$[\kappa\cdot\omega_g]\in H^{1,1}(\overline{\mathcal M}_g)$ and the
braiding representation
$\pi_1(\operatorname{Conf}_n(X))\to
\operatorname{Aut}(V_\Lambda^{\otimes n})$
act on complementary factors of the state space.  The curvature sees
$\mathcal H^{\otimes N}$; the braiding sees
$\mathbb C[\Lambda]_\varepsilon$.  The two are orthogonal.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Shadow obstruction tower and shells.}
