The shadow obstruction tower inherits the Gaussian archetype from the Heisenberg
factor: shadow depth~$2$.  All cubic and higher obstructions vanish.
Genus-two shell profile: loop$\circ$loop only.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Special cases.}
The $E_8$ lattice: rank~$8$, self-dual, $\kappa=8$.  The Leech
lattice: rank~$24$, self-dual, $\kappa=24$.  For a self-dual lattice,
$V_\Lambda$ is a holomorphic vertex algebra: the modular functor is
trivial, and the partition function is an honest modular form
(the theta function $\Theta_\Lambda(\tau)/\eta(\tau)^N$).

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Non-simply-laced algebras.}\enspace
For the non-simply-laced simple Lie algebras $B_2$, $C_2$, $G_2$,
$F_4$: all are class~L (shadow depth~$3$).  The short-root
correction to the Killing form modifies~$\kappa$ by the
lacing number but does not affect the depth classification.
The Langlands dual pair $(B_N, C_N)$ has $\kappa(B_N) \neq
\kappa(C_N)$ but both are class~L: the lacing distinguishes the
scalar invariant but not the structural type.

% ----- 7.7 Yangians -----
\subsection*{7.7.\quad Yangians and quantum groups}

The Yangian is the line-operator algebra: it governs the topological
direction of a holomorphic-topological theory, and its $R$-matrix is
the genus-$0$ binary shadow of the MC element.  The Yang--Baxter
equation is the arity-$3$ MC equation; the RTT relations encode all
arities.

Fix a simple Lie algebra~$\mathfrak g$ of rank~$\ell$.  The Yangian
$Y(\mathfrak g)$ governs the $E_1$-chiral atom: chiral algebras on
ordered configurations in $\mathbb C\times\mathbb R$, where
$\mathbb C$ carries the holomorphic direction and $\mathbb R$ the
topological direction.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The $R$-matrix as genus-$0$ binary shadow.}
The $R$-matrix
\[
R(z)
\;=\;
1\;+\;\frac{r}{z}\;+\;\frac{r^{(2)}}{z^2}\;+\;\cdots
\;\in\;
Y(\mathfrak g)\otimes Y(\mathfrak g)[[z^{-1}]]
\]
is the genus-$0$ binary shadow of the MC element:
\[
r(z) \;=\; \operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}(\Theta_\cA).
\]
The classical $r$-matrix $r_{\mathrm{cl}}=\Omega/z$ (where
$\Omega=\sum_a J^a\otimes J^a$ is the Casimir tensor) satisfies the
classical Yang--Baxter equation (CYBE):
\[
[r_{12},r_{13}]+[r_{12},r_{23}]+[r_{13},r_{23}] = 0.
\]
This is the Arnold relation on $\operatorname{FM}_3(\mathbb C)$
evaluated on the Casimir: the three terms correspond to the three
boundary divisors of $\overline C_3(\mathbb C)$, and the CYBE is
$d_{\barB}^2=0$ projected to arity~$3$ and genus~$0$.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Type-$A$ MC3 reduction.}
On the type-$A$ Yangian surface, the post-CG problem is reduced to a
single remaining compact/completed extension packet.  The reduction
proceeds via:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\alph*),nosep]
\item \emph{Chromatic filtration.}  Filter
  $K_0(\operatorname{Rep})$ by the support of $q$-characters.  The
  successive quotients are controlled by products of prefundamental
  modules.
\item \emph{Clebsch--Gordan closure.}  The tensor product
  $V_n\otimes L^-=\bigoplus_{j=0}^n L^-(n-2j)$ at character level,
  for all~$n$.  Every Verma character lies in the $K_0$-span of
  $\{[V_n]\cdot[L^-]\}$.
\item \emph{Completion formalism} (more precisely,
  Francis--Gaitsgory pro-nilpotent completion).  Evaluation modules
  are compact, so once an equivalence on the relevant compact core is
  known, it extends to the corresponding ind-completion.  This does
  not by itself supply that compact-core equivalence.
\end{enumerate}
Extension to arbitrary simple type requires the all-types
prefundamental CG package together with the remaining post-CG
extension/completion packets.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The dg-shifted Yangian.}
The modular dg-shifted Yangian
$Y_T^{\mathrm{mod}}=\varprojlim_r Y_T^{\mathrm{mod},\le r}$ is the
pronilpotent completion of the convolution dg Lie algebra associated
to the chiral algebra of a 3d holomorphic-topological theory~$T$.
The modular $R$-matrix
\[
R_T^{\mathrm{mod}}(z;\hbar)
\;\in\;
\operatorname{MC}(Y_T^{\mathrm{mod}})
\]
is an MC element.  The Yang--Baxter equation is the MC equation
projected to arity~$3$; the higher RTT relations
$R_{12}R_{13}R_{23}=R_{23}R_{13}R_{12}$ encode the MC equation
at all arities.  The RTT tower is a pro-system of finite-dimensional
MC equations, and the inverse limit converges by Mittag-Leffler
stabilisation: at each finite truncation, the obstruction group is
finite-dimensional and eventually stationary.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Drinfeld--Kohno.}
The KZ connection on $\operatorname{Conf}_n(\mathbb C)$ with values
in $\mathfrak g^{\otimes n}$ is
\[
\nabla_{\mathrm{KZ}}
\;=\;
d\;-\;\hbar\sum_{i<j}
\Omega_{ij}\,d\log(z_i-z_j).
\]
Its monodromy representation
$\pi_1(\operatorname{Conf}_n(\mathbb C))\to
\operatorname{Aut}(V^{\otimes n})$
is compared by the affine Drinfeld--Kohno theorem with the
corresponding quantum-group representation category.  In the
shadow obstruction tower:
\[
\nabla_{\mathrm{KZ}}
\;=\;
\operatorname{Sh}_{0,n}(\Theta_{\widehat{\mathfrak g}_k}):
\]
on the affine Kac--Moody comparison surface, the KZ connection is
identified with the genus-$0$ shadow connection determined by the
universal MC element.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Shadow obstruction tower.}
The Yangian inherits its shadow structure from the underlying affine
algebra.  At the $E_1$-chiral level, the shadow obstruction tower is controlled
by the $R$-matrix expansion: the arity-$r$ shadow at genus~$0$ is
$r^{(r-1)}/z^{r-1}$, and each coefficient satisfies an RTT-type
constraint.  The genus-$0$ shadow terminates at
depth~$3$ (for class~$\mathbf{L}$ algebras, the CYBE is the full genus-$0$ content at arity~$3$; for class~$\mathbf{M}$, the arity-$3$ MC equation carries strictly more, encoding the homotopy Jacobiator); the modular
extension to genus~$g\ge 1$ requires the completed dg-shifted Yangian
and does not terminate.


\subsection*{7.8.\quad Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction as package morphism}

$\mathrm{DS}\colon\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_3{}_k
\to\mathcal W_3{}_{c(k)}$
with $c(k)=2-24(k+2)^2/(k+3)$ extends to a morphism
\[
\mathrm{DS}\colon
\mathcal H(\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_3{}_k)
\;\longrightarrow\;
\mathcal H(\mathcal W_3{}_{c(k)})
\]
acting on each component:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{lll}
& $\mathcal H(\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_3{}_k)$
  & $\mathrm{DS}(\mathcal H)$ \\
\hline
$\cA$ & $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_3{}_k$
  & $\mathcal W_3{}_{c(k)}$ \\
$\cA^!$ & $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_3{}_{-k-6}$
  & $\mathcal W_3{}_{100-c(k)}$ \\
$r(z)$ & $\Omega_{\mathfrak{sl}_3}/z$
  & $r_c^{W_3}(z)$ \\
$\kappa$ & $4(k+3)/3$
  & $5c(k)/6$ \\
depth & $3$
  & $\infty$ \\
$\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{pf}}$ & $0$
  & $\neq 0$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\smallskip\noindent
The Casimir $r$-matrix $\Omega/z$ specialises to
$r_c^{W_3}(z)$.  The curvature shifts.  The shadow depth
jumps from $3$ to~$\infty$: DS reduction creates the
planted-forest shell.  The off-diagonal $TW$-mixing in the
genus-$1$ Hessian is the image of the $\mathfrak{sl}_3$ root
structure.  At the critical level $k=-3$:
$\kappa\to 0$ on the affine side (curvature vanishes),
$c\to\infty$ on the $\mathcal W_3$ side (Sugawara pole).

The DS-HPL transfer theorem
(Volume~II, Theorem~thm:ds-hpl-transfer) makes the
chain-level mechanism precise: homological perturbation through
the SDR of the BRST complex transfers the affine dg-shifted
Yangian triple $(m, r, \Delta)$ to the $\mathcal{W}$-algebra side.
The $\Ainf$ products transfer nontrivially (the quartic pole forces
infinite arity), and the $r$-matrix transfers with the expected
pole-order shift.  The coproduct, however, is annihilated: a
ghost-number obstruction kills every HPL tree correction,
so $\Delta_z^{\mathcal{W}} = 0$ at all arities
(Principle~\ref{princ:gravitational-primitivity}).
DS reduction is therefore a functor on modular Koszul triples
(Construction~\ref{constr:ds-functor-triples}), and all
gravitational dynamics resides in the $r$-matrix, not in
coproduct vertices.

\subsection*{Central charge additivity under DS}

The ghost central charge is $k$-independent:
$c_{\mathrm{ghost}} = c(\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_3{}_k) - c(\mathcal W_3{}_{c(k)})
= 8k/(k{+}3) - (2 - 24/(k{+}3)) = 6 = 2|\Delta^+(\mathfrak{sl}_3)|$.
The modular characteristics involve different anomaly
ratios: $\kappa(\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_3{}_k) = 4(k{+}3)/3$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality}),
$\kappa(\mathcal W_3{}_{c(k)}) = 5c(k)/6$, and the deficit
$\kappa_{\mathrm{aff}} - \kappa_{W_3}$ is a rational function
of~$k$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:partition-dependent-complementarity}).
The DS morphism of holographic data is compatible with
the genus expansion at every genus simultaneously, by
functoriality of the graph-sum~\eqref{eq:pref-theta} under DS.

\subsection*{7.9.\quad The geometric localization principle}

The algebraic functoriality above has a geometric substrate.
Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction is not merely an algebraic
construction: it is \emph{Hamiltonian reduction from
$J_\infty(\mathfrak{g}^*)$ to $J_\infty(S_f)$}, where
$S_f = f + \mathfrak{g}^e$ is the Slodowy transverse slice
to the nilpotent orbit of~$f$
(here $\mathfrak{g}^e$ is the centralizer of the nilpotent
element~$e$ in an $\mathfrak{sl}_2$-triple $(e,h,f)$;
Definition~\ref{def:slodowy-slice}).

The Slodowy slice is the universal transverse section through a
nilpotent orbit: it meets every orbit transversally, carries a
Poisson structure from the Kirillov--Kostant bracket, and its
quantization is the finite $W$-algebra
(Gan--Ginzburg~\cite{GanGinzburg02},
Premet~\cite{Premet02}).  The affine/chiral upgrade replaces
$S_f$ by its arc space $J_\infty(S_f)$ (the space of
formal arcs, i.e.\ $\mathbb{C}[\![t]\!]$-points of~$S_f$), and
$\operatorname{gr}_F \mathcal{W}^k(\mathfrak{g},f)
\cong \mathbb{C}[J_\infty(S_f)]$
(Remark~\ref{rem:jet-slodowy}).  In this reading:
\begin{itemize}
\item The PBW--Slodowy collapse
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:w-pbw-slodowy-collapse}) is the algebraic
  expression of \emph{smoothness of the Slodowy slice}
  (Remark~\ref{rem:pbw-slodowy-master-square}).
\item For $\mathcal{W}$-algebras, the shadow depth jump
  $3 \to \infty$ under DS records the \emph{nonlinearity of
  the Dirac bracket} on the arc space $J_\infty(S_f)$: the
  Hamiltonian reduction from the linear Kirillov--Kostant bracket
  on $J_\infty(\mathfrak{g}^*)$ to the nonlinear Dirac bracket
  on $J_\infty(S_f)$ creates the infinite shadow obstruction tower
  (Remark~\ref{rem:ds-depth-increase-geometric}).
\item Barbasch--Vogan orbit duality
  $f \leftrightarrow f^D$, through which the Koszul dual
  orbit is identified, is \emph{Springer duality of Slodowy slices}:
  the curvature complementarity
  $\kappa(\mathcal{W}^k) + \kappa(\mathcal{W}^{k'}) = \mathrm{const}$
  is an algebraic identity under the Feigin--Frenkel involution
  $k + h^\vee \mapsto -(k + h^\vee)$
  (Remark~\ref{rem:bv-springer-duality}).
\item The master commutative square
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:master-commutative-square}) encodes all of
  this: bar complexes on the upper row, Hamiltonian reduction on
  arc spaces on the lower row, PBW identification on the vertical
  arrows.
\end{itemize}


% ====================================================================
\section*{8.\quad The arithmetic of the shadow obstruction tower}
% ====================================================================

The shadow obstruction tower coefficients for the standard families are rational
functions of the central charge.  Their denominators, zeros, and
growth rates carry arithmetic information connecting the shadow
calculus to $L$-functions.  What number-theoretic structures does the MC
equation force?

\subsection*{The Dirichlet--sewing lift}

The genus-$1$ free energy $F_1^{\mathrm{conn}}(\cA;q)
=-\log\det(1-K_q)$, where $K_q$ is the sewing kernel
on $\overline{\cM}_{1,1}$, encodes connected sewing
amplitudes $a_\cA(N)$ as Fourier coefficients.  The
\emph{Dirichlet--sewing lift}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:preface-dirichlet-sewing}
S_\cA(u)
\;:=\;
\sum_{N=1}^\infty a_\cA(N)\,N^{-u}
\;=\;
\frac{(2\pi)^u}{\Gamma(u)}\int_0^\infty
F_\cA^{\mathrm{conn}}(e^{-2\pi y})\,y^{u-1}\,dy
\end{equation}
is a Dirichlet series whose analytic structure is controlled
by the shadow obstruction tower $\Theta_\cA$.  The sewing amplitudes define
an inner product
$\langle f,g\rangle_\cA=\sum_N a_\cA(N)\,f(N)\,g(N)$
on Dirichlet polynomials.  The reproducing kernel
$K_\cA(s,t)=S_\cA(s{+}t)$ is the
\emph{sewing reproducing kernel}, and the surface moment matrix
$\mathscr M_{ij}=K_\cA(\alpha/2{+}i,\,\alpha/2{+}j)$
is positive definite for all $\alpha\geq 2$:
it is a Gram matrix $V^T\!DV$ with Vandermonde~$V$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:gram-positivity}).

Explicit values:
\[
\begin{aligned}
S_{\cH}(u)&=\zeta(u)\,\zeta(u{+}1),\\
S_{V_k(\fg)}(u)&=\dim(\fg)\cdot\zeta(u)\,\zeta(u{+}1),\\
S_{\mathrm{Vir}}(u)&=\zeta(u{+}1)\bigl(\zeta(u)-1\bigr),\\
S_{\mathcal W_N}(u)&=\zeta(u{+}1)\Bigl((N{-}1)\zeta(u)
  -\textstyle\sum_{j=1}^{N-1}H_j(u)\Bigr),
\end{aligned}
\]
where $H_j(u)=\sum_{n=1}^j n^{-u}$ are partial harmonic sums.
The Heisenberg lift is a product of two Riemann zeta functions;
the Virasoro lift subtracts the first Fourier coefficient from
$\zeta$; the $\mathcal W_N$ lifts interpolate via a harmonic sum
that stabilises as $N\to\infty$.

\subsection*{The three-tier Euler--Koszul classification}

The \emph{Euler defect}
$D_\cA(u):=S_\cA(u)\big/(|W(\cA)|\,\zeta(u)\,\zeta(u{+}1))$
classifies chiral algebras into three tiers:
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{lll}
\textbf{Tier} & \textbf{Condition} & \textbf{Families} \\ \hline
Exact Euler--Koszul & $D_\cA(u)\equiv 1$
  & $\cH$, $V_k(\fg)$, $\beta\gamma$ \\[2pt]
Finitely defective & $1-D_\cA(u)$ is a finite harmonic ratio
  & Virasoro, $\mathcal W_N$ \\[2pt]
Non-Euler--Koszul & $S_\cA$ decomposes into Hecke $L$-functions
  & lattice VOAs with $h(D)\geq 2$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The Euler--Koszul class $\mathrm{ek}(\cA)=\max_i(w_i-1)$
and the shadow depth $r_{\max}(\cA)$ are independent invariants
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-euler-independence}):
the first reads the character, the second the OPE.  The two
axes of difficulty, arithmetic (how the coefficients grow)
and algebraic (how the OPE interacts), are logically
independent.

\subsection*{The two-variable $L$-object}

The Rankin--Selberg unfolding against the Eisenstein series
$E^*(\tau,s)$ produces
\begin{equation}\label{eq:preface-two-variable-L}
L_\cA(s,u)
\;:=\;
\int_{\cF}^{\mathrm{reg}}
F_\cA^{\mathrm{conn}}(\tau)\,E^*(\tau,s)\,y^{u-2}\,dx\,dy.
\end{equation}
The \emph{sewing--Hecke reciprocity theorem} collapses the
two variables to one:
$L_\cA(s,u)=\frac{\Gamma(v)}{(2\pi)^v}\,S_\cA(v)$
with $v:=s+u-1$.  Special cases:
the Dirichlet slice $L_\cA(1,u)=\frac{\Gamma(u)}{(2\pi)^u}S_\cA(u)$;
the Selberg slice
$L_\cA(s,0)=\frac{\Gamma(s{-}1)}{(2\pi)^{s-1}}S_\cA(s{-}1)$.
The scattering poles of the Eisenstein series at
$s=\rho/2$ (for nontrivial zeros~$\rho$ of~$\zeta$)
are \emph{not} poles of~$L_\cA$: the Rankin--Selberg
unfolding is holomorphic at these points
(Proposition~\ref{prop:scattering-residue}).
The nontrivial zeros enter as a structural obstruction
to the Euler product, not as poles of the $L$-object.

\subsection*{The shadow-moduli resolution}

The shadow obstruction tower enters the arithmetic through the
\emph{shadow-moduli map} $t\colon\mathfrak H\to\mathbb C$,
solving
\[
\prod_j(1-\lambda_j\,t(q))^{c_j}
\;=\;
\det(1-K_q^{\mathrm{conn}}),
\]
where $\lambda_j$ are the spectral atoms and $c_j$ their
multiplicities.  The connected free energy factors as
$F_1^{\mathrm{conn}}(q;\cA)=G_\cA(t(q))$ with
\[
G_\cA(t)=\int\log(1-\lambda\,t)\,d\rho_\cA(\lambda),
\]
a function determined by the spectral measure~$\rho_\cA$ alone
(Theorem~\ref{thm:universality-of-G}).
The shadow obstruction tower enters as follows: expanding
$G_\cA(t)=-\sum_{r\geq 1}\frac{\mu_r}{r}\,t^r$, the
moments $\mu_r=\int\lambda^r\,d\rho_\cA$ are determined
by the MC equation arity by arity.  At arity~$r{+}1$:
\[
\mu_{r+1}
\;=\;
(r{+}1)\,\operatorname{Br}_{r+1}(\mu_2,\mu_3,\ldots,\mu_r;\cA),
\]
where $\operatorname{Br}_{r+1}$ is a universal polynomial
in the lower moments and the structure constants of~$\cA$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:mc-bracket-determines-atoms}).  For two
Satake-type atoms $\lambda_1=\alpha$, $\lambda_2=\beta$, this
yields, via the Newton relations, a formal spectral polynomial:
the power sums $p_r=e_1\,p_{r-1}-e_2\,p_{r-2}$ encode the MC
recursion in spectral coordinates.

\subsection*{The interacting Gram matrix}

The shadow obstruction tower provides interacting corrections to the
Gram positivity.  The \emph{interacting sewing weight}
\[
w_\cA(N;\alpha)
\;:=\;
a_\cA(N)\cdot\prod_j(1-\lambda_j\,N^{-\alpha/2})^{c_j}
\]
is unconditionally positive when all spectral atoms
$\lambda_j$ are negative
(Theorem~\ref{thm:interacting-gram-positivity}(i)).  The
interacting Gram matrix
$\mathscr M_{ij}^{\mathrm{int}}
=\sum_N w_\cA(N;\alpha)\,N^{-\alpha/2-i}\,N^{-\alpha/2-j}
\succ 0$
in this case.
For Virasoro with $c > 0$: $\lambda_{\mathrm{eff}} = -6/c < 0$,
so positivity holds for all $\alpha \geq 2$ unconditionally
(Corollary~\ref{cor:virasoro-interacting-gram}).
The resonance locus $\mathcal{R}$ is empty for $c > 0$
and confined to the non-unitary regime $c < 0$, with the
Lee--Yang point $c = -22/5$ as the first entry
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-resonance-locus}).

\subsection*{The Weil analogy}

The structural parallel between the MC equation and the Weil
conjectures for curves over finite fields organises the
arithmetic programme:
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{ll}
\textbf{Weil proof for $C/\mathbb F_q$}
  & \textbf{MC equation for~$\cA$} \\ \hline
Curve $C/\mathbb F_q$
  & chirally Koszul algebra $\cA$ \\[2pt]
Frobenius $\mathrm{Frob}_q$
  & MC element $\Theta_\cA=D_\cA-d_0$ \\[2pt]
$\mathrm{Frob}^2=q$ (functional equation)
  & $D_\cA^2=0$ (nilpotence) \\[2pt]
\'Etale cohomology $H^i_{\text{\'et}}$
  & cyclic deformation complex $\Defcyc(\cA)$ \\[2pt]
Weight filtration $W_\bullet$
  & arity filtration $\Theta_\cA^{\leq r}$ \\[2pt]
Eigenvalues $\alpha_i$ on $H^1$
  & spectral atoms $\lambda_j$ of~$\rho_\cA$ \\[2pt]
$\|\alpha_i\|=q^{1/2}$ (Riemann hypothesis)
  & $|a_{f_j}(p)|\leq 2p^{(k-1)/2}$ (Ramanujan) \\[2pt]
Lefschetz operator $L$
  & bracket with $\kappa(\cA)$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
For even unimodular lattice vertex algebras $V_\Lambda$
with theta series $\Theta_\Lambda
=c_E\,E_{r/2}+\sum_j c_j f_j$ (cusp forms~$f_j$),
the Hecke--Newton closure
(Theorem~\ref{thm:hecke-newton-lattice}) gives the chain:
MC equation $\Rightarrow$ prime-local CG closure
$\Rightarrow$ CPS automorphy $\Rightarrow$
$\operatorname{Sym}^{r-1}(f)$ identification
$\Rightarrow$ Ramanujan bound.
The endpoint recovers the Ramanujan bound for
lattice VOAs
(Corollary~\ref{cor:unconditional-lattice}).
The MC equation supplies the Hecke decomposition and
CPS automorphy; the Ramanujan bound itself follows from
Deligne's theorem on Hecke eigenvalues of cusp
forms~\cite{Deligne1974}, an external input, not
reproved here.  The contribution of the MC framework is
the systematic derivation of the Hecke decomposition
from chiral bar-cobar data, not an independent proof
of the bound.

\subsection*{The Polyakov--bar-cobar dictionary}

The shadow obstruction tower proves Polyakov's worldsheet functional-integral
programme~\cite{Pol87} algebraically:
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{ll}
\textbf{Polyakov object}
  & \textbf{Bar-cobar counterpart} \\ \hline
Conformal anomaly $\langle T^a{}_a\rangle=(c/12)R$
  & modular characteristic $\kappa(\cA)$ \\[2pt]
Functional determinant $\det'_\zeta\Delta$
  & Fredholm $\det(1-K)$ on Bergman kernel \\[2pt]
Critical dimension $c=26$
  & dual characteristic $\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c})=0$ \\[2pt]
Ghost system $bc$ ($c_{\mathrm{ghost}}=-26$)
  & Koszul dual $\cA^!$ (BRST pairing, not literal) \\[2pt]
Genus expansion $Z=\sum_g g_s^{2g-2}Z_g$
  & MC5 sewing, $F_g=\kappa\cdot\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$ (uniform weight) \\[2pt]
BPZ equations (Virasoro degenerate-module surface)
  & shadow connection $\nabla^{\mathrm{sh}}$ on that comparison surface \\[2pt]
Instanton sectors
  & Novikov-completed bar $B^\Lambda(\cA)$ \\[2pt]
Wilson line $\langle W(C)\rangle$
  & Swiss-cheese boundary module
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The anomaly, the genus expansion, the duality, the critical
dimension, and the non-perturbative completions all descend from
$\Theta_\cA\in\mathrm{MC}(\gAmod)$.  The four shadow depth
classes (Gaussian, Lie, contact, mixed) correspond to increasing
levels of departure from the Gaussian path integral.

The Polyakov dictionary identifies the shadow obstruction tower with the
worldsheet programme at the level of individual objects.  The
following construction upgrades this identification to a connection
on the space of Hecke eigenvalues, providing a differential-geometric
framework for the prime-by-prime structure of the sewing amplitudes.

\subsection*{The arithmetic packet connection}

The Hecke operators $T_p$ ($p$ prime) act on
the space of graph amplitudes
$\ell_\Gamma^{(g)}(\cA)$
through their action on modular forms.
Let $M_\cA$ be the $\bC$-span of the activated amplitudes,
and decompose $M_\cA = \bigoplus_\chi M_\chi$ into
generalised Hecke eigenspaces: on~$M_\chi$, the operator
$T_p$ acts by a scalar $a_\chi(p)$ plus a nilpotent part
$N_\chi$ (the Jordan block defect).  To each eigenspace
attach its \emph{packet function}, the completed
$L$-function of the corresponding eigenform:
for an Eisenstein eigenspace, $\Lambda_0(s) =
C_0(s)\,\zeta(s)\,\zeta(s{-}r/2{+}1)$;
for a cusp eigenspace attached to a normalised eigenform
$f_j$, $\Lambda_j(s) = C_j(s)\,L(s,f_j)$.

The \emph{arithmetic packet connection}
(Definition~\ref{def:arithmetic-packet-connection}) is the
flat meromorphic connection
\[
\nabla_\cA^{\mathrm{arith}}
\;:=\;
d \;-\; \bigoplus_\chi
\frac{\Lambda_\chi'(s)}{\Lambda_\chi(s)}
\bigl(\mathrm{id}_{M_\chi}+N_\chi\bigr)\,ds
\]
on the trivial bundle $M_\cA \otimes \cO_\bC$ over
the spectral line $s \in \bC$.  Flatness is immediate:
on each block, the connection form is a scalar $1$-form
times a constant endomorphism, so both $dA_\chi$ and
$A_\chi \wedge A_\chi$ vanish for degree reasons
(Theorem~\ref{thm:packet-connection-flatness}).
The singular divisor
$D_\cA = \bigcup_\chi \operatorname{div}(\Lambda_\chi)$
is the zero-and-pole set of the packet functions; it
depends only on the semisimple quotient
$M_\cA^{\mathrm{ss}}$ (the \emph{arithmetic skeleton}),
not on the nilpotent parts~$N_\chi$.  The nilpotent
parts produce only unipotent local monodromy
$\exp(2\pi i\,\operatorname{ord}_\rho(\Lambda_\chi)\,
N_\chi)$ around each component of~$D_\cA$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:packet-connection-flatness}(iii)).

The completed Eisenstein scattering function on
$\cM_{1,1}$ is
$\varphi(s) := \Lambda^*(1{-}s)/\Lambda^*(s)$,
where $\Lambda^*(s) = \pi^{-s}\Gamma(s)\zeta(2s)$.
Write $\Lambda_{\mathrm{Eis}}(s) := \Lambda_0(s)$
for the Eisenstein packet.  The \emph{frontier defect
form}
(Definition~\ref{def:frontier-defect-form})
\[
\Omega_\cA
\;:=\;
d\log\Lambda_{\mathrm{Eis}}(s)
\;-\;
d\log\varphi(s)
\]
vanishes iff the Eisenstein block of
$\nabla^{\mathrm{arith}}$ is gauge-equivalent to the
scattering connection $d - d\log\varphi(s)$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:gauge-criterion-scattering};
the additional condition $N_{\mathrm{Eis}} = 0$ is needed
for the gauge to be scalar).
For even unimodular lattice VOAs at rank~$r$:
$\Lambda_{\mathrm{Eis}}(s) = C_0(s)\,\zeta(s)\,\zeta(s{-}r/2{+}1)$,
while $\varphi(s)$ involves $\zeta(2s)/\zeta(2s{-}1)$;
since $\zeta(s)$ and $\zeta(2s)$ have different zero
sets, $\Omega_{V_\Lambda} \neq 0$ in general.

The packet connection treats each algebra uniformly.  For
$\mathcal W_N$ algebras, the DS reduction from affine Kac--Moody
provides additional structure: the Miura transformation splits the
$\mathcal W_N$ character into a Heisenberg core and a finite
correction, isolating all arithmetic content beyond Heisenberg in a
finite product.

\subsection*{The finite Miura defect}

For principal $\cW_N$ with generators of spins
$2,3,\ldots,N$, the $\cW_N$ character is
$\chi_{\cW_N}(q) = \prod_{n \geq 2}
(1 - q^n)^{-\min(n-1,\,N-1)}$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:wn-character-primitive}).
The Heisenberg character is
$\chi_\cH(q) = \prod_{n \geq 1}(1 - q^n)^{-1}$.
The ratio is a finite product
(Theorem~\ref{thm:finite-miura-defect}):
\[
\chi_{\cW_N}(q)
\;=\;
\chi_\cH(q)^{N-1}
\cdot\prod_{m=1}^{N-1}(1-q^m)^{N-m},
\]
since the exponent $(N{-}1) - \min(n{-}1,N{-}1)$
vanishes for $n \geq N$ and equals $N{-}n$ for
$2 \leq n \leq N{-}1$.  The finite product is the
\emph{Miura defect}; all genus-$1$ arithmetic content
in~$\cW_N$ beyond Heisenberg is carried by it.
At the Dirichlet level:
$D_{\cW_N}^{\mathrm{prime}}(u)
= -\zeta(u{+}1)\sum_{m=1}^{N-1}(N{-}m)\,m^{-u}$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:prime-side-defect-formula}).
The packet connection of~$\cW_N$ splits as
$(N{-}1)$ copies of the diagonal Heisenberg connection
$d - d\log[\zeta(s)\zeta(s{+}1)]\,ds$
plus a defect connection governing modes
$m = 1,\ldots,N{-}1$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:miura-packet-splitting}).
The Heisenberg copies contribute only the universal
divisor $\operatorname{div}(\zeta(s))
\cup \operatorname{div}(\zeta(s{+}1))$, and their
contribution to $\Omega_{\cW_N}$ cancels: the frontier
defect form is determined by the defect alone.

The constructions above produce proved arithmetic invariants from the
MC element.  The final programme of this section reverses the
direction: it asks what constraints the nontrivial zeros of
$L$-functions impose on the MC data, through the quartic shadow.

\subsection*{The quartic closure programme}

The quartic resonance class
$\mathfrak{R}_{4,g,n}^{\mathrm{mod}}(\cA)$, the first
nonlinear shadow of~$\Theta_\cA$ (arity~$4$ projection
of the MC element), satisfies a proved clutching law
along every separating boundary stratum
$\xi\colon \overline{\cM}_{g_1,n_1+1} \times
\overline{\cM}_{g_2,n_2+1} \to \overline{\cM}_{g,n}$:
\[
\xi^*\mathfrak{R}_{4,g,n}^{\mathrm{mod}}
\;=\;
p_1^*\mathfrak{R}_{4,g_1,n_1+1}^{\mathrm{mod}}
\;+\;
p_2^*\mathfrak{R}_{4,g_2,n_2+1}^{\mathrm{mod}}
\;+\;
\mathfrak{T}_{3,\xi}
\]
(Theorem~\ref{thm:nms-clutching-law-modular-resonance}).
The $3\times 3$ Schur complement of the mixed
$(s,u)$-transform extracts the quartic contact coupling
$Q_v^{\mathrm{ct}}$ on the potential side and its
reciprocal $(Q_v^{\mathrm{ct}})^{-1}$ on the Gram side
(Theorem~\ref{thm:schur-complement-quartic}).
For Virasoro:
$\Sigma_2^{\mathrm{Vir}} = 10/[c(5c{+}22)]$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:virasoro-quartic-determinant}).

Three closure conjectures form a strict hierarchy
(each implies all predecessors):
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item \emph{quartic closure}
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:quartic-closure}):
  the intersection of quartic Gram-compatibility loci
  over all families, slices, and regulators is
  $\{\rho : \operatorname{Re}(\rho) = 1/2\}$;
\item \emph{Beilinson closure}
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:beilinson-closure}):
  the global discrepancy functional $\cB^{\mathrm{glob}}(\rho)$
  vanishes iff $\operatorname{Re}(\rho) = 1/2$;
\item \emph{clutching closure}
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:clutching-closure}):
  the residue clutching defect $K_{\cA,\rho,\xi}$
  (Definition~\ref{def:residue-clutching-defect})
  vanishes for all families and all boundary strata
  iff $\operatorname{Re}(\rho) = 1/2$.
\end{enumerate}
The chain of constructions:
$\Theta_\cA$ (proved, Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic})
$\to$ residue kernel $w_{c,\rho,u_0}$
(proved, Proposition~\ref{prop:on-off-line-distinction})
$\to$ residue Gram matrix
(Definition~\ref{def:genuine-residue-moment-matrix})
$\to$ Schur complement
(proved, Theorem~\ref{thm:schur-complement-quartic})
$\to$ quartic resonance divisor
(proved, Theorem~\ref{thm:nms-clutching-law-modular-resonance})
$\to$ residue clutching defect
(Definition~\ref{def:residue-clutching-defect})
$\to$ closure conjecture \textup{(conjectural)}.

For lattice vertex algebras, the arithmetic programme has a concrete
incarnation: the bar complex selects a sublattice, and the Epstein
zeta function restricted to that sublattice recovers the Riemann zeta
in the simplest case.

\subsection*{The constrained Epstein zeta}

For a lattice vertex algebra $V_\Lambda$ of rank~$r$,
the \emph{constrained Epstein zeta function}
\[
\varepsilon^c_s(V_\Lambda)
\;:=\;
\sideset{}{'}\sum_{\ell\in\Lambda^{\mathrm{bar}}}
\|\ell\|^{-2s}
\]
restricts the Epstein series to the sublattice
$\Lambda^{\mathrm{bar}}\subset\Lambda$ determined by
the bar complex: the summation runs over those lattice
vectors that contribute nontrivially to the bar
differential.  For the rank-$1$ lattice $V_{\bZ}$
at self-dual radius $R=1$, every nonzero integer
contributes, giving
\[
\varepsilon^1_s(R{=}1) \;=\; 4\,\zeta(2s):
\]
the constrained Epstein zeta of the simplest lattice
VOA \emph{is} the Riemann zeta function (up to the
elementary factor~$4$).

The Hecke operators decompose the constrained series into
$L$-functions:
\[
\varepsilon^r_s(V_\Lambda)
\;=\;
\sum_j c_j\,L(s,\chi_j)
\]
where the sum runs over the Hecke characters~$\chi_j$ of
$\Lambda$ activated by the bar sublattice.  Shadow
depth~$d$ contributes $d-1$ critical lines to the
meromorphic continuation of~$\varepsilon^r_s$, one for
each arity stratum of the shadow obstruction tower beyond the
Gaussian base.  The nontrivial zeros of the
component $L$-functions are the scattering resonances of
the hyperbolic Laplacian on $\cM_{1,1}=\mathrm{SL}(2,\bZ)\backslash\mathfrak H$:
they are the frequencies at which the genus-$1$ sewing
amplitude of~$V_\Lambda$ fails to decay.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The B\"ocherer bridge (genus~$2$).}\enspace
At genus~$2$, the shadow tautological class for lattice vertex
algebras computes a central $L$-value via the B\"ocherer conjecture
(Furusawa--Morimoto).  For the Leech lattice $V_\Lambda$ with
$\Lambda = \Lambda_{24}$: the Siegel modular form
$\chi_{12} = \mathrm{SK}(f_{22})$ is the Saito--Kurokawa lift of the
unique weight-$22$ cuspidal eigenform, and the MC-derived second
Fourier coefficient $c_2 \approx -1.918 \times 10^{-6} \neq 0$ is
the first nonzero central $L$-value produced by the shadow obstruction tower,
connecting the MC element $\Theta_\cA$ to the arithmetic of
Siegel modular forms at genus~$2$.

\section*{9.\quad Scalar saturation and the Koszulness programme}
% ====================================================================

The bar construction works for all chiral algebras.  But it works
\emph{best} (the cobar inverts the bar, the spectral sequence
collapses, the resolution is linear) precisely on the Koszul locus.
Characterizing this locus is the central foundational question.  Two
complementary results: scalar saturation (the MC element is determined by a single scalar for
all standard families) and the Koszulness meta-theorem (twelve characterizations, ten unconditionally equivalent, one conditional
on perfectness, one one-directional).

\subsection*{9.1.\quad Scalar saturation}

For a one-parameter algebraic family~$\cA_k$ with rational OPE
coefficients (meaning the structure constants are rational functions
of the level~$k$), the universal MC element satisfies:
\[
\Theta_{\cA_k}
\;=\;
\kappa(\cA_k)\cdot\eta_{\mathrm{univ}}\otimes\Lambda_{\mathrm{univ}}
\;+\;
(\text{terms in $F^3\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{mod}}_{\cA_k}$}).
\]
\emph{Scalar saturation universality}: the higher-order terms vanish.
For every algebraic family with rational OPE coefficients,
$\Theta_{\cA_k}$ is determined by the single scalar
$\kappa(\cA_k)$ modulo terms in the arity-$\ge 3$ filtration.

The proof proceeds in two steps.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Step 1: Whitehead reduction.}
For a vertex algebra~$\cA_k$ with reductive symmetry at generic~$k$,
the primitive cyclic cohomology
$H^2_{\mathrm{cyc,prim}}(\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{mod}}/F^3,\,d_2)$ is
computed by a Whitehead-type spectral sequence.  The $E_2$ page is
\[
E_2^{p,q}
\;=\;
H^p\!\bigl(\mathfrak g;\,
\operatorname{Sym}^q V\bigr),
\]
the Lie algebra cohomology of the symmetry algebra acting on the
conformal-weight filtration.  For reductive~$\mathfrak g$ and generic
level, $H^2(\mathfrak g;\operatorname{Sym}^q V)=0$ by the Whitehead
lemma (vanishing of $H^2$ for finite-dimensional semisimple Lie
algebras acting on finite-dimensional modules).  The arity-$2$ MC
class therefore lifts uniquely to the full complex.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Step 2: Algebraic semicontinuity.}
The vanishing locus
\[
E \;=\; \bigl\{k\in\mathbb C :
  H^2_{\mathrm{cyc,prim}}(\cA_k)\neq 0\bigr\}
\]
is Zariski-closed in the parameter space (upper semicontinuity of
cohomology dimension as a constructible function).  At the free-field
point $k=\infty$, the algebra is Heisenberg and
$H^2_{\mathrm{cyc,prim}}=0$.  Therefore $E$ is a proper
Zariski-closed subset.  Explicit computation verifies $E=\varnothing$
for $\mathfrak{sl}_N$ ($N=2,\dots,10$): no exceptional level exists.
The result covers the entire standard Lie-theoretic landscape at all
non-critical levels, including admissible ones.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Scope.}
Scalar saturation applies to every family in the standard landscape:
affine Kac--Moody (all types, all non-critical levels),
Virasoro (all~$c$), $\mathcal W_N$ (all~$N$, all non-degenerate
levels), $\beta\gamma$ and lattice algebras (all parameters).  The
residual conjecture, that $E=\varnothing$ for \emph{every}
positive-energy chiral algebra with rational OPE coefficients, is
open only for non-algebraic-family constructions (no known counterexample).


\subsection*{9.2.\quad The Koszulness meta-theorem}

The Koszul condition admits twelve formulations,
spanning homological algebra (PBW collapse, Ext vanishing),
homotopy theory ($A_\infty$ formality, $E_2$ formality),
operadic algebra (Barr--Beck--Lurie comparison, FM boundary
acyclicity), modular geometry (FH concentration, tropical
Koszulness), and symplectic topology (Lagrangian criterion).
Ten of these are unconditionally equivalent; one (the Lagrangian
criterion) is conditional on perfectness/nondegeneracy; and one
($\mathcal{D}$-module purity) is one-directional (forward direction
proved, converse open).

The PBW criterion detects Koszulness for every standard family
but does not characterize it intrinsically.
Theorem~\ref{thm:koszul-equivalences-meta}: ten conditions on~$\cA$ are
mutually equivalent, with one conditional on
perfectness and one partial implication.

\medskip
\begin{center}
\emph{For $\cA$ positive-energy and finitely strongly generated,
the following are equivalent:}
\end{center}

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item $\cA$ is chirally Koszul (Definition~\ref{def:chiral-koszul-morphism}).
\item The PBW spectral sequence on $\barB^{(g)}(\cA)$
  collapses at~$E_2$ for every~$g$.
\item The minimal $A_\infty$-model of $H^\bullet(\barB(\cA))$
  is formal: $m_n = 0$ for $n \geq 3$.
\item $\operatorname{Ext}^{p,q}_\cA(\omega_X, \omega_X) = 0$
  for $p \neq q$ (Ext diagonal vanishing).
\item The bar-cobar counit
  $\Omega(\barB(\cA)) \to \cA$ is a quasi-isomorphism.
\item The Barr--Beck--Lurie comparison for $\barB \dashv \Omega$
  is an equivalence.
\item $\textstyle\int_X \cA$ is concentrated in degree~$0$
  for every smooth proper~$X$.
\item $\mathrm{ChirHoch}^*(\cA)$ vanishes outside degrees
  $\{0,1,2\}$.
\item The Kac--Shapovalov determinant $\det G_h \neq 0$
  in the bar-relevant range.
\item The restriction $i_S^!\,\barB_n(\cA)$ to every FM boundary
  stratum~$S$ is acyclic outside degree~$0$.
\end{enumerate}

\noindent
Under the additional hypothesis that the ambient tangent complex
is perfect and nondegenerate:

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep,start=11]
\item $\mathcal M_\cA$ and $\mathcal M_{\cA^!}$ are transverse
  Lagrangians in the $(-1)$-shifted symplectic deformation
  space $\mathcal M_{\mathrm{comp}}$ (Lagrangian criterion).
\end{enumerate}

\noindent
Finally, (xii)~$\Rightarrow$~(x), where:

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep,start=12]
\item Each $\barB_n(\cA)$ is pure of weight~$n$ as a mixed Hodge
  module, with characteristic variety aligned to FM boundary strata
  ($\mathcal{D}$-module purity).
\end{enumerate}

\noindent
The converse of~(xii) is open.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The proof circuit.}
The core equivalence chain is
$\textup{(i)} \Leftrightarrow \textup{(ii)}
\Leftrightarrow \textup{(iii)}
\Leftrightarrow \textup{(v)}
\Leftrightarrow \textup{(viii)}$,
proved by PBW concentration~$\to$ bar-cobar inversion~$\to$ Hochschild
polynomial growth~$\to$ Koszul-complex acyclicity, with the $A_\infty$
formality branch via HPL transfer and Keller classicality.  From this
core, the remaining equivalences follow:
(iv) by Ext spectral sequence,
(vi) by conservativity + log-FM totalization,
(vii) by $\barB = \int_X$,
(ix) by non-degeneracy forcing PBW injectivity,
(x) by stratum-by-stratum PBW concentration.
The Lagrangian criterion~(xi) uses PTVV derived intersection theory
on the perfectness hypothesis.  The $\mathcal{D}$-module purity
implication (xii)$\Rightarrow$(x) uses weight filtration on the bar
complex; the converse would require concentration to force purity.
The cycle closes via
(viii)$\Rightarrow$(i): Koszul-complex acyclicity implies the
defining characterization, completing the equivalence.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Beyond the meta-theorem.}
Six additional characterizations are proved in the text, complementing
but not contained in items~(i)--(xii):

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)},nosep]
\item \emph{Shadow-formality at low arity.}
  The shadow obstruction tower
  $\Theta^{\le r}_\cA$ equals the $L_\infty$-formality obstruction
  tower of $\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{mod}}_\cA$ at arities $r=2,3,4$
  (Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow-formality-low-arity}).
  At arities $2,3,4$, the shadow obstruction tower \emph{is} the formality
  obstruction tower; full equivalence to~(iii) requires all arities.

\item \emph{$E_2$-formality of chiral Hochschild cohomology.}
  Koszulness implies $\mathrm{ChirHoch}^*(\cA)$ is formal as an
  $E_2$-algebra (Deligne conjecture applied to the bar-cobar
  resolution).  A consequence of~(v), not an independent equivalence.

\item \emph{Genus-$0$ curve independence.}
  Koszulness on~$\mathbb P^1$ implies Koszulness on every smooth
  proper curve
  (Proposition~\ref{prop:genus0-curve-independence}).
  Proved independently by factorization descent.

\item \emph{PBW universality} (sufficient condition).
  Every freely strongly generated vertex algebra is chirally Koszul
  (Proposition~\ref{prop:pbw-universality}; this applies to the
  universal algebra; Koszulness of simple quotients at admissible
  levels is open).
  In particular, $V_k(\mathfrak g)$ is Koszul at \emph{every}
  level~$k$, including critical and admissible.
  This is one-directional: not every Koszul algebra is freely
  strongly generated.

\item \emph{Tropical Koszulness.}
  $\cA$ is chirally Koszul iff $\barB^{\mathrm{trop}}(\cA)$ is
  acyclic (Theorem~\ref{thm:tropical-koszulness}).
  Proved by the weight spectral sequence on the real blowup.

\item \emph{Bifunctor obstruction decomposition} (one-directional).
  Koszulness implies the RNW one-slot obstruction decomposes into
  independent bar-side and cobar-side components
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:bifunctor-obstruction-decomposition}).
  The converse is open.
\end{enumerate}

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Status summary.}
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{clll}
\multicolumn{4}{l}{\emph{Meta-theorem
  \textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:koszul-equivalences-meta}\textup{)}:}}\\[2pt]
& (i)--(x) & \textbf{10 unconditional equivalences} & proved\\
& (xi) Lagrangian & conditional on perfectness & proved
  (unconditional for standard landscape,
  Proposition~\ref{prop:lagrangian-perfectness})\\
& (xii) $\mathcal{D}$-module purity & (xii)$\Rightarrow$(x) only
  & converse open\\[4pt]
\multicolumn{4}{l}{\emph{Additional characterizations:}}\\[2pt]
& (a) Shadow-formality & equivalence at arities $2,3,4$ & proved\\
& (b) $E_2$-formality & consequence of Koszulness & proved\\
& (c) Curve independence & independent theorem & proved\\
& (d) PBW universality & sufficient condition & proved\\
& (e) Tropical Koszulness & equivalence & proved\\
& (f) Bifunctor decomposition & one-directional & converse open
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\subsection*{9.3.\quad Shadow depth and operadic complexity}

The four depth classes G/L/C/M of \S6.5 admit a refinement.
In general, $r_{\max}$ can take any value in
$\{2,3,4,5,\ldots\}\cup\{\infty\}$: the class $\mathbf{F}_r$
(tower terminates at arity~$r$) is structurally permitted for
all $r \geq 2$, with $\mathbf{G}=\mathbf{F}_2$,
$\mathbf{L}=\mathbf{F}_3$, $\mathbf{C}=\mathbf{F}_4$ naming the
standard-landscape representatives.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The operadic complexity theorem.}
The \emph{operadic complexity theorem}
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{conj:operadic-complexity-detailed}}\textup{)}
asserts:
\[
r_{\max}(\cA)
\;=\;
A_\infty\text{-depth}(\cA)
\;=\;
L_\infty\text{-formality level}
(\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{mod}}_\cA).
\]
Here $A_\infty$-depth is the minimal~$r$ such that the transferred
$A_\infty$-structure on $H^\bullet(\barB(\cA))$ has $m_k=0$ for all
$k>r$; and $L_\infty$-formality level is the minimal~$r$ such that
the $L_\infty$-structure on $\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{mod}}_\cA$ is
formal through arity~$r$.

The identification has three consequences:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),nosep]
\item The shadow obstruction tower \emph{is} the $L_\infty$-formality obstruction
  tower: $\Theta^{\le r}_\cA$ encodes precisely the obstruction to
  $L_\infty$-formality through arity~$r$.
\item The depth classification ($\mathbf{F}_r$ / $\mathbf{M}$)
  becomes a structural invariant of the operadic type of~$\cA$:
  $\mathbf{F}_2$ = free, $\mathbf{F}_3$ = Lie,
  $\mathbf{F}_4$ = quadratic non-Lie, higher $\mathbf{F}_r$ = higher
  non-Lie, $\mathbf{M}$ = genuinely nonlinear.
\item The shadow obstruction tower of a Gaussian algebra is a quadratic form; of a
  Lie algebra, a Chevalley--Eilenberg complex; of a contact algebra, a
  cyclic $A_\infty$-structure; of a mixed algebra, an infinite
  $L_\infty$-tower with no polynomial truncation.
\end{enumerate}


\subsection*{9.4.\quad The PBW spectral sequence}

The computational engine for bar cohomology within each fixed genus
is the PBW (Poincar\'e--Birkhoff--Witt) spectral sequence.  Filter
$\barB^{(g)}(\cA)$ by the \emph{conformal weight}: assign to each
normally ordered monomial in the strong generators its total weight
(the sum of the conformal weights of the constituent fields).  The
associated graded is the bar complex of a free-field algebra, a
computation that reduces to combinatorics of symmetric functions.

The $E_1$ page at genus~$g$ decomposes:
\[
E_1^{p,q}(g)
\;=\;
E_1^{p,q}(g{=}0)
\;\oplus\;
\cE^{p,q}_g,
\]
where the first summand is the genus-$0$ bar cohomology (determined
by Koszulness of the associated graded) and $\cE^{p,q}_g$ is the
genus-$g$ enrichment from the Hodge bundle.  The enrichment at
genus~$g$ arises from the regular Eisenstein series coupled to the
curvature.

\emph{Concentration}: $E_\infty^{p,q}(g)=0$ for $q\neq 0$ at all
genera $g\ge 1$, for all standard families
(Kac--Moody, Virasoro, principal $\mathcal W_N$).  This is PBW
degeneration: the spectral sequence collapses at~$E_2$, and the
bar cohomology is concentrated on the diagonal.

The PBW spectral sequence is \emph{not} the genus spectral sequence
of section~5.5.  The PBW spectral sequence uses conformal weight
within a fixed genus to compute the bar cohomology groups; the genus
spectral sequence uses the genus filtration on the deformation
algebra to control the Maurer--Cartan lift across genera.  One
computes \emph{what}; the other determines \emph{whether}.


\subsection*{9.5.\quad Chiral Hochschild cohomology (Theorem~H)}

The chiral Hochschild complex $\mathrm{ChirHoch}^\bullet(\cA)$ is
the derived endomorphism algebra of the identity functor on
$\cA$-modules, computed by the bar construction with
$\cA$-bimodule coefficients.  At genus~$0$:
\[
\mathrm{ChirHoch}^\bullet(\cA)
\;\simeq\;
R\!\operatorname{Hom}_{\cA\text{-bimod}}(\cA,\cA)
\;\simeq\;
\operatorname{Ext}^\bullet_{\cA^e}(\cA,\cA),
\]
where $\cA^e=\cA\otimes\cA^{\mathrm{op}}$ is the enveloping
chiral algebra.

For $\cA=\mathcal W^k(\mathfrak g,f_{\mathrm{prin}})$ a principal
$\mathcal W$-algebra at generic level:
\[
\mathrm{ChirHoch}^*(\mathcal W^k(\mathfrak g))
\;\cong\;
\mathbb{C}[\Theta_1,\dots,\Theta_r],
\qquad
\deg\Theta_i = m_i+1,
\]
where $m_1,\dots,m_r$ are the exponents of~$\mathfrak g$
and $r = \operatorname{rank}(\mathfrak g)$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:w-algebra-hochschild}).
For $\mathfrak g=\mathfrak{sl}_2$:
$\mathrm{ChirHoch}^*(\mathrm{Vir}_c)=
\mathbb{C}[\Theta]$ with $\deg\Theta=2$
(one polynomial generator, $2$-periodic).
For $\mathfrak g=\mathfrak{sl}_3$:
$\mathrm{ChirHoch}^*(\mathcal W_3)=
\mathbb{C}[\Theta_1,\Theta_2]$ with
generators in degrees $2$ and~$3$.

On the Koszul locus, $\mathrm{ChirHoch}^\bullet(\cA)$ carries an
$E_2$-algebra structure that is formal.  The Connes periodicity
operator $S\colon\mathrm{ChirHoch}^n\to\mathrm{ChirHoch}^{n-2}$
intertwines Koszul duality:
$S\circ\mathrm{KD}=\mathrm{KD}\circ S$.

At genus~$0$, the chiral Hochschild complex identifies with the bulk
chiral homology complex of Volume~II: $\mathrm{ChirHoch}^\bullet(\cA)
\simeq\mathrm{ChirHoch}^\bullet_{\mathrm{bulk}}(\cA)$.
The bulk-boundary-line triangle of section~9.6 is the genus-$0$
shadow of this identification:
$\cA_{\mathrm{bulk}}\simeq Z_{\mathrm{der}}(\cB_\partial)
\simeq\mathrm{ChirHoch}^\bullet(\cA^!)$.


\subsection*{9.6.\quad The shadow algebra}

The \emph{shadow algebra} $\cA^{\mathrm{sh}}$ is the cohomology of
the modular cyclic deformation complex as a graded-commutative ring:
\[
\cA^{\mathrm{sh}}
\;:=\;
H_\bullet\!\bigl(\Defcyc^{\mathrm{mod}}(\cA)\bigr),
\qquad
\cA^{\mathrm{sh}}=\bigoplus_{r\ge 2,\,g\ge 0}
\cA^{\mathrm{sh}}_{r,g}.
\]
The single MC element $\Theta_\cA$ decomposes into components
graded by arity~$r$ and genus~$g$.  Each named shadow is a
projection:
\begin{align*}
\kappa(\cA) &= \cA^{\mathrm{sh}}_{2,0},\\
\mathfrak C(\cA) &= \cA^{\mathrm{sh}}_{3,0},\\
\mathfrak Q(\cA) &= \cA^{\mathrm{sh}}_{4,0},\\
\mathrm{Sh}_r(\cA) &= \cA^{\mathrm{sh}}_{r,0},\qquad r\ge 5.
\end{align*}
The shadow algebra organises the entire hierarchy.  It is a
homotopy invariant of~$\cA$, computed by the Weil homomorphism of
the Chern--Weil dictionary (section~5.4).

The all-arity master equation, read in the shadow algebra, becomes:
$\nabla_H(\mathrm{Sh}_r)+o^{(r)}=0$ for all $r\ge 3$.  The
obstruction class $o^{(r)}$ lies in $\cA^{\mathrm{sh}}_{r,0}$ and
measures the failure of the truncation $\Theta^{\le r-1}_\cA$ to
extend to arity~$r$.


\subsection*{9.7.\quad BV/BRST identification at genus~$0$}

At genus~$0$, the bar differential of a chiral algebra on
$\mathbb C$ is the BRST differential of the associated
holomorphic twist:
\[
(d_{\barB})_{g=0}
\;=\;
Q_{\mathrm{BRST}}.
\]
The bar complex $\barB^{(0)}_{\mathbb C}(\cA)$ is the BRST complex
of the 2d chiral algebra, and bar-cobar inversion
$\Omega(\barB(\cA))\xrightarrow{\sim}\cA$ (Theorem~B) is the
statement that the BRST cohomology, processed through the cobar
functor, reconstructs the original algebra.

At genus~$1$, the identification acquires curvature:
\[
d^2_{\mathrm{fib}}
\;=\;
\kappa(\cA)\cdot\omega_1
\;=\;
\text{one-loop anomaly},
\]
and the curved bar complex is the curved BRST complex of the
theory on an elliptic curve.  The complementarity
$Q_1(\cA)\oplus Q_1(\cA^!)=H^*(\overline{\cM}_{1,1},\cZ_\cA)$
is the genus-$1$ anomaly cancellation condition.

At genus~$g\ge 2$, the identification with the Costello--Gwilliam
BV formalism requires renormalisation: the higher-loop integrals
over $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$ need regularisation beyond the
algebraic bar-cobar framework, and the correct receptacle is the
coderived category.

The shadow obstruction tower equals the $L_\infty$-formality obstruction
tower at all arities
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-formality-identification}).

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Genus-two shell activation as depth diagnostic.}
The genus-two shell profile independently confirms the depth
classification:

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{lccc}
& $\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{loop}^2}$
& $\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{sep}\circ\mathrm{loop}}$
& $\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{pf}}$\\
\hline
\textbf{G} (Heisenberg, lattice) & $\checkmark$ & --- & ---\\
\textbf{L} (affine $\widehat{\mathfrak g}_k$) & $\checkmark$
  & $\checkmark$ & ---\\
\textbf{C} ($\beta\gamma$) & $\checkmark$ & --- & ---\\
\textbf{M} (Virasoro, $\mathcal W_N$) & $\checkmark$
  & $\checkmark$ & $\checkmark$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent
Gaussian and contact algebras activate only the loop$\circ$loop shell;
Lie/tree algebras add the sep$\circ$loop shell; only mixed algebras
activate all three shells including the planted-forest shell.  The
planted-forest shell is the diagnostic: its presence forces infinite
shadow depth.
% ====================================================================
\section*{10.\quad The open/closed world (Volume II)}
% ====================================================================

The bar complex lives naturally in three dimensions.  On the product
$\mathbb C_z \times \mathbb R_t$, the holomorphic direction along
$\mathbb C$ produces the closed-string bar complex of
Sections~1--9: the differential extracts OPE residues from
collisions of points in the holomorphic plane.  The topological
direction along $\mathbb R$ produces the open-string coproduct: the
ordered splitting of tensor factors at a cut point of the real line.
The Swiss-cheese operad encodes the interaction of these two
structures: holomorphic operations acting on the fiber above
the topological interval, topological operations governing the
sequential composition.  The resulting two-colour algebraic
framework is not an embellishment of the bar complex but its
natural habitat: without the topological direction, the coproduct
has no operadic home, and the line-operator category has no
definition.

The primitive object of three-dimensional holomorphic-topological
quantum field theory on $\mathbb C_z \times \mathbb R_t$ is
therefore not the bar complex but the open/closed factorization
dg-category $\mathcal C$ on the bordified curve~$\widetilde{X}_D$.  Its
objects are boundary conditions, its morphisms are open-string
states, and a choice of vacuum~$b$ yields a boundary algebra
$A_b = \operatorname{End}_{\mathcal C}(b)$, determined only up to
Morita equivalence.  The governing operadic structure is the two-coloured
Swiss-cheese operad~$\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$, with closed
colour $\operatorname{FM}_k(\mathbb C)$ and open colour $E_1(m)$,
and it is homotopy-Koszul (proved).

The bar complex of Volume~I is the coalgebraic shadow of this
category: its differential records how closed-sector operations
twist the open-sector composition, and its coproduct records the
ordered splitting of the topological direction.  Together they make
$\barB(\cA)$ a coalgebra over the bar cooperad of the Swiss-cheese
operad.  The bar complex classifies \emph{twisting morphisms},
universal couplings between~$\cA$ and its Koszul dual~$\cA^!$,
and is not the bulk.

Three independent objects are constructed from~$\mathcal C$, and
must never be conflated:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item the \emph{bar complex} $\barB(A_b)$ classifies couplings
  between $A_b$ and~$A_b^!$;
\item the \emph{chiral derived center}
  $\cZ^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal C) =
  R\!\operatorname{Hom}_{\operatorname{Fun}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)}
  (\operatorname{Id}, \operatorname{Id})$
  is the universal bulk, computed in any chart by chiral Hochschild
  cochains $C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(A_b, A_b)$;
\item the \emph{Koszul dual} $A_b^!$ governs the line-operator
  category.
\end{enumerate}
The primitive hierarchy is:
\[
\mathcal C_{\mathrm{op}}
\;\xrightarrow{\;\operatorname{End}(b)\;}
A_b
\;\xrightarrow{\;\barB\;}
\barB(A_b)
\;\xrightarrow{\;\Theta\;}
\Theta_\cA
\;\xrightarrow{\;+\mu^{M_j}\;}
\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA.
\]
Each arrow is a lossy functor: $\mathcal C_{\mathrm{op}}$ is
Morita-invariant; $A_b$ depends on the choice of boundary
condition~$b$; $\barB$ forgets the bulk; $\Theta_\cA$ is the
closed-sector MC element; $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ restores the
full open/closed package.
Modularity is determined by the open sector: a cyclic trace on
$\operatorname{End}(b)$ seeds the Calabi--Yau structure; the
annulus identification
$\int_{S^1} \mathcal C \simeq \operatorname{HH}_\bullet(\mathcal C)$
is the first modular shadow; clutching (composing along
boundary circles via nodal degeneration) raises genus.
The genus expansion of
$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ yields the perturbative free energies
$F_g$; the shadow archetypes
$\mathsf{G}/\mathsf{L}/\mathsf{C}/\mathsf{M}$
classify the nonlinear complexity of the Swiss-cheese operations.

Volume~II constructs this architecture in four stages:
\emph{Stage~1} (local one-colour theorem: Swiss-cheese
universality of the derived center) $\Rightarrow$
\emph{Stage~2} (open primitive: $\mathcal C$ with Morita
invariance) $\Rightarrow$
\emph{Stage~3} (globalization on tangential log curves
$(X,D,\tau)$) $\Rightarrow$
\emph{Stage~4} (modularization: trace plus clutching producing
$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}$).
Stages~1--3 are proved.  In Stage~4, the open/closed MC element
$\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}}_\cA$ is constructed, the modular
MC equation holds at all genera
(Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-oc-mc-equation}), and the
projection principle recovers both the closed-sector genus
tower and the open-sector module structures
(Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-oc-projection}).
The annulus trace is proved
(Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-annulus-trace}).
The independent open-sector derivation of higher-genus
amplitudes and the chain-level cooperad compatibilities remain
open.

\subsection*{10.1.\enspace The holomorphic-topological Swiss-cheese operad}

The \emph{holomorphic-topological Swiss-cheese operad}
$\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ is a two-colored operad with color
set $\{\mathrm{ch},\mathrm{top}\}$.  The color $\mathrm{ch}$ is
\emph{closed} (holomorphic); the color $\mathrm{top}$ is
\emph{open} (topological).  The operation spaces are:
\begin{align*}
\mathsf{SC}(\mathrm{ch}^k;\mathrm{ch})
&=\operatorname{FM}_k(\mathbb C),\\
\mathsf{SC}(\mathrm{ch}^k,\mathrm{top}^m;\mathrm{top})
&=\operatorname{FM}_k(\mathbb C)\times E_1(m),\\
\mathsf{SC}(\ldots,\mathrm{top},\ldots;\mathrm{ch})
&=\varnothing.
\end{align*}
Closed-to-closed is the Fulton--MacPherson
compactification of configuration spaces in~$\mathbb C$.
The mixed direction combines holomorphic
configurations with the $E_1$-operad: $k$
holomorphic and $m$ topological insertion points,
with holomorphic insertions acting on the fiber above the interval.
Open-to-closed is forbidden.

Operadic composition is determined by the boundary stratification of
FM spaces in the holomorphic direction and by nested interval
inclusions in the topological direction.  If $\sigma_S$ denotes
the boundary stratum of $\operatorname{FM}_k(\mathbb C)$
corresponding to the simultaneous collision of the subset
$S\subset\{1,\ldots,k\}$, then the operadic composition map
$\gamma_{S}$ is the inclusion of the fiber product
\[
\gamma_S\colon
\operatorname{FM}_{|S|}(\mathbb C)\times\operatorname{FM}_{k-|S|+1}(\mathbb C)
\;\hookrightarrow\;
\operatorname{FM}_k(\mathbb C)
\]
as the normal bundle of~$\sigma_S$.  In the topological direction,
$E_1$-composition is the standard operadic substitution of intervals
into intervals.

A bar element of tensor degree~$k$ lives on the product
$\operatorname{FM}_k(\mathbb C)\times\operatorname{Conf}_k(\mathbb R)$.
The bar differential extracts OPE residues along collision divisors
of the first factor: when points $z_i$ and $z_j$ collide, the
residue of the propagator $\eta_{ij}=d\log(z_i-z_j)$ against the
collision divisor $\sigma_{\{i,j\}}$ yields the OPE mode
$a_{(n)}b$.  The coproduct splits an ordered sequence of tensor
factors at a point of the second factor: an element
$a_1\otimes\cdots\otimes a_k$ with ordering
$t_1<\cdots<t_k$ on $\mathbb R$ is decomposed at a cut point
$t_p<c<t_{p+1}$ into
$(a_1\otimes\cdots\otimes a_p)\otimes(a_{p+1}\otimes\cdots\otimes a_k)$.
The bar complex carrying both structures is an
$\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$-algebra.

\subsection*{10.2.\enspace Homotopy-Koszulity of $\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$}

The classical Swiss-cheese operad $\mathsf{SC}$ is Koszul
(Livernet, Voronov; Ginzburg--Kapranov).  The proof: the
Koszul dual cooperad $\mathsf{SC}^{\text{\raisebox{0.3ex}{!`}}}$
has a quadratic presentation, and the bar-cobar resolution is a
quasi-isomorphism by the combinatorial criterion of distributive
lattices applied to the poset of nested disks.  Kontsevich formality
supplies a quasi-isomorphism
\[
\Phi\colon\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}
\;\xrightarrow{\;\sim\;}\;
\mathsf{SC}
\]
constructed from Kontsevich's formality morphism for the $E_2$-operad
(configuration space integrals on FM spaces with propagators), extended
to the Swiss-cheese setting by including the half-plane $\mathbb H$
and its boundary $\mathbb R$.  The bar-cobar adjunction preserves
quasi-isomorphisms by the standard filtration-spectral-sequence
argument on the cobar side; the two-out-of-three property in the
model category of operads then gives
\[
\Omega\mathbf B(\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}})
\;\xrightarrow{\;\sim\;}\;
\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}.
\]
The bar-cobar adjunction on
$\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$-algebras is therefore a
\emph{Quillen equivalence}: the derived unit and counit are both
weak equivalences.  This has three consequences:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),nosep]
\item Every $\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$-algebra admits a
  cofibrant replacement by a bar-cobar resolution.
\item The homotopy category of
  $\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$-algebras is equivalent to the
  homotopy category of coalgebras over the Koszul dual cooperad.
\item The line-operator category $\cA^!\text{-}\mathsf{mod}$ is
  unconditionally defined as a module category over the bar
  resolution, without any finiteness hypothesis on~$\cA$.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{10.3.\enspace The $A_\infty$ chiral algebra structure}

The full Swiss-cheese MC element
$\alpha_T \in \operatorname{MC}(\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{SC}}_T)$
lives in the Swiss-cheese convolution algebra
$\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{SC}}_T :=
\operatorname{Hom}_\Sigma\bigl(
\mathbf{B}(\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}),
\operatorname{End}_{(B_\partial,\,\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{line}})}\bigr)$.
Its closed-colour projection $(m_k)_{k\ge 1}$
encodes the $A_\infty$ chiral algebra on~$\cA$.  Each component
\[
m_k\colon\cA^{\otimes k}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\cA((\lambda_1))\cdots((\lambda_{k-1}))
\]
is a configuration-space integral on
$\operatorname{FM}_k(\mathbb C)\times\operatorname{Conf}_k(\mathbb R)$.
Write $\omega_I$ for the form on $\operatorname{FM}_k(\mathbb C)$
obtained by wedging the propagators $\eta_{ij}=d\log(z_i-z_j)$
for all pairs $(i,j)\in I$.  The holomorphic factor produces the
OPE singularity; the topological factor produces the ordering.
Explicitly, $m_k$ at arity $k$ is the sum over trees $T$ with $k$
leaves of
\[
m_T(a_1,\ldots,a_k)
\;=\;
\int_{\operatorname{FM}_k(\mathbb C)}
\omega_T\,\cdot\,
\prod_{v\in V(T)} a_{(n_v)} b_v\,,
\]
where the integration is against the compactified configuration
space volume form and the product is over internal vertices of~$T$
with the OPE modes prescribed by the edge labels.

The Maurer--Cartan equation
$\partial\alpha+\alpha\star\alpha=0$ is the \emph{spectral Stasheff
identity}.  Integration over the boundary strata of
$\operatorname{FM}_k(\mathbb C)$ produces the $A_\infty$ relations
by Stokes' theorem:
\[
\sum_{\substack{p+q=k+1\\1\le i\le p}}
\pm\,m_p(a_1,\ldots,a_{i-1},\,m_q(a_i,\ldots,a_{i+q-1}),\,a_{i+q},\ldots,a_k)
\;=\;0.
\]
Each term in this identity corresponds to a codimension-one
boundary stratum of $\operatorname{FM}_k(\mathbb C)$ where a
subset of points collides: the inner $m_q$ extracts the OPE from
the collision, and the outer $m_p$ evaluates the remaining
configuration.

\subsection*{10.4.\enspace PVA descent: Theorem G}

On cohomology $H^\bullet(\cA,Q)$, the operations simplify by a
dimension count.

\medskip
\noindent\emph{The commutative product.}
The regular part of~$m_2$, the constant term as the two points
separate, is a commutative associative product~$\mu$:
\[
\mu(a,b)
\;=\;
\operatorname{Reg}_{z_1\to z_2}\,m_2(a(z_1),b(z_2)).
\]
Commutativity: $\operatorname{FM}_2(\mathbb C)$ has a $\mathbb Z/2$
involution exchanging the two points; the regular part is invariant.
Associativity: the three boundary strata of
$\operatorname{FM}_3(\mathbb C)$ corresponding to pairwise
collisions contribute only to the singular part; the regular
boundary term is associativity.

\medskip
\noindent\emph{The $\lambda$-bracket.}
The singular part of~$m_2$ defines the $\lambda$-bracket:
\[
\{a_\lambda b\}
\;=\;
\operatorname{Res}_{z_1\to z_2}\,
e^{\lambda(z_1-z_2)}\,
m_2(a(z_1),b(z_2)).
\]
The exponential extracts all pole orders simultaneously:
$\{a_\lambda b\}=\sum_{n\ge 0}\lambda^n a_{(n)}b/n!$.

\medskip
\noindent\emph{Vanishing of higher operations.}
All $m_{k\ge 3}=0$ on $H^\bullet$: the topological factor
$\operatorname{Conf}_k(\mathbb R)$ is contractible for $k\ge 3$
(it retracts to a point by pulling all $k$ ordered points together),
so the cohomological representative of $m_k$ is $d_{\mathbb R}$-exact
and therefore trivial on $H^\bullet$.

\medskip
\noindent\emph{Jacobi identity from the Arnold relation.}
On $\operatorname{FM}_3(\mathbb C)$, the three propagators
$\eta_{12}$, $\eta_{23}$, $\eta_{31}$ satisfy the Arnold relation:
\[
\eta_{12}\wedge\eta_{23}
\;+\;
\eta_{23}\wedge\eta_{31}
\;+\;
\eta_{31}\wedge\eta_{12}
\;=\;0.
\]
This identity on differential forms is equivalent to the three
codimension-one boundary divisors of $\overline M_{0,4}$ being
homologous to zero in sum.  Taking the residue of this relation
against $a\otimes b\otimes c$ produces the three terms of the
Jacobi identity for $\{-_\lambda-\}$:
\[
\{a_\lambda\{b_\mu c\}\}
\;-\;
\{b_\mu\{a_\lambda c\}\}
\;=\;
\{\{a_\lambda b\}_{\lambda+\mu}c\}.
\]

\medskip
\noindent\emph{Leibniz rule from three-face Stokes.}
The boundary of $\operatorname{FM}_3(\mathbb C)$ decomposes into
three codimension-one faces, each corresponding to a pairwise
collision.  The Stokes identity
\[
\int_{\partial\operatorname{FM}_3(\mathbb C)}\omega
\;=\;
\int_{\sigma_{12}}\omega
\;+\;
\int_{\sigma_{23}}\omega
\;+\;
\int_{\sigma_{13}}\omega
\;=\;0
\]
applied to the form
$\omega=\eta_{12}\wedge\eta_{23}\cdot a(z_1)b(z_2)c(z_3)$
gives: on~$\sigma_{12}$, the bracket $\{a_\lambda b\}$ is formed
first and then multiplied by~$c$; on~$\sigma_{23}$,
$a$ multiplied by $\{b_\lambda c\}$; on~$\sigma_{13}$,
$\{a_\lambda c\}\cdot b$.  The cancellation is the Leibniz rule:
\[
\{a_\lambda(b\cdot c)\}
\;=\;
\{a_\lambda b\}\cdot c
\;+\;
b\cdot\{a_\lambda c\}.
\]

\medskip
\noindent\emph{Skew-symmetry from the exchange cylinder.}
The exchange involution on
$\operatorname{FM}_2(\mathbb C)\times E_1(2)$ swaps the two
insertion points.  The monodromy of $\eta_{12}$ around the exchange
loop in the $E_1$ direction produces a sign and a shift:
$\{a_\lambda b\}=-\{b_{-\lambda-\partial}a\}$.  The derivative
$\partial$ appears because the exchange path on $E_1(2)$ winds
once around the difference coordinate $z_1-z_2$.

\medskip
\noindent
Thus $(\mu,\{-_\lambda-\})$ is a $(-1)$-shifted Poisson
vertex algebra, each axiom following in one line from the
geometry of $\operatorname{FM}_k(\mathbb C)$.

\subsection*{10.5.\enspace The Heisenberg algebra in Swiss-cheese coordinates}

For the Heisenberg algebra $\mathcal H_k$, generated by a
single field $J$ of conformal weight~$1$ with
$J(z)J(w)\sim k/(z-w)^2$:
\[
m_2(J,J)=k\cdot\mathbf{1},
\qquad
m_{k\ge 3}=0,
\qquad
\{J_\lambda J\}=k\lambda.
\]
All higher operations vanish because the OPE has no first-order
pole: the only nontrivial residue is $J_{(1)}J=k$, and
configuration-space integrals at arity $k\ge 3$ factor through
this single datum, yielding zero by degree considerations
(the form $\eta_{12}\wedge\cdots$ has too high a degree to pair
nontrivially with the rank-one OPE data).  The spectral
$R$-matrix is
\[
R(z)\;=\;\exp(k/z).
\]
The Yang--Baxter equation is trivially satisfied: the $R$-matrix is
scalar (acting on $\mathbb C\otimes\mathbb C$), so both sides of
the YBE are $\exp(k/z_{12}+k/z_{13}+k/z_{23})$.  The PVA
$\{J_\lambda J\}=k\lambda$ is the free bosonic PVA, the universal
enveloping PVA of the rank-one abelian Lie conformal algebra.

\subsection*{10.6.\enspace The Koszul triangle}

The open factorization dg-category $\mathcal C$ on
$\widetilde{X}_D$ produces three independent algebraic objects,
each by a different functor:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item \emph{Boundary.}  $A_b = \operatorname{End}_{\mathcal C}(b)$
  for a chosen vacuum object~$b$: an algebra over the open colour
  of $\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$, encoding the
  $E_1$-composition.  The boundary algebra is a \emph{chart} on
  $\mathcal C$, determined up to Morita equivalence by the choice
  of~$b$.
\item \emph{Bulk.}
  $\cZ^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal C)
  = R\!\operatorname{Hom}_{\operatorname{Fun}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)}
  (\operatorname{Id}, \operatorname{Id})$:
  the chiral derived center, the universal algebra of bulk
  operators.  It is Morita-invariant, independent of the choice
  of~$b$.  In any chart it is computed by chiral Hochschild
  cochains $C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(A_b, A_b)$.
\item \emph{Lines.}
  $A_b^{!}{}_\infty = D_{\operatorname{Ran}}(\barB(A_b))$: the
  \emph{homotopy} Koszul dual, obtained by Verdier duality on the
  bar coalgebra.  On the Koszul locus, its cohomology recovers the
  strict Koszul dual $A_b^! = (H^*(\barB(A_b)))^\vee$ (Theorem~A).
  The module category $A_b^!\text{-}\mathsf{mod}$, equipped with
  the spectral $R$-matrix~$R(z)$, is the braided tensor category
  of line operators.
\end{enumerate}
The three objects are related by a triangle of identifications
\[
\cZ^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal C)
\;\simeq\;
\operatorname{HH}^\bullet(A_b)
\;\simeq\;
\mathrm{ChirHoch}^\bullet(A_b^!),
\qquad
A_b^!\text{-}\mathsf{mod}\;=\;\{\text{line operators}\},
\]
but the three functors (endomorphisms, Ran-space Verdier
duality, identity-bimodule endomorphisms) must never be
conflated.  In particular: the bar complex $\barB(A_b)$ classifies
twisting morphisms (universal couplings between $A_b$ and~$A_b^!$)
and is not the bulk.  The derived center classifies bulk operators
acting on the boundary.

\medskip
\noindent\emph{The spectral braiding.}
The $R$-matrix $R(z)\colon L_1\otimes L_2\xrightarrow{\sim}
L_2\otimes L_1$ is the spectral braiding on $\cA^!$-modules.
Stokes' theorem on $\operatorname{FM}_3(\mathbb C)$ applied to
the triple convolution $\alpha\star\alpha\star\alpha$ decomposes
the boundary into three pairwise collision divisors, one for
each side of the Yang--Baxter equation:
\[
R_{12}(z_1{-}z_2)\,R_{13}(z_1{-}z_3)\,R_{23}(z_2{-}z_3)
\;=\;
R_{23}(z_2{-}z_3)\,R_{13}(z_1{-}z_3)\,R_{12}(z_1{-}z_2).
\]
The three boundary strata of $\operatorname{FM}_3(\mathbb C)$ are
in bijection with the three channels $(12|3)$, $(13|2)$,
$(23|1)$; the Stokes cancellation
$\sum_{\sigma}\int_{\sigma}\omega=0$ is precisely the YBE.

\medskip
\noindent\emph{Bulk = derived center.}
Let $\cB_\partial$ be the boundary factorization algebra on
$\mathbb R$ (the open/topological algebra of the SC structure).
Its derived center
$Z_{\mathrm{der}}(\cB_\partial)
:=R\operatorname{Hom}_{\cB_\partial\text{-}\mathrm{bimod}}
(\cB_\partial,\cB_\partial)$
computes endomorphisms of the identity bimodule.  The $E_1$-structure
on $\cB_\partial$ gives
$Z_{\mathrm{der}}(\cB_\partial)\simeq\mathrm{HH}^\bullet(\cB_\partial)$
as an $E_2$-algebra.  The Swiss-cheese structure maps the holomorphic
bulk algebra to this $E_2$-algebra, and the Quillen equivalence
makes the map an equivalence.

\medskip
\noindent\emph{Lines = $\cA^!$-modules.}
An $\cA^!$-module~$M$ defines a line operator: the module
structure $\cA^!\otimes M\to M$ is a topological boundary
condition parametrised by a line in $\mathbb R$, and the spectral
braiding $R(z)$ provides the crossing data when two lines
intersect.  The category $\cC:=\cA^!\text{-}\mathsf{mod}$ with
braiding $R(z)$ is the braided tensor category of line operators
of the 3d holomorphic-topological theory.

\subsection*{10.7.\enspace Curved Swiss-cheese at genus $g\ge 1$}

At genus $g\ge 1$, the bar complex
$(\bar B^{\mathrm{ch},(g)}(\cA),\,d_{\mathrm{fib}},\,\Delta)$
carries curvature:
\[
d_{\mathrm{fib}}^{\,2}\;=\;\kappa(\cA)\cdot\omega_g.
\]
The curvature $\omega_g$ is the Arakelov $(1,1)$-form on the fiber
of the universal curve $\pi\colon\cC_g\to\overline{\cM}_g$,
representing the first Chern class of the relative dualising sheaf.
The coproduct~$\Delta$ remains strictly coassociative: the
topological $E_1$-structure on $\mathbb R$ sees no curvature
(the interval has no nontrivial topology).  The curvature lives
entirely in the holomorphic direction.

The total corrected differential
\[
D_g\;=\;d_{\mathrm{fib}}+\nabla^{\mathrm{GM}}_g
\]
restores flatness over $\overline{\cM}_g$ by coupling the
$\mathbb R$-ordering to the Hodge bundle~$\mathbb E$.  The
Gauss--Manin connection $\nabla^{\mathrm{GM}}$ absorbs the
$(1,1)$-curvature: $D_g^{\,2}=0$ because
$d_{\mathrm{fib}}^{\,2}+[d_{\mathrm{fib}},\nabla^{\mathrm{GM}}]
+(\nabla^{\mathrm{GM}})^2=\kappa\omega_g-\kappa\omega_g=0$.

The derived category of modules must be replaced by the
\emph{coderived} category $\mathsf{D}^{\mathrm{co}}(\cA^{(g)})$
(or the contraderived category
$\mathsf{D}^{\mathrm{ctr}}(\cA^{(g)})$, depending on the side):
curvature forces $d^2\neq 0$ on fibers, so the ordinary derived
category is empty (every object is acyclic), while the coderived
category, defined via totalisation of the curvature bicomplex,
retains the correct homotopy theory.  The passage from derived
to coderived is the categorified form of the passage from
$d^2=0$ to the curved Maurer--Cartan equation
$d\alpha+\alpha^2+\kappa\omega=0$.

\subsection*{10.8.\enspace The Lagrangian self-intersection}

Volume~II identifies the geometric substrate of the bar construction:
the bar complex is the structure sheaf of the Lagrangian
self-intersection
$\mathfrak{S} = \mathcal{L} \times_{\mathcal{M}} \mathcal{L}$
in a $(-2)$-shifted symplectic stack, and every theorem of this
volume is a face of that geometry.
The bar-cobar adjunction (Theorem~A) is the groupoid
comodule-module adjunction for~$\mathfrak{S}$;
Koszul inversion (Theorem~B) reconstructs the Lagrangian from
its clean self-intersection;
complementarity (Theorem~C) is two Lagrangians whose intersection
carries a $(-1)$-shifted symplectic structure;
the modular characteristic (Theorem~D) is the Kodaira--Spencer
class of the Lagrangian family over the Hodge bundle;
and the Hochschild polynomial growth (Theorem~H) is the HKR
theorem for the Lagrangian embedding.

\subsection*{10.9.\enspace The factorization-primary hierarchy}

The Swiss-cheese operad $\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ is a
\emph{local model}: the formal completion of a factorization
structure at collision points.  The global truth is a factorizable
$\mathcal D$-module on $\operatorname{Ran}(\Sigma_g)$ (the Ran
space of finite non-empty subsets of the curve), varying in families
over~$\overline{\cM}_g$.  The operad is extracted from this by
restricting to formal neighborhoods of the small diagonal, where
$\Sigma_g \simeq \mathbb C$ and the factorization pattern reduces
to FM-space operations.  Six layers organise the hierarchy:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),nosep]
\item \emph{Geometric substrate:} smooth and stable nodal curves,
  Ran space, $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$.
\item \emph{Factorizable $\mathcal D$-modules} (Beilinson--Drinfeld):
  a chiral algebra is a factorizable $\mathcal D$-module on
  $\operatorname{Ran}(X)$, not an algebra over an operad.
\item \emph{HT product geometry:} $\Sigma_g \times \mathbb R$ with
  holomorphic factorization in~$\Sigma_g$ and locally constant
  factorization in~$\mathbb R$.
\item \emph{Bar as factorization coalgebra:} the bar complex is the
  factorization coalgebra on $\operatorname{Ran}(X)$ Koszul-dual to
  the chiral algebra.  At genus~$0$: honest dg coalgebra.  At
  genus~$g \ge 1$: curved factorization coalgebra.
\item \emph{Koszul duality as factorization duality:} bar-cobar is
  factorization algebra $\leftrightarrow$ coalgebra duality.
  Feynman involution $\mathrm{FT}^2 \simeq \mathrm{id}$ is the
  involutivity of this duality.
\item \emph{Three models as three gauges:} the flat associated graded
  ($D_0^2 = 0$, operadic/local), the corrected holomorphic
  ($D^{(g)\,2} = 0$, Fay trisecant, still local), and the curved
  geometric ($d_{\mathrm{fib}}^2 = \kappa \cdot \omega_g$, Arakelov,
  global).  The corrected model is visible to the local operad; the
  curved model requires the factorization framework.
\end{enumerate}
The curvature $d_{\mathrm{fib}}^2 = \kappa \cdot \omega_g$ is the
measure of what the local extraction loses: it is the monodromy of
the $\mathcal D$-module connection around the $B$-cycles of
$\Sigma_g$, invisible to the formal-disc model.  The modular bar
complex $\barB_{\mathrm{mod}}(\cA)$ is flat ($D^2 = 0$) because it
couples all genera simultaneously via the non-separating operator
$D_1$; the genus-$g$ bar complex on a fixed surface is curved
because restricting to a single genus decouples this connection.

The relative Feynman transform
$\mathrm{FT}_{\mathsf{Com}_{\mathrm{mod}}/\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}}$
mediates between the factorization (global) and operadic (local)
viewpoints.  The modular bar coalgebra is naturally an algebra over
this relative transform.  Relative homotopy-involutivity plus
factorization Koszul duality gives the flat-derived /
curved-coderived comparison at all genera: the two flat models share
an ordinary derived package, while the genus-fixed curved model is
its coderived avatar rather than a third ordinary chain complex.

\subsection*{10.10.\enspace The four-stage architecture}

Four stages, each depending on its predecessor.

\medskip
\noindent
\emph{Stage~1: Local one-colour theorem.}
The Swiss-cheese operad $\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ is
homotopy-Koszul; the resulting bar-cobar adjunction is a Quillen
equivalence.  The chiral derived center
$\cZ^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal C)
\simeq C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(A_b, A_b)$
is the universal bulk algebra.  \textsc{Proved.}

\medskip
\noindent
\emph{Stage~2: Open primitive.}
The primitive object is the open factorization dg-category
$\mathcal C$.  The boundary algebra
$A_b = \operatorname{End}_{\mathcal C}(b)$ is a chart, not an
essence; the bulk $\cZ^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal C)$
is Morita-invariant.  \textsc{Proved.}

\medskip
\noindent
\emph{Stage~3: Globalization.}
Tangential log curves $(X,D,\tau)$ provide the geometric substrate
for bordered Fulton--MacPherson compactification.  The local-global
bridge lifts the operad-level Swiss-cheese structure to a
factorizable $\mathcal D$-module on $\operatorname{Ran}(X)$.
\textsc{Proved locally; modest globally.}

\medskip
\noindent
\emph{Stage~4: Modularization.}
Trace and clutching on the open sector produce the full modular
Maurer--Cartan element $\Theta^{\mathrm{oc}} = \Theta_\cA
+ \sum \mu^{M_j}$.  The annulus trace
$\int_{S^1}\mathcal C \simeq \operatorname{HH}_\bullet(\mathcal C)$
is the first modular shadow of the open sector; clutching
along boundary circles via nodal degeneration raises genus.
\textsc{Annulus trace proved; full chain-level clutching is
programme.}

\medskip
Five negative principles constrain the architecture:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{N\arabic*.},nosep]
\item \emph{Bar $\neq$ bulk.}
  The bar complex $\barB(A_b)$ is a factorization coalgebra
  classifying twisting morphisms.  The bulk
  $\cZ^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal C)$ is the chiral
  derived center classifying bulk operators.  Different functors,
  different outputs.
\item \emph{Boundary algebra $=$ chart.}
  $A_b = \operatorname{End}_{\mathcal C}(b)$ depends on the choice
  of vacuum~$b$.  Only $\mathcal C$ itself and its derived center
  are intrinsic.
\item \emph{Tangential log geometry required.}
  The bordified curve $\widetilde{X}_D$ is a manifold with corners
  on an snc pair $(X,D)$.  Ordinary Fulton--MacPherson
  compactification is the $D = \varnothing$ special case.
\item \emph{Modularity $=$ trace $+$ clutching on the open sector.}
  The genus expansion is not an additional axiom on the closed
  algebra; it is determined by the cyclic trace on
  $\operatorname{End}_{\mathcal C}(b)$ and the gluing along
  boundary circles.
\item \emph{Honest scope.}
  The dg-shifted Yangian is proved for affine lineage (Kac--Moody
  and its standard reductions).  Extension to non-standard families
  is programme, not theorem.
\end{enumerate}

% ====================================================================
\section*{11.\quad Modular PVA quantization}
% ====================================================================

The open/closed world of Section~10 produces a genus-zero datum: the
Swiss-cheese MC element $\alpha_T$, the PVA
$(\mu,\{-_\lambda-\})$ on cohomology, and the KZ/BPZ shadow
connections at arity~$n$.  All of these are tree-level structures.
The question that forces the present section is: how does this
genus-zero structure extend across the genus filtration?  The
answer is the modular PVA quantization programme: a
genus-by-genus obstruction theory whose input is the genus-zero
PVA and whose output is the full modular MC element.  The
nonseparating degeneration operator $D_1$ is the primitive
genus-raising differential; it squares to zero, anticommutes
with the tree-level differential $D_0$, and defines a spectral
sequence whose obstructions are the quantization anomalies.

\subsection*{11.1.\enspace The one-edge principle}

To verify a modular operad structure, it suffices to check
compatibility with a single edge contraction: all higher-edge
relations follow from codimension-two cancellation.

If a complete filtered dg Lie algebra~$L$ carries a genus filtration
and its differential preserves genus exactly, then any genus-zero
Maurer--Cartan element
$\Theta_0\in\operatorname{MC}(\operatorname{gr}_F^0 L)$ extends
tautologically to a full MC element: genus by genus, the obstruction
class $[D_1\Theta_0]\in H^2(\operatorname{gr}^1 L)$ vanishes
because no differential raises genus.  Therefore every nontrivial
modular obstruction theory must contain a primitive genus-raising
operator.

The one-edge expansion of the stable-graph differential furnishes
this primitive.  Every one-edge degeneration of a stable graph is
either \emph{separating} (two vertices joined by one edge, total
genus preserved) or \emph{nonseparating} (one vertex acquiring one
loop, total genus raised by~$1$).  Set
\[
D_{\mathrm{exp}}\;=\;D_{\mathrm{sep}}+D_{\mathrm{nsep}},
\qquad
D_0\;:=\;D_{\mathrm{int}}+D_{\mathrm{sep}},
\qquad
D_1\;:=\;D_{\mathrm{nsep}}.
\]
Then $D_0$ preserves total genus, $D_1$ raises total genus by one,
and $(D_0+D_1)^2=0$ stratifies by genus shift into three identities:
\[
D_0^2=0,
\qquad
D_0 D_1+D_1 D_0=0,
\qquad
D_1^2=0.
\]
The first: $D_0$ is a differential.  The second: $D_1$ is a
$D_0$-derivation (it anticommutes with~$D_0$, so it descends to a
map on $D_0$-cohomology).  The third: $D_1$ squares to zero, so
the genus-one obstruction is a well-defined cohomology class.
