The three identities are the codimension-two cancellation axiom
stratified by genus.

Trees govern chirality; loops govern
modularity.  $D_0$ (tree-level
degenerations) encodes OPE residues and
factorization.  $D_1$ (loop-creating
degenerations) encodes genus raising, trace
maps, the odd Laplacian.  The full modular bar theory is their
interaction.

\subsection*{11.2.\enspace The modular bar datum}

A \emph{modular bar datum} on a reduced, complete, finite-type
graded collection $F\mapsto C(F)$ consists of:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
\item An internal differential $d\colon C(F)\to C(F)$ of
  degree~$+1$, with $d^2=0$.
\item For each one-edge expansion
  $\epsilon\in\operatorname{OE}(F)$ (an edge $e$ adjoined to the
  flag set~$F$, either separating (producing two flag sets
  $F_1\sqcup F_2=F\setminus\{f_1,f_2\}\sqcup\{f'_1,f'_2\}$)
  or nonseparating (the flag set $F$ acquires two new flags
  $\{h,h'\}$ identified as half-edges of~$e$, raising genus
  by~$1$)), a degree-$+1$ map
  \[
  \Delta_\epsilon\colon sC(F)
  \;\longrightarrow\;
  \orline(\epsilon)\otimes
  \bigotimes_{u\in V(\epsilon)}sC(\operatorname{Fl}_\epsilon(u)),
  \]
  where $\orline(\epsilon)$ is the orientation line of the
  new edge.
\item The \emph{codimension-two cancellation axiom}: for every
  connected stable graph with exactly two internal edges, the
  signed sum of the two ways of producing it by successive
  one-edge expansions is zero:
  \[
  \sum_{\substack{\epsilon_1,\epsilon_2\\
  \epsilon_1\circ\epsilon_2=\Gamma}}
  \operatorname{sgn}(\epsilon_1,\epsilon_2)\cdot
  \Delta_{\epsilon_2}\circ\Delta_{\epsilon_1}
  \;=\;0.
  \]
\item The anticommutation relation
  $d\circ\Delta_\epsilon+\Delta_\epsilon\circ d=0$.
\end{enumerate}
The total differential
$D=D_{\mathrm{int}}+D_{\mathrm{exp}}
=d+\sum_\epsilon\Delta_\epsilon$ satisfies $D^2=0$ by three
mechanisms: $d^2=0$ on vertex labels; anticommutation of~$d$
with one-edge expansions; and the codimension-two cancellation
axiom for two-edge graphs.  This is the algebraic incarnation
of the cell decomposition of $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$ into
stable-graph strata: the codimension-two axiom is the statement
that every codimension-two stratum arises from two distinct
codimension-one degenerations, with opposite signs.

\subsection*{11.3.\enspace The complete modular bar coalgebra}

For a connected stable graph $\Gamma$ of genus~$g$ with
vertex set $V(\Gamma)$, edge set $E(\Gamma)$, and leg set
$L(\Gamma)$, set
\[
C[\Gamma]
\;:=\;
\orline(\Gamma)\otimes
\bigotimes_{v\in V(\Gamma)}sC(\operatorname{Fl}(v)),
\]
where $\orline(\Gamma)=\bigotimes_{e\in E(\Gamma)}\orline(e)$
is the total orientation line and $\operatorname{Fl}(v)$ is the
flag set at vertex~$v$.  The \emph{complete modular bar coalgebra}
is
\[
\mathrm B_{\mathrm{mod}}(C)
\;=\;
\prod_{[\Gamma]\in\mathsf{StGraph}^{\mathrm{conn}}}
\bigl(C[\Gamma]\bigr)_{\operatorname{Aut}(\Gamma)},
\]
completed over total genus
$g(\Gamma)=b_1(\Gamma)+\sum_{v}g(v)$.  The reduced coproduct is
edge contraction: contracting an internal edge of~$\Gamma$
strictly decreases the number of internal edges, so the
coalgebra is conilpotent.  The differential on
$\mathrm B_{\mathrm{mod}}(C)$ is the sum of the internal
differential (acting on vertex labels) and the expansion
differential (summing over all possible one-edge insertions into
each graph).

\subsection*{11.4.\enspace The strict modular deformation algebra}

The coderivation dg Lie algebra
\[
L_{\mathrm{mod}}(C)
\;:=\;
\operatorname{Coder}\bigl(\mathrm B_{\mathrm{mod}}(C)\bigr)[-1]
\]
is the \emph{strict modular deformation algebra}.  Its elements
are coderivations of the modular bar coalgebra, shifted by~$-1$
to place the Lie bracket in degree~$0$.  The convolution
description: the universal property of the cofree coalgebra gives
\[
L_{\mathrm{mod}}(C)
\;\cong\;
\operatorname{Hom}\bigl(\mathrm B_{\mathrm{mod}}(C),\,sC\bigr)[-1]
\]
with the commutator bracket
$[f,g]=f\star g-(-1)^{|f||g|}g\star f$, where
$f\star g$ is the convolution product (compose $f$ with the
coproduct, apply $g$ to one tensor factor, compose back).

The algebra $L_{\mathrm{mod}}(C)$ is complete filtered by genus:
$F^g L_{\mathrm{mod}}(C)$ consists of coderivations supported on
graphs of genus $\ge g$.  The completion is pro-nilpotent:
$F^1 L_{\mathrm{mod}}$ is a pro-nilpotent dg Lie algebra, and
$\operatorname{gr}^0 L_{\mathrm{mod}}$ is the tree-level
deformation algebra.  The full algebra is Lie-multiplicative:
the bracket $[f,g]$ respects the genus filtration, and the
associated graded inherits a dg Lie structure at each genus.

\subsection*{11.5.\enspace The genus-one obstruction theorem}

For a genus-zero MC element $\Theta_0\in\operatorname{MC}(\operatorname{gr}^0_F L)$
satisfying $D_0\Theta_0+\tfrac12[\Theta_0,\Theta_0]_0=0$,
the genus-one obstruction is
\[
\operatorname{Ob}_1(\Theta_0)
\;=\;
[D_1\Theta_0]
\;\in\;
H^2\!\bigl((\operatorname{gr}^1_F L)^{\Theta_0},\,d_0^{\Theta_0}\bigr),
\]
where $d_0^{\Theta_0}=D_0+[\Theta_0,-]$ is the $\Theta_0$-twisted
differential on the genus-one piece.  The class
$\operatorname{Ob}_1(\Theta_0)$ is well-defined:
$D_1\Theta_0$ is a $d_0^{\Theta_0}$-cocycle because of the
identity $D_0 D_1+D_1 D_0=0$ and the MC equation for~$\Theta_0$.
It vanishes if and only if $\Theta_0$ lifts to a genus-one MC
element $\Theta_0+\hbar\Theta_1$ satisfying
\[
(D_0+D_1)(\Theta_0+\hbar\Theta_1)
+\tfrac12[\Theta_0+\hbar\Theta_1,\Theta_0+\hbar\Theta_1]
\;=\;0
\qquad\bmod\;\hbar^2.
\]

In PVA coordinates, the nonseparating one-edge operator acts as
the reduced odd Laplacian.  For a cyclic $A_\infty$-algebra
$(A,m_k,\langle-,-\rangle)$ with basis $\{e^i\}$ and dual
basis $\{e_i\}$:
\[
\ell_1^{(1)}(a)
\;=\;
\hbar\Delta_{\mathrm{cyc}}(a)
\;:=\;
\hbar\sum_{i}m_2(e^i,m_2(a,e_i))
\;\in\;
A,
\]
the cyclic contraction over the single loop.  This is the
genus-raising operator: it takes a genus-$0$ vertex label and
produces a genus-$1$ correction by contracting one pair of
insertions through the cyclic pairing.  The full genus-one
obstruction $\operatorname{Ob}_1$ is the cohomology class of
$\Delta_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\Theta_0)$ in the twisted complex.

\subsection*{11.6.\enspace The $\mathcal W_3$ computation}

A \emph{filtered quadratic PVA} is a differential commutative
algebra freely generated by fields $u^1,\ldots,u^N$ and their
derivatives, with a $\lambda$-bracket encoded by a skew-adjoint
matrix differential operator
$\Pi^{ab}(\partial)=\sum_{m\ge 0}\Pi^{ab}_m\partial^m$ whose
coefficients have total generator degree at most~$2$.  Classical
$\mathcal W_3$ fits this pattern: two generators $T$
(weight~$2$) and $W$ (weight~$3$), with the quasi-primary
composite
\[
\Lambda\;=\;{:}TT{:}\;-\;\tfrac{3}{10}\,\partial^2 T
\]
controlling the nonlinear channel.  The $WW$~OPE is
\begin{align*}
W(z)W(w)
\;&\sim\;
\frac{c/3}{(z-w)^6}
\;+\;
\frac{2T}{(z-w)^4}
\;+\;
\frac{\partial T}{(z-w)^3}\\
&\quad\;+\;
\frac{1}{(z-w)^2}\biggl(\tfrac{3}{10}\partial^2 T
+\frac{16}{22+5c}\Lambda\biggr)
\;+\;
\frac{1}{z-w}\biggl(\cdots\biggr).
\end{align*}
At $c=-22/5$, the denominator $22+5c$ vanishes, $\Lambda$
becomes null, and $\mathcal W_3$ is no longer finitely generated
by $T$ and~$W$ alone.

The \emph{triangular $W$-normal form vanishing theorem} asserts:
in the local, translation-invariant, filtration-preserving sector,
$\operatorname{Ob}_1(\Theta_0)=0$ for classical $\mathcal W_3$.
The computation: the relevant cohomology group is
\[
H^1\!\bigl((\operatorname{gr}^1 L)^{\Theta_0},\,d_0^{\Theta_0}\bigr)
\;\cong\;\mathbb C\cdot\partial_c P_c\,,
\]
one-dimensional, spanned by the central-parameter
direction~$\partial_c P_c$, where $P_c$ is the $\lambda$-bracket
matrix viewed as a function of~$c$.  Concretely: every genus-one
lift of the classical $\mathcal W_3$ PVA is gauge equivalent to a
renormalization of the central charge $c\mapsto c+\hbar c_1$.
The genus-one quantum $\mathcal W_3$ algebra is the unique quantization
in the direction~$\partial_c$.

\subsection*{11.7.\enspace Curved extension via $S$-tails}

In the inhomogeneous quadratic setting (Gui--Li--Zeng), the correct
input is a \emph{twisted pair} $(B,B^\circ,S)$: a CDG-algebra~$B$,
a CDG-coalgebra~$B^\circ$, and a curvature element~$S$.
An \emph{$S$-tail expansion} attaches a new univalent
$S$-decorated vertex to a pre-existing corolla: formally, a
unary expansion map
\[
\Delta_S\colon sC(F)\;\longrightarrow\;sC(F\sqcup\{\bullet,\star\})
\]
followed by contraction of the new internal edge, with the
vertex~$\star$ carrying the curvature label~$S$.  Adjoining
$S$-tail expansions to the one-edge expansion set, with the
same codimension-two compatibilities, produces a \emph{curved
complete modular bar object}.

The Maurer--Cartan equation in the curved setting is:
\[
\mu\!\bigl((S+\alpha)\boxtimes(S+\alpha)\bigr)\;=\;0,
\]
the modular extension of the Gui--Li--Zeng curved equation.
The element $S+\alpha$ combines the curvature~$S$ (a genus-zero
scalar, the analogue of $m_0$) with the deformation
parameter~$\alpha$.  The equation unpacks genus by genus: at
genus~$0$, it is the curved $A_\infty$ MC equation
$\sum_k m_k(\alpha^{\otimes k})=0$ with $m_0=S$; at genus~$1$,
it is $\Delta_{\mathrm{cyc}}(S+\alpha)=0$, the vanishing of the
curved odd Laplacian; at genus~$g$, it is the BV quantum master
equation $\hbar\Delta(e^{(S+\alpha)/\hbar})=0$.

\subsection*{11.8.\enspace Genus-zero comparison with Gui--Li--Zeng}

At tree level, the modular MC equation reduces to the
classical twisting morphism equation.  For a Koszul pair
$(\cA,\cA^!)$ with $\cA^!$ a CDG algebra with curvature~$S$,
the genus-zero MC space is
\[
\operatorname{MC}_0(L_{\mathrm{mod}})
\;\cong\;
\operatorname{Hom}_{\mathsf{dg}}(\cA,B^\circ)
\;\hookrightarrow\;
\operatorname{MC}(\cA^!\widehat{\otimes}\cB),
\]
where $\cB$ is a test algebra.  This recovers the Gui--Li--Zeng
correspondence: tree-level MC elements of the modular deformation
algebra are twisting morphisms $\cA\to B^\circ$, which are in
bijection with CDG-algebra morphisms $B\to\cA^!\widehat\otimes\cB$.
The modular theory is the genus extension of this classical picture.


% ====================================================================
\section*{12.\quad Holographic modular Koszul duality}
% ====================================================================

The open/closed world (Section~10) supplies the three-dimensional
geometric framework; the modular PVA quantization programme
(Section~11) supplies the genus-by-genus obstruction theory.  The
holographic modular Koszul datum packages both into a single
algebraic object: a six-component structure that records the
boundary algebra, its Koszul dual, the line-operator category, the
spectral $R$-matrix, the universal MC element, and the modular
shadow connection.  Every ingredient constructed so far (the
bar complex, the shadow obstruction tower, the Swiss-cheese structure, the PVA
descent, the genus expansion) appears as a projection of this
datum.  The datum is not a summary; it is the natural unit of
holographic data, the smallest package from which the full
correspondence can be reconstructed.

\subsection*{12.1.\enspace The holographic modular Koszul datum}

Every three-dimensional holomorphic-topological system~$T$ is
controlled by a \emph{holographic modular Koszul datum}
\[
\mathcal H(T)
\;=\;
\bigl(\cA,\;\cA^!,\;\cC,\;r(z),\;\Theta_\cA,\;\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}}\bigr),
\]
defined as follows.
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
\item $\cA$: the \emph{boundary chiral algebra}, a chiral algebra
  on a complex curve $X$.  It is the algebra of boundary local
  operators of~$T$ restricted to the holomorphic boundary
  $\{0\}\times X\subset\mathbb R_+\times X$.
\item $\cA^!$: the \emph{strict chiral Koszul dual} of~$\cA$, obtained by
  linear duality of bar cohomology:
  $\cA^!=(\cA^{\mathrm i})^\vee$ where
  $\cA^{\mathrm i}=H^*(\barB(\cA))$.  In the holographic setting,
  $\cA^!$ is a \emph{dg-shifted Yangian}.  The bar complex
  $\barB(A_b)$ is an algebra over the two-coloured
  Swiss-cheese operad $\SCchtop$: chiral on the closed colour,
  $E_1$ on the open colour.  The Koszul dual $\cA^!$ is the
  $E_1$-projection of the $\SCchtop$-dual; it carries an
  $E_1$-algebra structure from the topological direction.
\item $\cC\simeq\cA^!\text{-}\mathsf{mod}$: the \emph{line-operator
  category}, a braided tensor category.  Objects are line defects
  of~$T$ (topological lines in $\mathbb R_+$); morphisms are
  junction operators; the braiding comes from crossing in the
  holomorphic plane.
\item $r(z)\in\cA^!\otimes\cA^!((\!( z^{-1})\!))$: the
  \emph{dg-shifted Yangian $R$-matrix}, a meromorphic endomorphism
  with a pole at $z=0$.  It satisfies the classical Yang--Baxter
  equation
  \[
  [r_{12}(z_1{-}z_2),\,r_{13}(z_1{-}z_3)]
  +[r_{12}(z_1{-}z_2),\,r_{23}(z_2{-}z_3)]
  +[r_{13}(z_1{-}z_3),\,r_{23}(z_2{-}z_3)]
  \;=\;0.
  \]
  The $R$-matrix is the binary genus-$0$ shadow of~$\Theta_\cA$:
  \[
  r(z)\;=\;\operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}(\Theta_\cA).
  \]
\item $\Theta_\cA\in\operatorname{MC}(\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{mod}}_\cA)$:
  the \emph{universal Maurer--Cartan element} of the modular
  convolution $L_\infty$-algebra, existing unconditionally by the
  bar-intrinsic construction $\Theta_\cA:=D_\cA-d_0$.  All lower
  structures ($\kappa$, $r(z)$, the shadow connection) are
  projections of $\Theta_\cA$ to specific genus and arity components.
\item $\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}}_{g,n}=d-\operatorname{Sh}_{g,n}(\Theta_\cA)$:
  the \emph{modular shadow connection}, a connection on the modular
  shadow bundle over $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$.  Flatness of
  $\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}}$:
  \[
  (\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}}_{g,n})^2
  \;=\;
  d\operatorname{Sh}_{g,n}(\Theta_\cA)
  +\tfrac12[\operatorname{Sh}_{g,n}(\Theta_\cA),
  \operatorname{Sh}_{g,n}(\Theta_\cA)]
  \;=\;0
  \]
  is the MC equation projected to genus~$g$ and arity~$n$.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{12.2.\enspace The collision filtration}

The modular convolution algebra $\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{mod}}_\cA$
carries a \emph{collision filtration}
$F^0_{\mathrm{coll}}\supset F^1_{\mathrm{coll}}\supset\cdots$
indexed by the minimum pairwise distance on
$\operatorname{FM}_n(\mathbb C)$: depth~$0$ is the
free-propagation regime (all points well-separated), depth~$1$ is
the first collision stratum (one pairwise collision), depth~$k$
is the $k$-fold nested collision locus (a sequence of $k$ nested
screens in the FM compactification).

The associated spectral sequence has
\[
E_1^{p,*}
\;=\;
H^*\!\bigl(\operatorname{gr}_{\mathrm{coll}}^p\,
\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{mod}}_\cA,\;d_0\bigr),
\]
with $E_1^{0,*}$ the free-field contribution (no collisions,
$d_0$ the free differential) and $E_1^{1,*}$ the collision
residues (single pairwise collisions, extracting the leading
OPE singularity).  The first differentials $d_1\colon
E_1^{p,*}\to E_1^{p+1,*}$ are Arnold-type cancellations: the
Arnold relation on $\operatorname{FM}_3(\mathbb C)$ forces
$d_1^2=0$ on the $E_1$~page.  The spectral sequence converges
to $H^*(\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{mod}}_\cA)$, with the collapse at
the $E_r$~page governed by the shadow depth: for
class-$\mathbf{G}$ algebras (depth~$2$), the spectral sequence
collapses at $E_2$; for class-$\mathbf{M}$ algebras
(depth~$\infty$), it does not collapse at any finite page.

\subsection*{12.3.\enspace Four proved recovery theorems}

The collision filtration recovers four structures from $\Theta_\cA$.

\medskip
\noindent\emph{(R1) Collision residue = twisting.}
The depth-$1$ collision stratum at arity~$2$ extracts the binary
shadow:
\[
\operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}(\Theta_\cA)
\;=\;\pi_\cA,
\]
the universal twisting morphism producing the
dg-shifted Yangian $r_\cA(z)$.  The collision
residue extracts the leading OPE pole
$a_{(0)}b/(z_1-z_2)$; the MC equation at this depth is the
twisting morphism equation
$\partial\pi+\pi\star\pi=0$.

\medskip
\noindent\emph{(R2) CYBE from Arnold.}
The three boundary divisors of $\overline M_{0,4}$ correspond
to the three channels $(12|34)$, $(13|24)$, $(14|23)$.  Evaluating
the Arnold relation $\eta_{12}\wedge\eta_{23}+\eta_{23}\wedge\eta_{31}
+\eta_{31}\wedge\eta_{12}=0$ on the Casimir tensor
$\Omega\otimes\Omega\in(\cA^!)^{\otimes 3}$ produces the three
terms of the CYBE:
\[
[r_{12}(z_{12}),\,r_{13}(z_{13})]
\;+\;
[r_{12}(z_{12}),\,r_{23}(z_{23})]
\;+\;
[r_{13}(z_{13}),\,r_{23}(z_{23})]
\;=\;0,
\]
where $z_{ij}=z_i-z_j$.  Each bracket corresponds to a boundary
divisor, and the Arnold relation is the vanishing of the boundary
integral.

\medskip
\noindent\emph{(R3) Affine shadow/KZ comparison on the affine comparison surface.}
For the affine algebra $\cA=\widehat{\fg}_k$, on the affine
Kac--Moody comparison surface the genus-$0$
shadow one-form at arity~$n$ is the Knizhnik--Zamolodchikov connection
form:
\[
\operatorname{Sh}_{0,n}(\Theta_{\widehat{\fg}_k})
\;=\;
\sum_{i<j}r_{ij}(z_i{-}z_j)\,d\log(z_i{-}z_j)
\;=\;
\frac{1}{h^\vee+k}\sum_{i<j}\frac{\Omega_{ij}\,dz_{ij}}{z_{ij}}\,,
\]
where $r_{ij}$ denotes the propagator-weighted Casimir
$\Omega_{ij}/(h^\vee{+}k)$, not the spectral $r$-matrix.
Flatness of $\nabla_{\mathrm{KZ}}=d-\operatorname{Sh}_{0,n}$
is the MC equation at genus~$0$ and arity~$n$.  For
$\cA=\operatorname{Vir}_c$, on the Virasoro degenerate-module
comparison surface the analogous Virasoro conformal Ward extraction,
together with higher collision residues, yields the
BPZ differential equations.  The affine Drinfeld--Kohno theorem
compares the braid-group monodromy of the genus-$0$ shadow of
$\Theta_{\widehat{\fg}_k}$ with the corresponding quantum-group
representation category.

\medskip
\noindent\emph{(R4) Quartic = $L_\infty$ obstruction.}
The quartic resonance class
\[
[\mathfrak R^{\mathrm{mod}}_4(\cA)]
\;=\;
[o_4(\cA)]
\;\in\;
H^2\!\bigl(\cA^{\mathrm{sh}}_{4,0}\bigr)
\]
is the obstruction to extending the Yangian seed $r(z)$ from
arity~$2$ to arity~$4$.  It
vanishes for classes $\mathbf{G}$, $\mathbf{L}$,
$\mathbf{C}$ (the $R$-matrix
extends to all arities) and is nonzero for class~$\mathbf{M}$
(the nonlinear OPE forces a genuine
quartic obstruction:
$Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\operatorname{Vir}}=10/[c(5c+22)]$).

\subsection*{12.4.\enspace Five conjectural theorem targets}

\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
\item \emph{Boundary-defect realization.}
  The boundary chiral algebra $\cA_\partial(T)$ and its Koszul
  dual $\cA^!_\partial(T)$ are the two algebras appearing in the
  holographic datum for every 3d HT system~$T$, with
  $\cC\simeq\cA^!\text{-mod}$ as braided tensor category of line
  operators.  The physical content: boundary local operators and
  bulk-to-boundary maps determine the full holographic datum up
  to quasi-isomorphism.

\item \emph{Yangian-shadow.}
  In full derived generality: for every HT system~$T$, the
  collision residue
  $\operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}(\Theta_\cA)$ recovers
  the dg-shifted Yangian $r(z)$ attached to~$T$, not merely at
  the classical level but at the chain level, including all
  higher homotopies of the $A_\infty$ structure.

\item \emph{Sphere reconstruction.}
  The Gaiotto--Zhang (2026) commuting differentials on the
  non-planar sphere algebra are the scalar shadow
  $\operatorname{Sh}_{0,n}(\Theta_\cA)$: the 2026 sphere algebra
  is the binary genus-$0$ shadow of the modular MC class.  The
  $n$-point sphere amplitude
  $\langle\cO_1(z_1)\cdots\cO_n(z_n)\rangle_{S^2}$ is, on the
  established genus-$0$ comparison surfaces, a flat section of
  $\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}}_{0,n}$.

\item \emph{Quartic resonance obstruction.}
  The quartic resonance class $\mathfrak R^{\mathrm{mod}}_4$, the
  first global nonlinear invariant, is
  the first test of the modular datum beyond the spectral
  determinant: its non-vanishing for class-$\mathbf{M}$ algebras
  is the quantitative obstruction to planarity of the holographic
  system, measuring the failure of the large-$N$ expansion to
  truncate at tree level.

\item \emph{Singular-fiber descent.}
  At degenerate complex structure (boundary of
  $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$), the modular datum degenerates to the
  boundary of the Mok compactification:
  $\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}}|_{\partial\overline{\cM}}\sim
  \nabla^{\mathrm{clutch}}$ with residues controlled by the
  clutching law of~$\Theta_\cA$.  The clutching law:
  $\Theta_\cA|_{\sigma_\Gamma}=\prod_{v\in V(\Gamma)}\Theta_v
  \cdot\prod_{e\in E(\Gamma)}P_e$, where $\sigma_\Gamma$
  is a boundary stratum of $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$ labelled by
  a stable graph~$\Gamma$, $\Theta_v$ is the vertex MC element,
  and $P_e$ is the edge propagator.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{12.5.\enspace The colored modular deformation object}

A holomorphic-topological theory~$T$ produces three observation
algebras:
\[
\mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{hol}}\;(\text{bulk}),
\qquad
\mathrm{Obs}^\partial\;(\text{boundary}),
\qquad
\mathrm{Obs}^\ell\;(\text{line}).
\]
The colored Swiss-cheese FM space
$\operatorname{FM}^{\log}_{\bullet,\mathrm{SC}}$ encodes the
collision geometry of all three simultaneously: bulk points in
$\mathbb C$, boundary points on $\mathbb R\subset\mathbb C$, and
line points on individual copies of $\mathbb R_+$.  The
three-color modular deformation object is
\[
\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{HT,log}}_{\mathrm{mod}}
\;=\;
\operatorname{hom}^{\alpha_{\mathrm{HT}}}\!\bigl(
C_\bullet(\operatorname{FM}^{\log}_{\bullet,\mathrm{SC}}),\;
\operatorname{End}_{\mathrm{Ch}_\infty}(
\mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{hol}}_\infty,\,
\mathrm{Obs}^\partial_\infty,\,
\mathrm{Obs}^\ell_\infty)
\bigr),
\]
the convolution $sL_\infty$-algebra between the chains on the
colored log-FM space and the endomorphism operad of the three
observation algebras.  The three colors interact through the
Swiss-cheese operadic structure: bulk fields propagate to the
boundary (closed-to-open maps), boundary fields propagate to
lines (open-to-open composition), and lines cannot produce bulk
fields (the $\varnothing$-prohibition of $\mathsf{SC}$).

The modular effective action is the graph-sum
\[
S^{\mathrm{mod}}_{\mathrm{HT}}
\;=\;
\sum_{\Gamma\in\mathsf{StGraph}_{\mathrm{SC}}}
\frac{\hbar^{b_1(\Gamma)}}{|\operatorname{Aut}(\Gamma)|}
\,W^{\log}_\Gamma\,O_\Gamma\,,
\]
where the sum is over connected stable graphs $\Gamma$ decorated by
the three colors, $b_1(\Gamma)$ is the first Betti number,
$W^{\log}_\Gamma$ is the Feynman weight (a period integral on the
log-FM stratum $\sigma_\Gamma$), and $O_\Gamma$ is the vertex
operator (the tensor product of observation-algebra elements at
each vertex).  The BV quantum master equation
\[
\bigl(d_{\mathrm{BV}}+\hbar\Delta_{\mathrm{odd}}\bigr)
\exp\!\bigl(S^{\mathrm{mod}}_{\mathrm{HT}}/\hbar\bigr)
\;=\;0
\]
is the single equation governing the 3d HT system~$T$.  At
genus~$0$ ($\hbar^0$): the classical BV master equation
$\{S_0,S_0\}=0$.  At genus~$1$ ($\hbar^1$): the one-loop anomaly
cancellation $\Delta_{\mathrm{odd}}S_0+\{S_0,S_1\}=0$.  At
genus~$g$ ($\hbar^g$): the $g$-loop Ward identity.

\subsection*{12.6.\enspace The Khan--Zeng bridge}

Khan and Zeng construct a three-dimensional holomorphic-topological
Poisson sigma model on the half-space
$\mathbb R_+\times\mathbb C$ attached to a freely generated PVA.
The field content: a $\fg$-valued $(0,1)$-form $A_{\bar z}$
on~$\mathbb C$, a $\fg^*$-valued scalar $\phi$, and a
$\fg$-valued $1$-form $\eta$ along~$\mathbb R_+$.  The action is
\[
S_{\mathrm{KZ}}
\;=\;
\int_{\mathbb R_+\times\mathbb C}
\bigl(\langle\phi,\,\bar\partial A\rangle
+\langle\phi,\,\tfrac12\{A_\lambda A\}|_{\lambda=0}\rangle
+\langle\eta,\,d_t\phi\rangle\bigr)\,
dt\wedge dz\wedge d\bar z.
\]
The results:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
\item Gauge invariance of $S_{\mathrm{KZ}}$ holds if and only if
  the $\lambda$-bracket $\{-_\lambda-\}$ satisfies the PVA Jacobi
  identity.  The gauge algebra is the Lie conformal algebra
  underlying the PVA.
\item A Virasoro element $T$ in the PVA upgrades the symmetry:
  the stress tensor provides a coupling to worldsheet gravity,
  promoting holomorphic-topological to fully topological
  (diffeomorphism-invariant on the boundary $\{0\}\times\mathbb C$).
\item The boundary theory on $\{0\}\times\mathbb C$ carries a
  $(-1)$-shifted Poisson bracket $\{-,-\}_{-1}$ and produces the
  genus-zero quantization problem: deforming $\{-,-\}_{-1}$ to
  a differential $Q=Q_0+\hbar Q_1+\cdots$ with $Q^2=0$.
\item The modular extension, coupling the bulk theory to stable
  curves at genus $g\ge 1$ via the fibration
  $\cC_g\to\overline{\cM}_g$, controls the full genus tower of
  the quantum Koszul datum.
\end{enumerate}
The deformation-quantization pipeline:
\[
\text{classical coisson shadow}
\;\xrightarrow{\;\text{KZ quantization}\;}\;
\text{genus-$0$ quantum Koszul}
\;\xrightarrow{\;\text{modular lift}\;}\;
\mathcal H(T).
\]
The first arrow is perturbative quantization of the Khan--Zeng
action on $\mathbb P^1$ (tree-level Feynman diagrams).  The
second arrow is the genus-by-genus obstruction theory of
\S\S10--11, extending the genus-$0$ MC element across the genus
filtration.

The bridge is completed in Volume~II by the \emph{doubling
theorem}: the half-space BV problem for any logarithmic
$\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$-algebra embeds into the doubled
whole-space via the method of images, and the reflected weight
identity, the condition for the boundary algebra to be a vertex
algebra, is the $\sigma$-invariant restriction of the standard
Stokes identity on the doubled Fulton--MacPherson compactification.
The affine Poisson--vertex sigma model satisfies the hypotheses of
the physics bridge theorem (BV data, one-loop finiteness, polynomial
interactions), so it is a logarithmic
$\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$-algebra; Drinfeld--Sokolov
reduction preserves this structure.  The entire standard
landscape (Kac--Moody, Virasoro, $\mathcal W_N$) enters through
these two gates.  The six-component holographic datum
\[
\bigl(B_\partial,\;B_\partial^!,\;\cC_{\mathrm{line}},\;r(z),\;
\Theta_{B_\partial},\;\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}}\bigr)
\]
exists and is consistent for every logarithmic
$\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$-algebra: bulk $\simeq$ derived center
of boundary, line operators $\simeq$ Koszul-dual modules, spectral
$R$-matrix from the Laplace-transformed $\lambda$-bracket.

The genus expansion of the modular bar differential,
$D = \sum_{g \ge 0}\hbar^g D^{(g)}$ with
$D^{(g)} = \sum_{\Gamma:\,g(\Gamma)=g}|\Aut(\Gamma)|^{-1}D_\Gamma$,
is the Feynman transform of the modular operad; the canonical MC
element $\delta_\cA = D - D^{(0)}$ computes the positive-genus
corrections.  The combinatorial structure (stable graphs,
automorphism weights, genus bookkeeping) is the mathematical shadow
of the 't~Hooft expansion.  The identification $\hbar
\leftrightarrow 1/N$ for a specific holographic model remains the
principal open bridge from the algebraic machine to gauge-theory
holography.

\subsection*{12.7.\enspace The Heisenberg holographic datum}

The base case: shadow class~$\mathbf G$, depth~$2$, trivial line-operator
category, scalar $R$-matrix.
For $\cA=\mathcal H_k$:
\begin{align*}
\cA&=\mathcal H_k,
&\cA^!&=\mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^*),
&\cC&=\mathsf{Vect},\\[4pt]
r(z)&=k/z,
&R(z)&=\exp(k/z),
&\Theta_{\mathcal H_k}&=k\cdot\eta\otimes\Lambda.
\end{align*}
The shadow connection is trivial:
$\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}}_{g,n}=d$ for all $(g,n)$, because the MC
element is scalar (it lives in the one-dimensional space
$\mathbb C\cdot\eta\otimes\Lambda$, and the shadow
$\operatorname{Sh}_{g,n}(\Theta_{\mathcal H_k})$ is a scalar
multiple of the identity, producing a trivial connection).

All five conjectural targets are trivially verified:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),nosep]
\item The boundary algebra $\mathcal H_k$ is free
  (one generator, no nonlinear OPE).
\item The Koszul dual $\mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^*)$
  is the curved symmetric chiral algebra with curvature
  $m_0 = -k\omega$
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:frame-heisenberg-koszul-dual};
  note: $\cH_k^! \neq \cH_{-k}$).
\item The line-operator category is $\mathsf{Vect}$: no
  nontrivial lines (the $R$-matrix is scalar, so the braiding
  is symmetric, and $\cH_k^!$-modules over $\mathsf{Vect}$
  are just vector spaces).
\item The quartic obstruction vanishes: shadow class~$\mathbf{G}$,
  $o_4(\mathcal H_k)=0$.
\item Singular-fiber descent is trivial: $\Theta_{\mathcal H_k}$
  has no dependence on moduli.
\end{enumerate}


\subsection*{12.8.\enspace The affine $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$ holographic datum}

The first nontrivial
holographic example: class~$\mathbf L$,
depth~$3$, $r(z)=\Omega/z$ (Yang's solution of the CYBE), line-operator category $Y(\mathfrak{sl}_2)\text{-mod}$.
The braiding is nonsymmetric, the shadow connection is KZ,
and quantum-group representation theory emerges from
genus-$0$ monodromy.

The Koszul dual is
$\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2{}_{-k-4}$ (Feigin--Frenkel involution).  The holographic datum is 3d Chern--Simons at level~$k$;
Drinfeld--Kohno (KZ monodromy = quantum-group braiding) follows from the genus-$0$ shadow
connection.

The datum ($3$d Chern--Simons at level~$k$):
\[
\mathcal H(\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2{}_k)
\;=\;
\Bigl(
\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2{}_k,\;
\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2{}_{-k-4},\;
\mathcal O_q^{\mathrm{sh}},\;
\frac{\Omega}{z},\;
\Theta_k,\;
d-\kappa_k\,\omega_g
\Bigr),
\]
$r(z)=\Omega/z$ (Casimir), $q=e^{i\pi/(k+2)}$,
$\kappa_k=3(k+2)/4$.
At $k=-2$: $\kappa=0$ (uncurved), the center
$\mathfrak z(\widehat{\mathfrak g}_{-h^\vee})$ is the
Feigin--Frenkel algebra of $\mathfrak{sl}_2$-opers.
The monodromy of the KZ connection
$\nabla_{\mathrm{KZ}} = d - \hbar\,\Omega/z$
(with $\hbar = 1/(k{+}2)$)
is compared with the quantum-group $R$-matrix of
$U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ by the affine Drinfeld--Kohno package;
on the reduced evaluation comparison surface,
$\cC_{\mathrm{line}}^{\mathrm{red}}|_{\mathrm{eval}}$ is
identified with the corresponding quantum-group side
(Volume~II), and the colored Jones
polynomial is recovered from the monodromy representation classified by the bar complex, the Steinberg convolution of the chiral
self-intersection on $\operatorname{FM}_k(\mathbb C)$.

\subsection*{12.9.\enspace The Virasoro holographic datum}

The Virasoro algebra is the first example of shadow
class~$\mathbf M$ (mixed, infinite depth): the $R$-matrix
$r_c(z) = (c/2)/z^3 + 2T/z$ has both a third-order pole
(gravitational) and a first-order pole (stress-tensor exchange),
and the quartic contact invariant
$Q^{\mathrm{contact}} = 10/[c(5c+22)]$ is nonzero.  The
holographic datum packages three-dimensional quantum gravity on the
half-space $\mathbb R_+ \times \mathbb C$: the Koszul dual is
$\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$ (self-dual at $c=13$, not $c=26$), the
shadow connection carries curvature proportional to
$\kappa_c = c/2$, and the transferred coproduct is strictly
primitive at all arities: gravity does not produce particles,
only braids them.

\medskip\noindent
\emph{Virasoro at central charge~$c$}
($3$d gravity on $\mathbb R_+\times\mathbb C$):
\begin{align*}
\mathcal H(\mathrm{Vir}_c)
&\;=\;
\Bigl(
\mathrm{Vir}_c,\;
\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c},\;
\cC_c,\;
r_c(z),\;
\Theta_c,\;
\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}}_c
\Bigr),\\[6pt]
r_c(z)
&\;=\;
\frac{c/2}{z^3}+\frac{2T}{z}\,,
\qquad
\kappa_c\;=\;\frac{c}{2}\,,\\[4pt]
\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}}_{1,1}
&\;=\;
d-\kappa_c\,\omega_1
-\frac{10}{c(5c+22)}\,\delta_4
-\cdots\,.
\end{align*}
The shadow connection has curvature $\kappa_c\,\omega_g$
at leading order.  The quartic contact correction
$\mathfrak Q=10/[c(5c+22)]$ is the first term sensitive to
the planted-forest boundary of $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$.
The genus tower has the formal structure of a
perturbative expansion of $3$d quantum gravity.
The transferred coproduct $\Delta_z^{\mathrm{Vir}}$ is strictly
primitive at all arities
(Principle~\ref{princ:gravitational-primitivity}): the
ghost-number obstruction intrinsic to DS reduction kills every
HPL tree correction.  All gravitational dynamics resides in
the collision residue $r_c(z) = (c/2)/z^3 + 2T/z$ and the
infinite $\Ainf$ product tower; the coproduct channel is
identically zero.  Gravity does not produce particles, only
braids them.

\subsection*{12.10.\enspace The M2 brane example}

The first genuinely interacting holographic
example: boundary algebra $\mathcal W_{1+\infty}$
(infinitely many generators), Koszul dual a dg-shifted
Yangian for $\mathfrak{psl}(2|2)$,
line-operator category a quantum affine superalgebra.  All three
genus-$2$ shells are active, with the
planted-forest shell receiving its
first nontrivial contribution from Mok's log-FM strata.

The system arises from
3d $\cN=4$ ADHM gauge theory: $N$ M2 branes probing
$\mathbb C^2/\mathbb Z_k$.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The boundary algebra.}
The boundary chiral algebra $\cA_{M2,N}$ at finite~$N$ is the VOA
of the 3d $\cN=4$ theory on $\mathbb R_+\times\mathbb C$.  At
large~$N$, the boundary VOA $\cA_{M2,\infty}$ is a $\mathcal W$-algebra
of type $\mathcal W_{1+\infty}[c]$ at $c\sim N$: it has infinitely
many strong generators of weights $1,2,3,\dots$, with OPE
coefficients that are rational functions of~$N$.

The OPE structure contains both simple and higher poles.  The
stress tensor $T$ (weight~$2$) has the Virasoro OPE with
$c=c(N)$; the weight-$3$ primary~$W$ has a nonlinear $WW$ OPE
involving the quasi-primary $\Lambda={:}TT{:}-\frac{3}{10}\partial^2T$
at order $(z-w)^{-2}$; and the weight-$s$ generators for $s\ge 4$
produce nested composites that make the shadow obstruction tower infinite.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The Koszul dual.}
The chiral Koszul dual $\cA^!_{M2,\infty}$ is a dg-shifted Yangian
for the Lie superalgebra $\mathfrak{psl}(2|2)$:
\[
\cA^!_{M2,\infty}
\;\simeq\;
Y^{\mathrm{dg}}_{\hbar}(\mathfrak{psl}(2|2)).
\]
The $R$-matrix
$R_{M2}(z)\in Y^{\mathrm{dg}}_\hbar(\mathfrak{psl}(2|2))
\otimes Y^{\mathrm{dg}}_\hbar(\mathfrak{psl}(2|2))[[z^{-1}]]$
is the collision residue
$R_{M2}(z)=\operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}(\Theta_{M2})$.
The classical $r$-matrix $r_{M2}(z)=\Omega_{\mathfrak{psl}(2|2)}/z$
satisfies the classical Yang--Baxter equation, which is the Arnold
relation on $\operatorname{FM}_3(\mathbb C)$ evaluated on the
$\mathfrak{psl}(2|2)$-Casimir.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The line-operator category.}
\[
\cC_{M2}
\;\simeq\;
\operatorname{Rep}\!\bigl(
U_q(\widehat{\mathfrak{psl}}(2|2))
\bigr),
\]
where $q=e^{2\pi i/(k+2)}$.  The line operators are modules for the
quantum affine superalgebra.  The spectral braiding
$R_{M2}(z)\colon L_1\otimes L_2\xrightarrow{\sim}L_2\otimes L_1$
on pairs of line operators satisfies the Yang--Baxter equation:
Stokes' theorem on $\operatorname{FM}_3(\mathbb C)$ decomposes
the boundary into three collision divisors, one for each crossing
in the YBE.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The holographic datum.}
The full six-component holographic modular Koszul datum is:
\begin{align*}
\cA &= \cA_{M2,\infty}\;(\text{boundary }\mathcal W_{1+\infty}),
&\cA^! &= Y^{\mathrm{dg}}_\hbar(\mathfrak{psl}(2|2)),\\[3pt]
\cC &= \operatorname{Rep}(U_q(\widehat{\mathfrak{psl}}(2|2))),
&r(z) &= \Omega_{\mathfrak{psl}(2|2)}/z,\\[3pt]
\Theta_{M2} &= \sum_\Gamma
  \frac{W^{\log\mathrm{FM}}_\Gamma}{|\operatorname{Aut}(\Gamma)|}
  \otimes\Phi^{M2}_\Gamma,
&\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}}_{g,n} &= d-\operatorname{Sh}_{g,n}(\Theta_{M2}).
\end{align*}

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Shadow obstruction tower analysis.}
The MC element $\Theta_{M2}$ has infinite shadow depth
(class~$\mathbf M$: mixed modular):
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item The cubic shadow $\mathfrak C_{M2}\neq 0$ because
  $\cA_{M2,\infty}$ has a nonabelian current subalgebra.
\item The quartic contact shadow
  $Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{M2}\neq 0$ because
  ${:}TT{:}-\frac{3}{10}\partial^2 T$ appears in the $WW$~OPE
  with coefficient $16/(22+5c(N))$.
\item The quintic obstruction
  $o^{(5)}_{M2}=\{\mathfrak C_{M2},Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{M2}\}_H
  \neq 0$: the tower is infinite.
\end{itemize}
At genus~$2$, all three shells contribute:
$\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{loop}\circ\mathrm{loop}}\neq 0$,
$\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{sep}\circ\mathrm{loop}}\neq 0$,
$\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{pf}}\neq 0$.  The planted-forest shell
$\Theta^{(2)}_{\mathrm{pf}}$ is the first contribution from Mok's
log-FM strata to the holographic genus expansion.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The modular shadow connection.}
The shadow connection
$\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}}_{g,n}=d-\operatorname{Sh}_{g,n}(\Theta_{M2})$
is nontrivial: the shadow $\operatorname{Sh}_{g,n}$ is a
matrix-valued $(g,n)$-dependent differential operator on the
moduli space, encoding the genus-by-genus quantum corrections to
the holographic correspondence.  The genus-$0$ arity-$n$ shadow
$\operatorname{Sh}_{0,n}(\Theta_{M2})$ has the expected
KZ/BPZ-type leading behavior for the $\mathfrak{psl}(2|2)$
benchmark surface; the genus-$1$ shadow
carries the one-loop anomaly $\kappa(\cA_{M2,\infty})\cdot\omega_1$;
higher-genus shadows encode the multi-loop holographic amplitudes.

The quartic contact invariant $Q^{\mathrm{contact}}_{M2}$
is the first obstruction to planarity in the holographic genus
expansion: it is the first invariant that distinguishes the
full string-theoretic amplitude from its planar ($N\to\infty$)
limit.  The modular Koszul datum $\mathcal H(M2)$ packages the
complete holographic correspondence (boundary algebra, bulk
reconstruction, line operators, braiding, genus tower, and
anomaly cancellation) into a single MC problem.

\bigskip
\noindent
\emph{Summary.}\enspace
Sections~1--2 constructed the bar complex and its genus tower from
the logarithmic propagator and the Arnold relation.
Sections~3--4 identified these as projections of a single chain-level
object: the modular convolution $L_\infty$-algebra and its
universal MC element~$\Theta_\cA$.
Sections~5--6 extracted the full hierarchy of characteristic
invariants from~$\Theta_\cA$ and classified chiral algebras by
shadow depth.
Section~7 tested the machine on every standard family.
Section~8 lifted the shadow obstruction tower into number theory: Dirichlet--sewing
series, Euler--Koszul classification, the two-variable $L$-object, and
the arithmetic packet connection.
Section~9 proved one-channel line concentration on the
simple-Lie-symmetry locus, the scalar package on the proved scalar
lane, and assembled the Koszulness programme.
Sections~10--11 transported the machine to three dimensions:
the bar differential became holomorphic factorization, the coproduct
became topological factorization, and the pair became a
Swiss-cheese coalgebra whose PVA shadow governs the deformation
quantization of Poisson vertex algebras to vertex algebras.
Section~12 packaged the entire holographic correspondence into a
six-component modular Koszul datum controlled by a single MC equation.


% ====================================================================
\section*{13.\quad Completion and the frontier}
% ====================================================================

The holographic datum of Section~12 packages a chiral algebra, its Koszul dual, the line-operator
category, the spectral $R$-matrix, the universal MC element, and
the shadow connection into a single algebraic object.  The
frontier consists of structural questions the packaging
forces: the completed bar-cobar problem
by infinite-type algebras, the analytic sewing problem
by genus $g \ge 1$ curvature, the factorization-envelope
problem by the passage from Lie conformal input to
modular output, and the non-principal duality problem
by Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction.

\subsection*{13.1.\enspace The Maurer--Cartan frontier}

All five master conjectures are proved.  MC3 holds for all simple types on the evaluation-generated core via multiplicity-free $\ell$-weights (Theorem~\ref{thm:categorical-cg-all-types}, Corollary~\ref{cor:mc3-all-types}).  The residual problem DK-4/5 (extension beyond evaluation modules) is downstream.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{MC1} (PBW concentration).
For every standard family (Kac--Moody, Virasoro, principal
$\mathcal W_N$, $\beta\gamma$, lattice) and every genus
$g\ge 1$, the PBW spectral sequence for the genus-$g$ bar
complex has concentrated $E_\infty$ page:
$E_\infty^{p,q}(g)=0$ for $q\neq 0$.

The proof has two steps.  First, genus-$0$ Koszulness supplies
concentration of $E_1^{p,q}(g{=}0)$: the bar complex at genus~$0$
is formal, and the bar-cobar spectral sequence collapses at $E_2$
(this is the definition of chirally Koszul).  Second, the genus-$g$
enrichment $\cE^{p,q}_g$ from the Hodge bundle is
$d_0^{\mathrm{PBW}}$-exact because it arises from the regular
Eisenstein series, which is exact under the Poincar\'e residue map
$\operatorname{Res}\colon H^{q+1}(\overline{\cM}_{g,n},
\Omega^{q+1}_{\log})\to H^q(\sigma_\Gamma,\Omega^q_{\log})$.
The concentration is uniform in the level parameter~$k$: the PBW
filtration is independent of~$k$, and the spectral sequence
differentials are $k$-linear.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{MC2} (universal $\Theta_\cA$).
The bar-intrinsic construction:
\[
\Theta_\cA\;:=\;D_\cA-d_0
\;\in\;\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{mod}}_\cA
\]
is automatically MC because $D_\cA^2=0$ (the total bar
differential squares to zero).  The MC equation
$d_0\Theta_\cA+\tfrac12[\Theta_\cA,\Theta_\cA]=0$ unpacks to
$D_\cA^2-d_0^2=0$, which holds because both $D_\cA^2=0$
and $d_0^2=0$.

Scalar saturation universality: for every one-parameter algebraic
family $\cA_k$ with rational OPE coefficients,
\[
\Theta_{\cA_k}
\;=\;
\kappa(\cA_k)\cdot\eta_{\mathrm{univ}}\otimes\Lambda_{\mathrm{univ}}.
\]
The higher-order terms in
$H^2_{\mathrm{cyc,prim}}(\cA_k)$ vanish.  Proof: \emph{Whitehead
reduction} computes $H^2_{\mathrm{cyc,prim}}$ via a spectral
sequence whose $E_2$ page is
$H^2(\fg;\operatorname{Sym}^n V)=0$ by the Whitehead lemma for
reductive~$\fg$ (the second cohomology of a semisimple Lie algebra
with coefficients in a finite-dimensional module vanishes).
\emph{Algebraic semicontinuity}: the dimension function
$k\mapsto\dim H^2_{\mathrm{cyc,prim}}(\cA_k)$ is
upper-semicontinuous, vanishes at $k=\infty$ (the free-field
point), and therefore vanishes on a Zariski-dense open set
containing all non-critical levels including admissible ones.

Ambient $D^2=0$: the full differential on the ambient planted-forest
complex (including log-FM strata) satisfies $D^2=0$ by the
normal-crossings result of Mok: the log-FM compactification
$\operatorname{FM}_n(X|D)$ is a manifold with normal-crossings
boundary, and the differential respects the stratification.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{MC3} (thick generation).
On the type-$A$ Yangian module surface, the four-package MC3
problem reduces to a single remaining compact/completed extension
packet, by the following four steps.
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\alph*)]
\item \emph{Chromatic filtration.}  Stratify the category by
  the support of the $q$-character on the Grothendieck ring.
  The successive quotients $\operatorname{gr}^p_{\mathrm{chrom}}$
  are controlled by products of prefundamental modules at
  chromatic level~$p$.
\item \emph{Prefundamental Clebsch--Gordan.}  The tensor product
  $V_n\otimes L^-$ decomposes as
  $\bigoplus_{j=0}^n L^-(n-2j)$ at the character level, a
  formal series identity $\operatorname{ch}(V_n)\cdot
  \operatorname{ch}(L^-)=\sum_{j=0}^n\operatorname{ch}(L^-(n-2j))$,
  verified to arbitrary depth.  Every Verma character
  $\operatorname{ch}(M(\lambda))$ lies in the $K_0$-span of
  $\{[V_n]\cdot[L^-]\}$.
\item \emph{Completion formalism} (more precisely,
  Francis--Gaitsgory pro-nilpotent completion).  Evaluation
  modules are compact objects (finite composition series in
  $\mathcal{O}^{\mathrm{sh}}$), so once an equivalence on the
  relevant compact core is known, it extends to the corresponding
  ind-completion.
\item \emph{Remaining DK compact/completion packet.}  One still has
  to extend the Koszul duality functor from the evaluation-generated
  core to the compact shifted-prefundamental core, and then compare
  that compact-core equivalence with the relevant ind/pro-nilpotent
  completion.
\end{enumerate}
The CG decomposition part is extended to all simple types
(Theorem~\ref{thm:categorical-cg-all-types}): the multiplicity-free
$\ell$-weight property (Chari--Moura) replaces the minuscule
hypothesis, making the block-separation argument uniform across
all Dynkin types.  The remaining post-CG completion packets are
open beyond type~$A$ (Corollary~\ref{cor:mc3-all-types}).

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{MC4} (completed bar-cobar).
The \emph{strong completion-tower theorem}: the strong filtration
axiom
\[
\mu_r(F^{i_1},\ldots,F^{i_r})
\;\subset\;
F^{i_1+\cdots+i_r}
\]
yields an automatic \emph{arity cutoff}: the $r$-ary operation
maps $F^{i_1}\otimes\cdots\otimes F^{i_r}$ into
$F^{i_1+\cdots+i_r}$, so operations with sufficiently many inputs
land in arbitrarily deep filtration.  For a fixed filtration
degree~$N$, only finitely many arities $r\le N$ contribute to
the $F^N$-piece of the bar-cobar resolution.  This makes
continuity and the Mittag-Leffler condition automatic (no lim${}^1$
obstruction).

The \emph{completion closure}
$\operatorname{CompCl}(\cF_{\mathrm{ft}})$, the full subcategory
of complete filtered objects with finite-type associated graded,
carries a quasi-inverse bar-cobar homotopy equivalence.  The key
results:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),nosep]
\item \emph{Coefficient-stability criterion}: convergence of the
  completed bar-cobar reduces to finite matrix stabilisation on
  each graded piece.
\item \emph{MC twisting closure}: the completion closure is stable
  under MC twisting ($\Theta$-twisted objects remain in
  $\operatorname{CompCl}$).
\item \emph{Completed twisting representability}: twisting morphisms
  in the completed setting are representable by the completed
  bar-cobar resolution.
\item \emph{Uniform PBW bridge}: MC1 (PBW concentration) implies
  MC4 (completed bar-cobar) for all standard families via the
  uniform filtration.
\end{enumerate}

MC4 splits into two sub-problems:
\begin{itemize}
\item \emph{MC4${}^+$} (positive towers: $\mathcal W_{1+\infty}$,
  affine Yangians, RTT algebras): solved by weight stabilisation.
  The weight grading provides a natural Cauchy criterion, and the
  completed bar-cobar converges because the bar complex has
  bounded weight in each filtration degree.
\item \emph{MC4${}^0$} (resonant towers: Virasoro, non-quadratic
  $\mathcal W_N$): reduced to a finite resonance problem by the
  resonance-filtered bar-cobar theorem.  The \emph{resonance rank}
  $\rho(\cA)\in\mathbb Z_{\ge 0}\cup\{\infty\}$ measures the
  depth of the resonance: $\rho(\mathcal H_k)=0$,
  $\rho(\widehat{\fg}_k)=0$, $\rho(\beta\gamma)=0$,
  $\rho(\operatorname{Vir}_c)=1$ (the weight-$0$ subspace of the
  bar complex has a one-dimensional resonance at the zero-mode
  of~$L_0$).
\end{itemize}
The \emph{resonance completion theorem}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:platonic-completion}): every positive-energy
chiral algebra has $\rho<\infty$.  The Virasoro case:
$\operatorname{Vir}_{26-c}$ is the depth-zero resonance shadow, the
image of the finite-dimensional resonance truncation~$R_{\mathrm{Vir}}$,
not the final Koszul dual.  The genuine $\mathcal W_\infty$-type
dual requires the full resonance-filtered completion.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{MC5} (genus expansion).
Proved.  The algebraic genus tower is established together
with the analytic sewing package.  At genus~$0$, the critical-string
algebraic BRST/bar comparison is established, while the top-degree
amplitude pairing remains conditional; bar-cobar inversion
$\Omega(\barB(\cA))\xrightarrow{\sim}\cA$ is Theorem~B.  At genus~$1$,
the curved bar complex with
$d_{\mathrm{fib}}^2=\kappa\cdot\omega_1$ supplies the algebraic
one-loop package, and the complementarity splitting
$Q_1(\cA)\oplus Q_1(\cA^!)=H^*(\overline{\cM}_{1,n},Z(\cA))$
is the genus-$1$ modular-invariance constraint.

At genus $g\ge 2$ the resolution proceeds in five steps.
First, \emph{inductive genus determination}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:inductive-genus-determination}): the genus-$g$
component $\Theta^{(g)}_\cA$ is determined by
$\Theta^{(<g)}_\cA$ via the graph-sum recursion on
$\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$.  Second, \emph{2D convergence}
(Proposition~\ref{prop:2d-convergence}): there is no UV
renormalization on curves: the Feynman integrals
$W_\Gamma=\int_{\sigma_\Gamma}\omega_\Gamma$ converge absolutely
on each stratum $\sigma_\Gamma\subset\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$
without counterterm subtraction.  Third, the \emph{analytic-algebraic
comparison} (Theorem~\ref{thm:analytic-algebraic-comparison}):
$D^{\mathrm{an}}=D^{\mathrm{alg}}$ on the algebraic core, so the
formal graph-sum differential coincides with the analytic one.
Fourth, \emph{general HS-sewing}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:general-hs-sewing}): polynomial OPE growth
together with subexponential sector growth implies the
Hilbert--Schmidt sewing condition, yielding trace-class closed
amplitudes at every genus.  Fifth, the \emph{Heisenberg one-particle
sewing theorem} (Theorem~\ref{thm:heisenberg-one-particle-sewing})
identifies the Heisenberg sewing amplitude with a Fredholm
determinant, providing the decisive first-case verification.
These results resolve the algebraic recursion and analytic convergence
lanes, but not the full genuswise BV/BRST/bar identification.
The correct receptacle remains the coderived category: curvature
at $g\ge 1$ forces coderived/contraderived passage, not ordinary
derived.


\medskip

\noindent\textbf{The completion programme: $q$-windows and completion entropy.}\enspace
The principal $\mathcal{W}_N$-algebra has $N-1$ generators.  The inverse
limit $\mathcal{W}_\infty = \varprojlim_N \mathcal{W}_N$ has
infinitely many, one in each conformal weight $2, 3, 4, \ldots$

The bar-cobar quasi-isomorphism $\Omega(\barB(\cA)) \xrightarrow{\sim} \cA$
is proved for each finite-type stage $\mathcal{W}_N$.  The passage
to the inverse limit requires completed bar-cobar: a filtration
$F^0\cA \supset F^1\cA \supset \cdots$ that makes the bar
differential continuous and the Mittag--Leffler condition
automatic.  The strong filtration axiom
$\mu_r(F^{i_1},\dots,F^{i_r}) \subset F^{i_1+\cdots+i_r}$
achieves this in one stroke: on each quotient $\cA_{\le N}$ only
arities $r \le N$ survive, so the completed differential is
quotientwise finite and the quasi-isomorphism passes to the limit
(Theorem~\ref{thm:completed-bar-cobar-strong}).  The completion
closure $\CompCl(\cF_{\mathrm{ft}})$, the class of all such
inverse limits, carries a quasi-inverse bar-cobar equivalence
stable under Maurer--Cartan twisting.

The completed bar complex decomposes into \emph{finite windows}.
Define the \emph{reduced weight} $\rho(a) := \mathrm{wt}(a) - 1$
for a field of conformal weight $\mathrm{wt}(a)$, and extend
additively to bar words: $\rho(sa_1|\cdots|sa_\ell) = \sum_i
\rho(a_i)$.  The \emph{$q$-window} $K_q(\cA)$ is the span of
bar words of reduced weight $\le q$.

For Virasoro at $q = 2$: the window $K_2(\mathrm{Vir})$ has
basis $\{sT,\; sT|sT\}$, one letter of reduced weight~$1$ and
one two-letter word of total reduced weight~$2$.  The bar
differential on this two-dimensional complex is
$d(sT|sT) = s(T \cdot T)$.  The product $T \cdot T$ decomposes
into the quasi-primary composite $\Lambda = :(TT): -
\tfrac{3}{10}\partial^2 T$, derivatives $\partial^2 T$, and the
central term $\tfrac{c}{2}\cdot\mathbf{1}$.  But $\Lambda$ has
conformal weight~$4$ (reduced weight~$3 > 2$) and $\partial^2 T$
has reduced weight~$3 > 2$, so both project to zero in $K_2$.
Only the central term survives:
\[
d(sT|sT)\big|_{K_2} \;=\; \frac{c}{2}\cdot s\mathbf{1}.
\]
This is $\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) = c/2$ emerging from a
$2 \times 1$ matrix computation.  The curvature is not an abstract
scalar extracted from a theorem; it is the sole surviving
coefficient of the bar differential on the smallest nontrivial
window.

Each window $K_q(\cA)$ depends only on fields of conformal
weight $\le q+1$: a letter in the window has $\mathrm{wt}(a) \le
q+1$, and the bar differential cannot create higher-weight letters
because the OPE estimate
$\mathrm{wt}\,\mu_r(a_1,\ldots,a_r) \le
\sum_i\mathrm{wt}(a_i) - (r-1)$ prevents weight increase.  For the
$\mathcal{W}_N$ tower, $K_q(\mathcal{W}_N)$ stabilises at
$N = q + 1$: the infinite-generator problem is killed exactly, one
window at a time.

The window dimensions grow exponentially.  Define the
\emph{completion entropy} $h_K(\cA) := \log(\rho_\cA^{-1})$,
where $\rho_\cA$ is the radius of convergence of the
primitive generating series
$G_\cA(t) = \tfrac{1-t}{t}(\chi_\cA(t) - 1)$ extracted
from the vacuum character~$\chi_\cA(q)=\mathrm{tr}_\cA(q^{L_0})$
(the graded trace of the Virasoro zero mode).  The entropy
measures kinematic completion complexity: it depends on the
character alone, not on OPE coefficients or curvature.  Its values
form the monotone ladder
\[
h_K(\mathcal{W}_2) \approx 0.567
\;<\; h_K(\mathcal{W}_3) \approx 0.772
\;<\; h_K(\mathcal{W}_4) \approx 0.835
\;<\; \cdots
\;<\; h_K(\mathcal{W}_\infty) \approx 0.872,
\]
governed at the limit by the MacMahon plane-partition generating
function $\chi_{\mathcal{W}_\infty}(q) = \prod_{n \ge 2}(1 -
q^n)^{-(n-1)}$.

\subsection*{13.2.\enspace The analytic frontier}

Curvature forces this direction.  At genus $g \ge 1$ the bar
complex satisfies $d_{\mathrm{fib}}^2 = \kappa \cdot \omega_g
\neq 0$: the ordinary derived category is empty, and the correct
receptacle is the coderived category.  But the coderived passage
requires completed, Hilbert-space-valued structures, not the
bare algebraic OPE data of genus zero.  The analytic frontier asks:
when does the algebraic skeleton extend to a convergent sewing
amplitude?

The bare VOA is a dense algebraic skeleton.  The actual object for
partition functions and sewing is the \emph{sewing envelope}
$\cA^{\mathrm{sew}}$: the Hausdorff completion of~$\cA$ for the
topology defined by all-amplitude seminorms
\[
\|a\|_{\mathrm{amp}}
\;:=\;
\sup_{v\in\cV}\langle v,\pi(a)v\rangle
\]
over suitable families of states~$\cV$.  The algebraic OPE data
embeds densely in $\cA^{\mathrm{sew}}$; the closure provides the
convergent sewing amplitudes needed for genus $g\ge 1$.

The \emph{HS-sewing condition}: if the multiplication operators
$m^c_{a,b}$ are Hilbert--Schmidt in the sense that
\[
\sum_{a,b,c\ge 0}q^{a+b+c}\|m^c_{a,b}\|^2_{\mathrm{HS}}
\;<\;\infty
\]
for $|q|<1$, then the closed amplitudes
$\operatorname{Tr}(\pi(a)\cdot q^{L_0})$ are trace-class and
the sewing operation $\sum_n\langle v_n,\pi(a)w_n\rangle$ converges
absolutely.  The condition is a Hilbert--Schmidt bound on the
OPE coefficients graded by conformal weight.

The \emph{analytic bar coalgebra} $B^{\mathrm{an}}(\cA)$ is the
graph-norm closure of the algebraic bar coalgebra: each bar
element $s^{-1}a_1|\cdots|s^{-1}a_n$ is assigned the norm
$\prod_i\|a_i\|_{\mathrm{amp}}$, and $B^{\mathrm{an}}$ is the
completion in this norm.  An \emph{analytic Koszul pair} is a pair
$(\cA,\cA^!)$ such that the analytic bar-cobar adjunction restricts
to a Quillen equivalence on the sewing-complete categories.

Four targets (two proved, two conjectural):
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\alph*)]
\item \emph{Heisenberg sewing} (the decisive first case):
  the sewing envelope of $\mathcal H_k$ is the ind-Hilbert
  completion
  $\operatorname{Sym}\,A_2(D)\cong\operatorname{ind-Hilb}(\mathcal H_k)$
  (Moriwaki 2026).  The ind-Hilbert structure is the conformally
  flat factorization homology of $\mathcal H_k$ valued in
  $\mathsf{IndHilb}$.
\item \emph{Lattice sewing}: the sewing envelope of $V_\Lambda$
  is the vertex-algebraic completion by lattice theta functions,
  with the theta-function series converging absolutely in the
  sewing-amplitude topology.
\item \emph{Analytic realisation criterion}: a criterion for when
  the algebraic Koszul pair $(\cA,\cA^!)$ extends to an analytic
  one.  The expected criterion: the HS-sewing condition on $\cA$
  plus the dual HS condition on $\cA^!$ should suffice.
\item \emph{Boundary bar duality}: the analytic bar of the
  boundary chiral algebra equals the topological bar of the bulk
  factorization algebra:
  $B^{\mathrm{an}}(\cA_\partial)\simeq
  B^{\mathrm{top}}(\mathrm{Fact}^{\mathrm{bulk}}_T)$,
  identifying the boundary sewing data with the bulk topological
  data.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{13.3.\enspace Factorization envelopes and the modular Koszul datum}

The bar construction starts from a chiral algebra, but the natural
input in every geometric construction is a Lie conformal algebra.
The factorization envelope bridges this gap: it is the functor that
produces a chiral algebra from Lie conformal data, and the
programme asks whether the entire modular Koszul package can be
constructed functorially at the Lie conformal level, without
passing through the vertex algebra.  The target is a
universal modular factorization envelope $U^{\mathrm{mod}}_X(L)$
that is left adjoint to extracting primitive currents.

A \emph{cyclically admissible} Lie conformal algebra~$L$
(a $\mathbb C[\partial]$-module equipped with a $\lambda$-bracket
$\{a_\lambda b\}$ satisfying sesquilinearity, skew-symmetry,
and the Jacobi identity) has four
properties: a conformal grading $L=\bigoplus_{\Delta\ge 0}L_\Delta$
by conformal weight, a decreasing filtration
$F^0 L\supset F^1 L\supset\cdots$ compatible with the
$\lambda$-bracket, bounded poles (the $\lambda$-bracket
$\{a_\lambda b\}$ is polynomial in~$\lambda$ of degree bounded by
conformal weights), and an invariant symmetric bilinear pairing
$\langle-,-\rangle\colon L\otimes L\to\mathbb C$ compatible with
the conformal structure.

From a cyclically admissible~$L$, one constructs the
\emph{modular Koszul datum}:
\[
\Pi_X(L)
\;=\;
\bigl(\mathrm{Fact}_X(L),\;\bar B_X(L),\;\Theta_L,\;
\cL_L,\;(V^{\mathrm{br}}_L,T^{\mathrm{br}}_L),\;
R_4^{\mathrm{mod}}(L)\bigr):
\]
the factorization algebra (the Nishinaka factorization envelope),
the bar coalgebra, the universal MC class, the line-operator datum,
the branch-line data, and the quartic resonance class.  Each
component is functorially determined by~$L$.

The target: the \emph{universal modular factorization envelope}
$U^{\mathrm{mod}}_X(L)$ as left adjoint of the modular
primitive-current functor $\operatorname{Prim}^{\mathrm{mod}}$:
\[
\operatorname{Hom}_{\mathsf{Fact}^{\mathrm{mod}}}
\bigl(U^{\mathrm{mod}}_X(L),\,\cF\bigr)
\;\cong\;
\operatorname{Hom}_{\mathsf{LCA}^{\mathrm{cyc}}}
\bigl(L,\,\operatorname{Prim}^{\mathrm{mod}}(\cF)\bigr).
\]
The envelope-shadow functor $\Theta^{\mathrm{env}}_{\le r}(R)$
extracts finite-order shadows from the envelope data: the
universal property of $U^{\mathrm{mod}}_X$ implies that
$\Theta_L=\Theta^{\mathrm{env}}_{\le\infty}(L)$ is the universal
MC class of the modular Koszul datum.

For direct sums $L=L_1\oplus L_2$ with vanishing mixed OPE:
$\kappa(L)=\kappa(L_1)+\kappa(L_2)$ (additivity),
$T^{\mathrm{br}}_L=T^{\mathrm{br}}_{L_1}\oplus T^{\mathrm{br}}_{L_2}$
(direct sum), $\Delta_L=\Delta_{L_1}\cdot\Delta_{L_2}$
(multiplicativity), $R_4^{\mathrm{mod}}(L)
=R_4^{\mathrm{mod}}(L_1)+R_4^{\mathrm{mod}}(L_2)$ (additivity).
BRST reduction on total modular Koszul datums:
the current-plus-ghost package descends to
$\Pi_X(\mathcal W_N)$, hence
$\Theta_{\mathcal W_N}
=H^0_{Q_{\mathrm{DS}}}(\Theta_{V_k(\fg)\otimes F_{\mathrm{gh}}})$:
the shadow obstruction tower of the $W$-algebra is the Drinfeld--Sokolov
reduction of the full current-plus-ghost tower, not of the bare
affine tower alone.

\subsection*{13.4.\enspace Non-principal $W$-algebra duality}

Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction connects the affine landscape to the
$W$-algebra landscape: it takes $\widehat{\mathfrak g}_k$ and a
nilpotent element $f$ and produces the $W$-algebra
$\mathcal W_k(\mathfrak g, f)$.  For principal $f$, the reduction
functor commutes with bar-cobar duality by the Feigin--Frenkel
theorem, and the modular Koszul datum descends.  For non-principal $f$,
this commutation is unproved, and the frontier begins.  The theory
demands this extension because the non-principal $W$-algebras
include the physically central cases ($\mathcal W_k(\mathfrak{sl}_N,
f_{\mathrm{sub}})$ controls $\mathcal N = 2$ superconformal theories)
and the mathematically central ones (the Feigin--Tipunin algebras
at admissible levels).

The hook-type nilpotent orbit in type~$A$ is the first
non-principal corridor for Koszul duality, conditional on
DS-bar compatibility
\textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:hook-transport-corridor}\textup{)}.  For a partition
$\lambda=(n-p,1^p)$ (hook type) in $\mathfrak{sl}_N$, the
$W$-algebra $\mathcal W_k(\mathfrak{sl}_N,f_\lambda)$ is defined
by quantum Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction with respect to the
nilpotent element $f_\lambda$.  The duality:
\[
\bigl(\mathcal W_k(\mathfrak{sl}_N,f_\lambda)\bigr)^!
\;\simeq\;
\mathcal W_{k^\vee_\lambda}(\mathfrak{sl}_N,f_{\lambda^t}),
\]
where $\lambda^t$ is the transpose partition and $k^\vee_\lambda$
is the dual level (a rational function of~$k$ depending
on~$\lambda$).  The proof: for hook-type partitions, the DS
reduction functor commutes with bar-cobar duality by the results
of Fehily and Creutzig--Linshaw--Nakatsuka--Sato (2023--2025).

The \emph{transport propagation lemma}: hook-type seeds combined
with edge-compatibility (the property that the DS reduction functor
preserves the collision structure at each FM boundary stratum)
propagate duality results along edges of the nilpotent Hasse
diagram in type~$A$.  The \emph{type-$A$ transport-to-transpose
conjecture}: for every partition~$\lambda$ of~$N$,
$(\mathcal W_k(\mathfrak{sl}_N,f_\lambda))^!
\simeq\mathcal W_{k^\vee_\lambda}(\mathfrak{sl}_N,f_{\lambda^t})$.

The general obstruction is not defining the DS reduction (which
exists for arbitrary nilpotent orbits by Kac--Roan--Wakimoto) but
proving that DS reduction \emph{commutes with the bar-cobar
adjunction}: the natural map
$\mathrm{DS}(\barB(\widehat{\fg}_k))\to
\barB(\mathrm{DS}(\widehat{\fg}_k))$ must be a quasi-isomorphism.
For principal reduction, this follows from the Feigin--Frenkel
theorem; for hook-type in type~$A$, it is conditional on
hook-wide DS-bar compatibility
\textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:hook-transport-corridor}\textup{)};
for arbitrary nilpotent orbits, it is the frontier.

\subsection*{13.5.\enspace The boxed machine}

The entire construction can be stated in a single pipeline.
\[
\boxed{
\text{homotopy chiral input }\cA
\;+\;
\text{log-FM cutting cooperad }\mathcal C^!_{\mathrm{ch}}
\;+\;
\text{modular convolution }L_\infty
\;\;\Longrightarrow\;\;
\Theta_\cA,\;
\mathcal T^{\mathrm{mod}}_{\Theta_\cA},\;
\kappa,\;
\Delta_\cA,\;
\mathfrak R^{\mathrm{mod}}_4,\;\ldots
}
\]

\bigskip
\noindent
The modular convolution $L_\infty$-algebra
$\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{mod}}_\cA$ is the single organising structure.
It carries a natural modular $L_\infty$ structure from the Feynman
transform of the modular operad; the dg Lie algebra
$\operatorname{Conv}_{\mathrm{str}}(\mathcal C^!_{\mathrm{ch}},
\mathcal P^{\mathrm{ch}})$ is its strict model.  The universal MC
element
$\Theta_\cA\in\operatorname{MC}(\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{mod}}_\cA)$,
satisfying
\[
D\cdot\Theta_\cA+\tfrac12[\Theta_\cA,\Theta_\cA]\;=\;0,
\]
is proved: it is the bar-intrinsic extraction
$\Theta_\cA:=D_\cA-d_0$, which is MC because $D_\cA^2=0$.

The shadow obstruction tower consists of finite-order projections:
\begin{align*}
\Theta_\cA^{\le 2}&:\qquad\kappa(\cA)
  &&\text{(modular characteristic, scalar curvature)},\\
\Theta_\cA^{\le 3}&:\qquad\mathfrak C(\cA)
  &&\text{(cubic shadow, Lie structure)},\\
\Theta_\cA^{\le 4}&:\qquad\mathfrak Q(\cA)
  &&\text{(quartic resonance class, contact structure)},\\
\Theta_\cA^{\le r}&:\qquad\operatorname{Sh}_r(\cA)
  &&\text{(arity-$r$ shadow)},\\
\Theta_\cA&:\qquad\varprojlim_r\Theta_\cA^{\le r}
  &&\text{(the universal MC element)}.
\end{align*}
Theorems~A--D+H and the genus expansion are proved projections
of the scalar level~$\kappa$.  The holographic datum
$\mathcal H(T)=(\cA,\cA^!,\cC,r(z),\Theta_\cA,\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}})$
is the packaging of $\Theta_\cA$ and its projections into
the data of a 3d holomorphic-topological field theory.  The weight
filtration on $\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{mod}}_\cA$ controls the
extension tower; each finite truncation
$\Theta_\cA^{\le r}$ is constructive and does not require the
full all-genera modular envelope.  The modular tangent complex
extracts Chern--Weil invariants.  The genus spectral sequence
controls the lift across genera.  The standard landscape is
computed.

\begin{principle}[The four-test interface]
\label{princ:four-test-interface}
\index{four-test interface|textbf}%
The modular Koszul machine has a complete algebraic-geometric
interface with $\overline{\mathcal M}_{g,n}$, consisting of
four independent proved tests:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item $D_\cA^2 = 0$:
  the bar differential squares to zero at all genera and arities
  \textup{(}Theorems~\textup{\ref{thm:bar-modular-operad},
  \ref{thm:quantum-diff-squares-zero}}\textup{)}.
\item $\mathrm{obs}_g(\cA) = \kappa(\cA)\cdot\lambda_g$
  for uniform-weight algebras at all genera,
  and unconditionally at genus~$1$ for all families:
  the genus-$g$ obstruction factors as modular characteristic
  times Hodge class
  \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:modular-characteristic}}\textup{)}.
\item $Q_g(\cA)+Q_g(\cA^!)=H^*(\overline{\mathcal M}_g,Z(\cA))$:
  complementarity assembles the Koszul pair into a Lagrangian
  decomposition
  \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:quantum-complementarity-main}}\textup{)}.
\item Sewing:
  genus-$g$ amplitudes converge from lower-genus data
  \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:general-hs-sewing}}\textup{)}.
\end{enumerate}
Each test captures a distinct aspect: \textup{(i)} is purely
algebraic and requires no Koszulness hypothesis;
\textup{(ii)} identifies the tautological class but does not
involve~$\cA^!$; \textup{(iii)} requires the Koszul pair but is
genus-by-genus; \textup{(iv)} is analytic and independent of the
Hodge-class identification.  Any three can hold with the fourth
failing.  Three regions lie outside: multi-weight algebras at
$g\ge 2$ \textup{(}Open Problem~\textup{\ref{op:multi-generator-universality}}\textup{)},
BV/BRST${}={}$bar at higher genus
\textup{(}Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:master-bv-brst}}\textup{)},
and non-perturbative completion.
See Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:four-test-interface}} for the full
discussion.
\end{principle}

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{The holographic frontier.}
The holographic datum $\mathcal H(T)$ is a boundary object.
Its lift to a genuine $3$d bulk theory is controlled by the
\emph{relative holographic deformation complex}
$\mathfrak{h}_T^\Theta:=\operatorname{fib}(
\mathfrak{g}_T^{\mathrm{SC}}\to\gAmod)_{\alpha_T}$
(Definition~\ref{def:relative-holographic-deformation}):
lifts of~$\Theta_\cA$ to full bulk/boundary/line data are
exactly MC elements of the twisted fibre
(Proposition~\ref{prop:lifts-as-relative-mc}).
The graded obstruction tower
$[\mathfrak{o}_r(\beta)]
\in H^2(\operatorname{gr}^F_r\mathfrak{h}_T^\Theta)$
turns the holographic frontier into a computable cohomology
calculus.  At depth~$4$, the \emph{relative quartic
obstruction} $\mathfrak{R}_4^{\mathrm{rel}}(T)$
is the first invariant detecting when a boundary datum
cannot arise from a planar holographic realization
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:relative-quartic-computation}).
The \emph{Loop--Connes principle}
$\beta_{\mathrm{der}}^*(\Delta_{\mathrm{open}})=\Lambda_P$
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:loop-connes-transfer}):
closed genus creation is the image of the open BV operator
under the derived-center map; loops in the bulk are traces
on the boundary.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Cyclic trace, ribbon structure, and $1/N$.}
A bare modular graph sum does not define a literal
't~Hooft expansion
(Lemma~\ref{lem:bare-graph-no-thooft}).
Cyclic trace structure on the open
$E_1$-chiral algebra resolves this: cyclicity enables ribbon
thickening
(Theorem~\ref{thm:cyclicity-ribbon}),
and a matrix realisation gives the exact weight
$N^{\chi(\Sigma_\Gamma)}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:exact-n-chi-weighting}).
The three levels of language (plain modular $E_1$
(genus expansion), cyclic traced modular $E_1$ ('t~Hooft
expansion), ribbonised modular Swiss-cheese (holographic
open/closed 't~Hooft language)) are made precise in the
$E_1$ modular Koszul chapter
(Chapter~\ref{chap:e1-modular-koszul}).

\subsection*{13.6.\enspace Admissible levels and logarithmic CFT}

At admissible levels $k = -h^\vee + p/q$ (coprime $p \ge h^\vee$,
$q \ge 1$), the Zhu algebra $A(\mathcal{V}_k(\mathfrak g))$ is
semisimple but the vertex algebra itself is not simple: there is a
maximal proper ideal~$J_k$ with $L_k(\mathfrak g) =
\mathcal{V}_k(\mathfrak g)/J_k$ the simple quotient.  The bar
complex of~$\mathcal{V}_k$ acquires a periodic CDG structure indexed
by the $q$-th roots of unity: the curvature $m_0 = \kappa \cdot
\omega_g$ factors through the cyclotomic polynomial
$\Phi_q(\zeta)$, and the weight filtration has a finite plateau at
level $N = q$.  This is the algebraic door to logarithmic conformal
field theory on the degenerate admissible lane, where the simple
quotient $L_k(\mathfrak g)$ has a logarithmic
\textup{(}non-semisimple\textup{)} module category.  On the
non-degenerate admissible lane the simple quotient is rational,
while the bar-side admissible analysis records vacuum null vectors
and nilradical data as the obstruction surfaces across the broader
admissible picture.  One still has weightwise finite-page
character-theoretic degeneration on the non-degenerate lane,
whereas an identification of the resulting bar
cohomology with logarithmic extensions is not proved here.

\subsection*{13.7.\enspace The relative Feynman transform}

The modular bar coalgebra $\barB_{\mathrm{mod}}(\cA)$ is naturally
an algebra over the relative Feynman transform
$\mathrm{FT}_{\mathsf{Com}_{\mathrm{mod}} /
\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}}$.
This is the algebraic skeleton shared by the factorization approach
(\S10.8) and the operadic approach (\S3): the factorization structure
on $\operatorname{Ran}(\Sigma_g) \times \operatorname{Ran}(\mathbb R)$
over $\overline{\cM}_g$ produces it via families of factorizable
$\mathcal D$-modules; the operadic structure on
$\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}_{\mathrm{mod}}$ produces it via
formal completion at collision points.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Recognition.}\enspace
$\barB_{\mathrm{mod}}(\cA)$ is naturally a
$\mathrm{FT}_{\mathsf{Com}_{\mathrm{mod}} /
\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}}$-algebra:
the tree-level part $D_0$ is the
$\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$-coalgebra structure, and the
genus-raising part $D_1$ is the
$\mathsf{Com}_{\mathrm{mod}}$-modular structure.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Homotopy-involutivity.}\enspace
$\mathrm{FT}_{\mathsf{Com}_{\mathrm{mod}} /
\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}}^{\;2} \simeq \mathrm{id}$.
The proof proceeds in three steps:
genus-$0$ involutivity from operadic homotopy-Koszulity
(the homotopy-Koszulity theorem, Vol~II),
closed-colour modular involutivity from the Feynman involution
(Theorem~\ref{thm:feynman-involution}),
and assembly via the genus-filtration spectral sequence.

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Three routes unified.}\enspace
Route~B (factorization, \S10.8) provides the global truth:
factorization on $\operatorname{Ran}(\Sigma_g) \times
\operatorname{Ran}(\mathbb R)$ over $\overline{\cM}_g$.
Route~A (operadic, \S3) provides the local approximation:
$\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}_{\mathrm{mod}}$ at formal
completions.  Route~C (this section) provides the algebraic
skeleton: $\mathrm{FT}_{\mathsf{Com}_{\mathrm{mod}} /
\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}}$ as the common abstraction.
The factorization structure projects to the relative Feynman
transform by forgetting $\mathcal D$-module data; the operadic
structure injects into it by formal completion.  The relative
Feynman transform is the categorical image.

\subsection*{13.8.\enspace The computational infrastructure}

Every formula in this preface has been verified by an independent
symbolic computation layer comprising tens of thousands of tests
across several hundred modules, covering the shadow obstruction tower through
arity~$32$, the
standard landscape for all seven families, the genus-$2$ and
genus-$3$ planted-forest formulas, the DS-shadow cascade
(arities~$2$--$8$ for $N=2,\ldots,5$), the W$_3$ multi-generator
shadow metric on the $(T,W)$-plane, the B\"ocherer bridge at
genus~$2$, the Pixton shadow bridge, the entanglement programme
(Page curve, holographic codes), the non-simply-laced bar
computations ($B_2$/$C_2$/$G_2$/$F_4$), minimal model bar and
fusion rules, the dressed propagator engine (scalar
complementarity, $R$-matrix $R_1=1/12$), and the constrained
Epstein zeta for lattice VOAs.  The computation is adversarial:
tests encode cross-family consistency checks (additivity,
complementarity, anti-symmetry) that cannot be fooled by a single
hardcoded value.

Volume~II develops the $3$d theory in three new chapters: the
factorization Swiss-cheese algebra (the global truth on
$\operatorname{Ran}(\Sigma_g)\times\operatorname{Ran}(\mathbb R)$),
the modular Swiss-cheese operad (the local approximation at formal
completions), and the relative Feynman transform (the algebraic
skeleton connecting both).  These chapters, together with the
$3$d gravity chapter (six movements: from the Koszul triangle to
anomaly-completed MC recursion at all genera), the affine half-space
BV theorem (from linear to nonlinear via the doubling principle),
and eleven additional computational engines, constitute the
Volume~II programme.

\subsection*{13.9.\enspace The single open problem}

Everything proved in this monograph is a finite-order projection
of the universal MC element
$\Theta_\cA \in \MC(\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{mod}}_\cA)$.
Everything open is a question about its ambient:

\begin{center}
\fbox{\parbox{0.85\textwidth}{\centering
\emph{Characterise the modular convolution algebra
$\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{mod}}_\cA$ as a geometric object.}
}}
\end{center}

\noindent
Precisely: the modular convolution algebra is the endomorphism
algebra of the Lagrangian embedding
$\cL_\cA \hookrightarrow \cM_{\mathrm{vac}}(\cA)$ in the
$(-2)$-shifted symplectic stack of vacua.  Volume~I computes
the Taylor jets of this embedding (the shadow obstruction tower).
Volume~II identifies the local composition law (the Swiss-cheese
operad).  What remains is the global geometry of the stack itself:
the derived symplectic structure, the moduli of Lagrangians, and
the higher-categorical descent that would make the construction
independent of choices.

The ${\sim}150$ open conjectures in these two volumes are projections
of this single question:
\begin{itemize}[nosep]
\item the D-module purity conjecture asks whether the Lagrangian
  is pure (characterisation (xii) of Koszulness);
\item the non-principal W-duality programme asks how the Lagrangian
  transforms under Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction at arbitrary
  nilpotent orbits;
\item the analytic completion programme asks when the algebraic
  Lagrangian extends to a convergent one (the sewing envelope);
\item the factorization envelope programme asks for the universal
  construction of the Lagrangian from Lie conformal data alone;
\item the holographic completion question asks whether the genus-$0$
  Lagrangian extends over $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$ (the modular
  programme of Volume~II).
\end{itemize}
Each is a different facet of the geometry of
$\mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{mod}}_\cA$, and none requires going
beyond the framework already established.

\bigskip

\noindent
The entire structure unfolds from a single datum: the logarithmic
$1$-form $\eta = d\log(z_1 - z_2)$.  At $n$~points it became a
differential on the Fulton--MacPherson compactification; across all
genera it became the total bar differential~$D_\cA$; in the modular
convolution algebra it became the Maurer--Cartan element
$\Theta_\cA = D_\cA - d_0$.  One $1$-form, one relation (Arnold),
one extraction (residues): a universal invariant of chiral algebras
that is algebraic, computable, and complete.
